[-LSB-edit-RSB- History In the mid-1770s, the British government levied taxes that impeded Providence's maritime, fishing and agricultural industries, the mainstay of the city's economy.][[0.0]]
[One example was the Sugar Act, which was a tax levied against Providence's distilleries that adversely affected its trade in rum and slaves.][[0.0]]
[These taxes caused Providence to join the other colonies in renouncing allegiance to the British Crown.][[0.0]]
[In response to enforcement of unpopular trade laws, Providence residents spilled the first blood of the American Revolution in the notorious Gaspée Affair of 1772.][[0.0]]
[Though during the Revolutionary War the city escaped enemy occupation, the capture of nearby Newport disrupted industry and kept the population on alert.][[0.0]]
[Troops were quartered for various campaigns and Brown University's University Hall was used as a barracks and military hospital.][[0.0]]
[After departing from Newport, French troops sent by King Louis XVI and commanded by the Comte de Rochambeau passed through Providence on their way to join the attack against British forces.][[0.0]]
[The march from Newport to Providence was the beginning of a campaign led jointly by General George Washington in a decisive march that ended with the defeat of General Cornwallis in the Siege of Yorktown at Yorktown, Virginia and the Battle of the Chesapeake.][[0.0]]
[Following the war, the economy shifted from maritime endeavors to manufacturing, particularly machinery, tools, silverware, jewelry and textiles.][[0.0]]
[At one time, Providence boasted some of the largest manufacturing plants in the country, including Brown & Sharpe, Nicholson File, and Gorham Silverware, and with 7,614 people, was the country's ninth-largest city.b-LSB-'-RSB- The city's industries attracted many immigrants from Ireland, Germany, Sweden, England, Italy, Portugal, Cape Verde, and French Canada.][[0.0]]
[Economic and demographic shifts caused social strife, notably with a series of race riots between whites and blacks during the 1820s.][[0.0]]
[In response to these troubles and the economic growth, Providence residents ratified a city charter in 1831 as the population passed 17,000.][[0.0]]
[During the Civil War, local politics split over slavery as many had ties to Southern cotton.][[0.0]]
[Despite ambivalence concerning the war, the number of military volunteers routinely exceeded quota, and the city's manufacturing proved invaluable to the Union.][[0.0]]
[Postwar, horsecar lines covering the city enabled its growth and Providence thrived with waves of immigrants and land annexations bringing the population from 54,595 in 1865 to 175,597 by 1900.][[0.0]]
[The city's boom began to wane in the mid-1920s as industries, notably textiles, shut down.][[0.0]]
[Jewelry manufacturing continued to grow, taking up the slack and employing many of the city's new immigrants, coming from Portuguese, Italian, Polish, Lithuanian and Jewish backgrounds.][[0.0]]
[A number of hospitals also opened.][[0.0]]
[The Great Depression hit the city hard, and Providence's downtown was subsequently flooded by the New England Hurricane of 1938.][[0.0]]
[Though the city received a boost from World War II, this ended with the war.][[0.0]]
[The city saw further decline as a result of nation-wide trends, with the construction of highways and increased suburbanization.][[0.0]]
[The population would drop by 38% over the next three decades.][[0.0]]
[From the 1950s to the 1980s, Providence was a notorious bastion of organized crime.][[0.0]]
[The mafia boss Raymond L.S. Patriarca ruled a vast criminal enterprise.][[0.0]]
[The city's eponymous ``Renaissance'' began in the 1970s.][[0.0]]
[From 1975 until 1982, $606 million of local and national Community Development funds were invested throughout the city, and the hitherto falling population began to stabilize.][[0.0]]
[In the 1990s, Mayor Vincent Cianci, Jr showcased the city's strength in arts and pushed for further revitalization, ultimately resulting in the uncovering of the city's natural rivers -LRB-which had been paved over-RRB-, relocation of a large section of railroad underground, creation of Waterplace Park and river walks along the river's banks, and construction of the Fleet Skating Rink -LRB-now the Bank of America Skating Rink-RRB- downtown and the 1.4 million ft² Providence Place Mall.][[0.0]]
[New investment triggered within the city, with new construction including numerous condo projects, hotels, and a new office high-rise all filling in the freed space.][[0.0]]
[Despite new investment, poverty remains an entrenched problem as it does in most post-industrial New England cities.][[0.0]]
[Nearly 30 percent of the city population lives below the poverty line.][[0.0]]
[Recent increases in real estate values further exacerbate problems for those at marginal income levels, as Providence had the highest rise in median housing price of any city in the United States from 2004 to 2005.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Geography The Providence city limits enclose a small geographic region, with a total area of 20.5�square miles -LRB-53.2�km²-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[18.5�square miles -LRB-47.8�km²-RRB- of it is land and the remaining 2.1�square miles -LRB-5.3�km²-RRB- -LRB-roughly 10%-RRB- of it is water.][[0.0]]
[Providence is located at the head of Narragansett Bay, with the Providence River running into the bay through the center of the city, formed by the confluence of the Moshassuck and Woonasquatucket Rivers.][[1.0]]
[The Waterplace Park amphitheater and riverwalks line the river's banks through downtown.][[0.0]]
[Constitution Hill -LRB-near downtown-RRB-, College -LRB-or Prospect-RRB- Hill -LRB-east of the Providence River-RRB-, and Federal Hill -LRB-west of downtown and is New England's largest Italian district-RRB- are the most prominent of the city's hills.][[0.0]]
[The remaining hills include Tockwotten Hill at Fox Point, Smith Hill -LRB-where the State House is located-RRB-, Christian Hill at Hoyle Square -LRB-junction of Cranston & Westminster Streets-RRB-, and Weybosset Hill at the lower end of Weybosset Street, which was leveled in the early 1880s.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Neighborhoods Providence has 25 official neighborhoods, though these neighborhoods are often grouped together and referred to collectively:  -LSB-edit-RSB- Cityscape The city of Providence is geographically very compact, characteristic of eastern seaboard cities which developed prior to use of the automobile.][[0.0]]
[It is among the most densely populated cities in the country.][[0.0]]
[For this reason, Providence has the eighth-highest percentage of pedestrian commuters.][[0.0]]
[The street layout is somewhat chaotic--over one thousand streets -LRB-a great number for the city's size-RRB- run haphazardly, connecting and radiating from traditionally bustling places like Market Square.][[0.0]]
[Downtown Providence has numerous 19th century mercantile buildings in the Federal and Victorian architectural styles, as well as several post-modern and modernist buildings, are located throughout this area.][[0.0]]
[In particular, a fairly clear spatial separation appears between the areas of pre-1980s development and post-1980s development.][[0.0]]
[West Exchange Street and Exchange Terrace serve as rough boundaries between the two.][[0.0]]
[The newer area, sometimes called ``Capitol Center'', includes Providence Place Mall -LRB-1999-RRB-, a Westin hotel -LRB-1993-RRB- and The Residences at the Westin -LRB-2007-RRB-, GTECH -LRB-2006-RRB-, Waterplace condominiums -LRB-2007-RRB-, and Waterplace Park -LRB-1994-RRB-; the area tends toward newer development since much of it is land reclaimed in the 1970s from a mass of railroad tracks which was referred to colloquially as the ``Chinese Wall''.][[0.0]]
[This part of Downtown is characterized by open spaces, wide roads, and intent landscaping.][[0.0]]
[The historic part of downtown has many streetscapes that look as they did eighty years ago.][[0.0]]
[Many of the state's tallest buildings are found here.][[0.0]]
[The largest structure, to date, is the art-deco-styled former Industrial Trust Tower, currently the Bank of America Building at 426 feet -LRB-130 m-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[By contrast, nearby to it is the second tallest One Financial Plaza, designed in modern taut-skin cladding, constructed a half century later.][[0.0]]
[In between the two is 50 Kennedy Plaza.][[0.0]]
[The Textron Tower is also a core building to the modest Providence skyline.][[0.0]]
[Downtown is also the home of the Providence Biltmore and Westminster Arcade, the oldest enclosed shopping mall in the U.S., built in 1828.][[0.0]]
[The city's southern waterfront, away from the downtown core, is the location of many oil tanks, a docking station for a ferry boat, a decommissioned Russian submarine, a non-profit sailing center, bars, strip clubs, and power plants.][[0.0]]
[The Fox Point Hurricane Barrier is also found here, built to protect Providence from storm surge, like that it had endured in the 1938 New England Hurricane and again in 1954 from Hurricane Carol.][[0.0]]
[The majority of the cityscape comprises abandoned and revitalized industrial mills, double and triple decker housing -LRB-though the row houses found so commonly in other Northeast cities, are notably rare here-RRB-, a small number of high-rise buildings -LRB-predominantly for housing the elderly-RRB-, and single family homes.][[0.0]]
[I-95 serves as a physical barrier between the city's commercial core and neighborhoods such as Federal Hill and the West End.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Climate Providence's climate is between humid continental climate and humid subtropical climate, with warm summers, cold winters, and high humidity year-round.][[0.0]]
[The USDA rates the city at Zone 6a, which is an ``in-between'' climate.][[0.0]]
[The influence of the Atlantic Ocean keeps Providence, and the rest of the state of Rhode Island, warmer than many inland locales in New England.][[0.0]]
[January is the coldest month with average high temperatures of 37�°F -LRB-3�°C-RRB- and average low temperatures of 20 °F -LRB--7 °C-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[July is the warmest month with average high temperatures of 83 °F -LRB-28 °C-RRB- and average low temperatures of 64 °F -LRB-18 °C-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The record high temperature in the city was 104 °F -LRB-40 °C-RRB- recorded in 1975.][[0.0]]
[The record low temperature in the city was -17 °F -LRB--27 °C-RRB- recorded in 1934.][[0.0]]
[As with the rest of the northeastern seaboard, Providence receives ample precipitation year-round.][[0.0]]
[Monthly precipitation ranges from a high of 4.43 inches -LRB-112.5�mm-RRB- in March to a low of 3.17�inches -LRB-80.5�mm-RRB- in July.][[0.0]]
[Precipitation levels are generally slightly lesser in the summer months than the winter months when powerful storms known as Nor'easters can cause significant snowfall and blizzard conditions.][[0.0]]
[Although hurricanes are not frequent in coastal New England, Providence's location at the head of Narragansett Bay makes it vulnerable to them.][[0.0]]
[According to Forbes.com, the Providence-New Bedford-Fall River metropolitan area is ranked 30 on America's Most Toxic Cities  -LSB-edit-RSB- Demographics As of the census of 2000, the population comprised 173,618 people, 62,389 households, and 35,859 families.][[0.0]]
[The population density was 3,629.4/km² -LRB-9,401.7/sq�mi-RRB-, characteristic of comparatively older cities in New England such as New Haven, Connecticut; Boston, Massachusetts and Hartford, Connecticut.][[0.0]]
[Also like these cities, its population peaked in the 1940s just prior to the nationwide period of rapid suburbanization.][[0.0]]
[Providence has had a substantial Italian population since the turn of the century, with 14% -LRB-a pluralityc-LSB-'-RSB--RRB- of the population claiming Italian ancestry.][[0.0]]
[Italian influence manifests itself in Providence's Little Italy in Federal Hill.][[0.0]]
[Irish immigrants have also had considerable influence on the city's history, with 8% of residents claiming Irish heritage.][[0.0]]
[Belying Providence's traditionally white makeup is the sizable minority presence it has acquired in the last twenty years.][[0.0]]
[Though nearby cities like Boston and Hartford have longer-standing black and Latino communities, Providence now surpasses both in the density of its minority population, with non-Hispanic whites comprising less than half -LRB-40.9%-RRB- of the population.][[0.0]]
[Though salient contributions to this growth have been among Asians and unspecified races, the most dramatic change comes from Hispanics, whose presence has increased fivefold.][[0.0]]
[Having origins in Puerto Rico, Colombia, Bolivia, the Dominican Republic, and Central America -LRB-particularly Guatemala-RRB-, Hispanics have strong influence in the neighborhoods of Elmwood, the West End, and Upper and Lower South Providence.][[0.0]]
[Hispanic impact is even larger in the city's schools.][[0.0]]
[Hispanics represent over half -LRB-55%-RRB- of all students in the city's school system while comprising only 36% of Providence's population.][[0.0]]
[In addition, Providence, like the nearby Massachusetts cities of Fall River and New Bedford, has a considerable community of immigrants from various Portuguese-speaking countries, living mostly in the areas of Washington Park and Fox Point.][[0.0]]
[Portuguese is the city's third-largest nationality, -LRB-after Italian and Irish-RRB- at 4% of the population while Cape Verdeans make up another 2%.][[0.0]]
[African Americans constitute approximately 17% of the city with the largest percentages in Mount Hope and Upper and Lower South Providence neighborhoods.][[0.0]]
[Asians are 6% of Providence's population and have enclaves scattered throughout the city.][[0.0]]
[Another 6% of the city has multiracial ancestry.][[0.0]]
[Native Americans and Pacific Islanders make up the remaining 1.3%.][[0.0]]
[With Liberians comprising .4% of the population, the city is home to the one of the three largest Liberian immigrant populations in the country.][[0.0]]
[The Providence metropolitan area, which includes Providence, Fall River, Massachusetts, and Warwick is estimated to be 1,622,520.][[0.0]]
[In 2006, this area was officially added to the Boston Combined Statistical Area -LRB-CSA-RRB-, the fifth-largest CSA in the country.][[0.0]]
[In the last fifteen years, Providence has experienced a sizable growth in its under-18 population, attributed to the influx of Hispanics.][[0.0]]
[The median age of the city is 28 years, while the largest age cohort is 20 to 24 year olds, owing to the city's large student population.][[0.0]]
[The per capita income, as of the 2000 census, was $15,525, which is well below both the state average of $29,113, and the national average of $21,587.][[0.0]]
[The median income for a household was $26,867, and the median income for a family in Providence was $32,058, according to the 2000 census.][[0.0]]
[The city has one of the highest rates of poverty in the nation with 29.1% of the population and 23.9% of families living below the poverty line in 2000, the largest concentrations being found in the city's Olneyville, and Upper and Lower South Providence areas.][[0.0]]
[Poverty has affected children at a disproportionately higher rate with 40.1% of those under the age of 18 living below the poverty line, concentrated particularly west of downtown in the neighborhoods of Hartford, Federal Hill, and Olneyville.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Crime Compared to the national average, Providence has a higher than average rate of property crime and an average rate of violent crime per 100,000 inhabitants.][[0.0]]
[In 2009, there were 24 murders, the highest number since 2000 and a jump from the previous year's 13.][[1.0]]
[Crime in all categories had been dropping substantially during 2002-2007, contrary to national trends.][[0.0]]
[The nearby city of Worcester, Massachusetts which is about the same size had six murders in 2009 by comparison.][[0.0]]
[The much larger city of Boston had 42.][[0.0]]
[The police chief asserted that such violence was not stranger-to-stranger, but relationship driven.][[0.0]]
[The pattern of violent crime was highly specific by neighborhood with vast majority of the murders taking place in the poorest sections of Providence, such as Washington Park, Elmwood, South Providence and the West End.][[0.0]]
[In 2003, of the 239 United States cities with populations over 100,000, Providence's violent crime rate ranked 84th, as compared with New York City at 94th and Boston at 28th.][[0.0]]
[Providence has the fifth-highest rate of property crime per 100,000 inhabitants in the country.][[0.0]]
[Burglary and car theft, in particular constitute 1.12 and 2.49 times the national average.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Economy Providence was one of the first cities to industrialize in the United States.][[0.0]]
[By 1830, the city had manufacturing industries in metals, machinery, textiles, jewelry, and silverware.][[0.0]]
[Though manufacturing has declined, the city is still one of the largest centers for jewelry and silverware design and manufacturing.][[1.0]]
[Services, particularly education, health care, and finance, also make up a large portion of the city's economy.][[0.0]]
[Providence also is the site of a sectional center facility, a regional hub for the U.S. Postal Service.][[0.0]]
[Since it is the capital of Rhode Island, Providence's economy additionally consists of government services.][[0.0]]
[The Fortune 500 conglomerate Textron and Fortune 1000 company Nortek Incorporated are both headquartered in the city, and GTECH's world headquarters has recently been moved to downtown Providence.][[0.0]]
[Citizens Bank is also headquartered in Providence.][[0.0]]
[Another company whose origins were in the city is Fleet Bank.][[0.0]]
[Once Rhode Island's largest bank, it moved its headquarters to Boston, Massachusetts, after acquiring Shawmut Bank in 1995.][[0.0]]
[Before its acquisition by Bank of America, Fleet merged with BankBoston to become New England's largest commercial bank.][[0.0]]
[The city is home to the Rhode Island Convention Center, which opened in December 1993.][[0.0]]
[Along with a hotel, the convention center is connected to the Providence Place Mall, a major retail center, through a skywalk.][[0.0]]
[The Port of Providence, the second largest deepwater seaport in New England, handles cargo such as cement, chemicals, heavy machinery, petroleum, and scrap metal.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Government Providence serves as Rhode Island's capital, housing the Rhode Island General Assembly as well as the offices of the Governor and the Lieutenant Governor in the Rhode Island State House.][[0.0]]
[Providence's city government has a mayor-council form of government.][[0.0]]
[The Providence City Council consists of fifteen city councilors, one for each of the city's wards.][[0.0]]
[The council is tasked with enacting ordinances and passing an annual budget.][[0.0]]
[Providence also has probate and superior courts.][[0.0]]
[The U.S. District Court for the District of Rhode Island is located downtown across from City Hall adjacent to Kennedy Plaza.][[0.0]]
[David N. Cicilline was elected mayor by a large margin in 2002 and was re-elected without any major opposition in 2006.][[0.0]]
[Cicilline is the first and only openly gay mayor of an American state capital.][[0.0]]
[Providence was the largest American city to have an openly gay mayor, until Sam Adams took office in Portland, Oregon on January 1, 2009.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Education -LSB-edit-RSB- Postsecondary Seven of the fourteen institutions of higher learning in Rhode Island have campuses in Providence -LRB-city proper-RRB-: Between these schools the number of postsecondary students is approximately 44,000, or 25% the population of Providence.][[0.0]]
[Compounded by Brown University's being the second-largest employer, higher education exerts a considerable presence in the city's politics and economy.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Private and charter schools Several private schools, including Moses Brown, the Lincoln School, and the Wheeler School, are in the city's East Side.][[0.0]]
[LaSalle Academy is located in the Elmhurst area of the city near Providence College.][[0.0]]
[The public charter schools Time Squared Academy -LRB-K-12-RRB- and Textron Chamber of Commerce -LRB-9-12-RRB- are funded by GTECH and Textron respectively.][[0.0]]
[In addition, the city's South Side houses Community Preparatory School, a private school serving primarily low-income students in grades 3-8.][[0.0]]
[Within the semi-private schools, The Metropolitan Regional Career and Technical Center -LRB-The Met-RRB- and The Big Picture Company schools serve students through real world experiences and project-based learning.][[0.0]]
[There are two separate centers for students with special needs.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Public schools The Providence Public School District serves about 26,000 students from pre-Kindergarten to grade 12.][[0.0]]
[The district has 25 elementary schools, nine middle schools, and thirteen high schools.][[0.0]]
[The Providence Public School District features magnet schools at the middle and high school level, Nathanael Greene and Classical respectively.][[0.0]]
[The overall graduation rate as of 2007 is 70.1%, which is close to the statewide rate of 71% and the national average of 70%.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Culture Much of Providence culture is synonymous with Rhode Island culture.][[0.0]]
[Like the state, the city has a non-rhotic accent which can be heard on local media.][[0.0]]
[Providence also shares Rhode Island's affinity for coffee, as the former has the most coffee/doughnut shops per capita of any city in the country.][[0.0]]
[Providence is also reputed to have the highest number of restaurants per capita, many of which are founded and/or staffed by its own Johnson & Wales graduates.][[0.0]]
[Providence has several ethnic neighborhoods, notably Federal Hill and the North End -LRB-Italian-RRB-, Fox Point -LRB-Cape Verdean and Portuguese-RRB-, West End -LRB-mainly Central American and Asians-RRB-, and Smith Hill -LRB-Irish with miscellaneous enclaves of other groups-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[There are also many dedicated community organizations and arts associations located in the city.][[0.0]]
[The city gained the reputation as one of the most active and growing LGBT communities in the Northeast; the rate of reported gay and lesbian relationships is 75% higher than the national average and Providence has been named among the ``Best Lesbian Places to Live''.][[0.0]]
[The current mayor, David Cicilline, won his election running as an openly gay man, making him the first openly gay mayor of a U.S. state capital.][[0.0]]
[Former Mayor Cianci instituted the position of Mayor's Liaison to the Gay and Lesbian community in the 1990s.][[0.0]]
[There are numerous social and community organizations supporting the gay, lesbian, bisexual, and transgender community.][[0.0]]
[Providence is home to the largest gay bathhouse in New England.][[1.0]]
[During the summer months, the city regularly hosts WaterFire, an environmental art installation that consists of about 100 bonfires that blaze just above the surface of the three rivers that pass through the middle of downtown Providence.][[0.0]]
[There are multiple Waterfire events that are accompanied by various pieces of classical and world music.][[0.0]]
[The public art displays, most notably sculptures, change on a regular basis.][[0.0]]
[The city is also the home of the Tony Award-winning theater group Trinity Repertory Company, the Providence Black Repertory Company, and the Rhode Island Philharmonic Orchestra.][[0.0]]
[Providence is also the home of several performing arts centers such as the Veterans Memorial Auditorium, the Providence Performing Arts Center, and the Providence Festival Ballet.][[1.0]]
[The city's underground music scene, centered around artist-run spaces such as the now-defunct Fort Thunder, is known in underground music circles.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Sites of interest Providence is home to an 1,200-acre -LRB-4.9�km2-RRB- park system, notably Waterplace Park and Riverwalk, Roger Williams Park, Roger Williams National Memorial, and Prospect Terrace Park, the latter featuring expansive views of the downtown area.][[0.0]]
[As one of the first cities in the country, Providence contains many historic buildings while the East Side neighborhood in particular includes the largest contiguous area of buildings listed on the National Register of Historic Places in the U.S. with many pre-revolutionary houses.][[1.0]]
[The East Side is also home to the First Baptist Church in America, the oldest Baptist church in the Americas, founded by Roger Williams in 1638, as well as the Old State House, which served as the state's capitol from 1762 to 1904.][[1.0]]
[Nearby is Roger Williams National Memorial.][[0.0]]
[Downcity Providence is home to the fourth largest unsupported dome in the world -LRB-the second largest marble dome after St. Peter's Basilica in Rome-RRB-, as well as the Westminster Arcade, which is the oldest enclosed shopping center in the U.S..][[0.0]]
[The main art museum is the Rhode Island School of Design Museum, which has the twentieth largest collection in the country.][[0.0]]
[The city's southern waterfront hosts a decommissioned Cold War era Russian submarine.][[0.0]]
[In addition to the Providence Public Library and its nine branches, the city is home to the Providence Athenæum, the fourth oldest library in the country.][[0.0]]
[Here, on one of his many visits to Providence, Edgar Allan Poe, met and courted a love interest named Sarah Helen Whitman.][[1.0]]
[Poe was a regular fixture there, as was H. P. Lovecraft; both of them influential writers of gothic literature.][[0.0]]
[The Bank of America Skating Center, formerly the Fleet Skating Center, is located near Kennedy Plaza in the downtown district, connected by pedestrian tunnel to Waterplace Park, a cobblestone and concrete park below street traffic that abuts Providence's three rivers.][[0.0]]
[The southern part of the city is home to the famous roadside attraction Nibbles Woodaway -LRB-also known as the ``Big Blue Bug''-RRB-, the world's largest termite, as well as the aforementioned Roger Williams Park, which contains a zoo, a botanical center, and the Museum of Natural History and Planetarium.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Sports The city is home to the American Hockey League team Providence Bruins, which plays at the Dunkin' Donuts Center -LRB-formerly the Providence Civic Center-RRB-.][[1.0]]
[From 1926 to 1972, the AHL's Providence Reds -LRB-renamed the Rhode Island Reds in their last years-RRB- played at the Rhode Island Auditorium.][[0.0]]
[In 1972, the team relocated to the Providence Civic Center, where they played until moving to Binghamton, New York, in 1977.][[0.0]]
[Providence has its own roller derby league.][[0.0]]
[Formed in 2004, it currently has four teams: the Providence Mob Squad, the Sakonnet River Roller Rats, the Old Money Honeys, and the Rhode Island Riveters.][[0.0]]
[The NFL's New England Patriots and MLS's New England Revolution play in Foxborough, Massachusetts, which is situated halfway between Providence and Boston.][[0.0]]
[Providence was formerly home to two major league franchises: the NFL's Providence Steam Roller in the 1920s and 1930s, and the NBA's Providence Steamrollers in the 1940s.][[0.0]]
[The city is also where Rocky Marciano won 29 of his 49 fights.][[0.0]]
[The city's defunct baseball team, the Providence Grays, competed in the National League from 1879 through 1885.][[0.0]]
[The team defeated the New York Metropolitans in baseball's first successful ``world championship series'' in 1884.][[0.0]]
[In 1914, after the Boston Red Sox purchased Babe Ruth from the then-minor league Baltimore Orioles, the team prepared Ruth for the major leagues by sending him to finish the season playing for a minor league team in Providence that was also known as the Grays.][[0.0]]
[Today, professional baseball is offered by the Pawtucket Red Sox, the AAA affiliate of the Boston Red Sox which plays in nearby Pawtucket.][[0.0]]
[Most baseball fans--along with the local media--tend to follow the Boston Red Sox.][[0.0]]
[Major colleges and universities fielding NCAA Division I athletic teams are Brown University and Providence College.][[0.0]]
[The latter is a member of the Big East Conference.][[0.0]]
[Much local hype is associated with games between these two schools or the University of Rhode Island.][[0.0]]
[Providence has also hosted the alternative sports event Gravity Games from 1999 to 2001, and was also the first host of ESPN's X Games, known in its first edition as the Extreme Games, in 1995.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Infrastructure -LSB-edit-RSB- Health and medicine Providence is home to eight hospitals, most prominently Rhode Island Hospital, the largest general acute care hospital in the state.][[0.0]]
[The hospital is in a complex along I-95 that includes Hasbro Children's Hospital and Women and Infants Hospital.][[0.0]]
[The city is also home to the Roger Williams Medical Center, St. Joseph Hospital For Specialty Care -LRB-a division of St. Joseph Health Services Of Rhode Island-RRB-, The Miriam Hospital, a major teaching affiliate associated with the Alpert Medical School of Brown University, as well as a VA medical center.][[0.0]]
[Providence is home to the Quality Assurance Review Center -LRB-QARC-RRB-, which performs thousands of radiotherapy reviews per year.][[0.0]]
[QARC is primarily supported by grants from the National Cancer Institute -LRB-NCI-RRB- and contracts from the pharmaceutical industry.][[0.0]]
[It receives radiotherapy data from around one-thousand hospitals in both the United States and abroad.][[0.0]]
[The center also maintains a strategic affiliation with the University of Massachusetts Medical School in Worcester, Massachusetts.][[0.0]]
[The Rhode Island Blood Center has its main headquarters in Providence.][[0.0]]
[Since 1979, the Rhode Island Blood Center has been the sole organization in charge of blood collection and testing and distribution of blood products to 11 hospitals in Rhode Island.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Transportation Providence is served by air primarily by the commercial airfield T. F. Green Airport in nearby Warwick.][[0.0]]
[General aviation fields also serve the region.][[0.0]]
[Due to overcrowding and Big Dig complications in Boston, Massport has been promoting T.F. Green as an alternative to Boston's Logan International Airport.][[0.0]]
[Providence Station, located between the Rhode Island State House and the downtown district, is served by Amtrak and MBTA Commuter Rail services, with a commuter rail running to Boston.][[0.0]]
[Approximately 2400 passengers daily pass through the station.][[0.0]]
[Additionally, funds have been allocated to extend the commuter rail from Providence to T. F. Green Airport terminating at a $222.5 million intermodal station to be completed in 2009.][[0.0]]
[I-95 runs from north to south through Providence while I-195 connects the city to eastern Rhode Island and southeastern Massachusetts, including New Bedford, Massachusetts, and Cape Cod.][[1.0]]
[I-295 encircles Providence while RI 146 provides a direct connection with Worcester, Massachusetts.][[0.0]]
[The city has commissioned and begun a long-term project, the Iway, to move I-195 not only for safety reasons, but also to free up land and to reunify the Jewelry District with Downcity Providence, which had been split from one another by the highway.][[0.0]]
[The project is estimated to cost $446 million and be completed in 2012.][[0.0]]
[Kennedy Plaza, in downtown Providence, serves as a transportation hub for local public transit as well as a departure point for Peter Pan and Greyhound bus lines.][[0.0]]
[Public transit is managed by Rhode Island Public Transit Authority -LRB-RIPTA-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Through RIPTA alone Kennedy Plaza serves over 71,000 people a day.][[0.0]]
[The majority of the area covered by RIPTA is served by traditional buses.][[0.0]]
[Of particular note is the East Side Trolley Tunnel running under College Hill, the use of which is reserved for RIPTA buses.][[0.0]]
[RIPTA also operates the Providence LINK, a system of tourist trolleys in downtown Providence, as well as a ferry to Newport between May and October.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Utilities Electricity and natural gas are provided by Narragansett Electric Company which is owned by National Grid USA.][[0.0]]
[Providence Water is responsible for the distribution of drinking water, ninety percent of which comes from the Scituate Reservoir about ten miles -LRB-16�km-RRB- west of downtown, with contributions coming from four smaller bodies of water.][[0.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Plot The film opens with a series of grainy, color-warped still photographs appearing over melancholy piano music, representing the abstract memories of the unseen Herman Raucher -LRB-Robert Mulligan narrating in voiceover-RRB-, a middle-aged man from Brooklyn.][[0.0]]
[After the stills finish, we hear Raucher speaking in the present day -LRB-1971 according to the book-RRB-, recalling the summer he spent on the island -LRB-fictionalized in the novel as ``Packett Island''-RRB- in 1942.][[0.0]]
[The film flashes back to a day that then 15-year-old ``Hermie'' -LRB-Gary Grimes-RRB- and his friends�-- jock Oscy -LRB-Jerry Houser-RRB- and introverted nerd Benjie -LRB-Oliver Conant-RRB-�-- spent running and playing on the beach.][[0.0]]
[In the middle of their goofing off, the three boys spot a newlywed young soldier carrying his bride -LRB-Jennifer O'Neill-RRB- into a house on the beach.][[0.0]]
[The boys are all struck by her beauty, especially Hermie, who finds himself unable to get her out of his mind.][[0.0]]
[The next several days on the island find the boys continuing to spend their afternoons on the beach, where, in the midst of young, scantily-clad teenage girls, their thoughts invariably turn to sex; all of them are virgins, the height of their experience being when Oscy and Hermie touched a girl's breasts when they were twelve.][[0.0]]
[While Oscy is more interested in sex with gorgeous girls, however, Hermie finds himself developing genuine romantic interest in the young bride, whose husband he spots leaving the island on a military transport boat one morning.][[0.0]]
[Later that day, Hermie spots her trying to carry numerous bags of groceries by herself, and helps her get them back to her house.][[0.0]]
[The two strike up a friendship and he agrees to return in the future to help her out with chores.][[0.0]]
[Meanwhile, Benjie mentions that one of the books kept in the beach house his parents are renting is a sex manual.][[0.0]]
[Oscy and Hermie convince the reluctant Benjie to steal the book; upon reading it, Oscy and Hermie become convinced they now know everything necessary to lose their virginity and become great lovers.][[0.0]]
[They decide to put this hypothesis to the test by going to the island film house and picking up a trio of girls; Oscy happens to find three high-school girls, and sets about staking out the most attractive one, Miriam -LRB-Christopher Norris-RRB-, for himself, ``giving'' Hermie her wallflower friend, Aggie -LRB-Katherine Allentuck-RRB- and leaving Benjie with Gloria, a heavyset girl with braces.][[1.0]]
[Frightened by the reality of the concept of sex, Benjie runs away into the night, and is not seen by Hermie or Oscy again the whole summer.][[0.0]]
[Gloria, thinking that her appearance repulsed Benjie, likewise walks away.][[0.0]]
[Hermie and Oscy spend the entirety of the film -LRB-Now, Voyager - an anachronism, as that film wasn't released until October 1942-RRB- attempting to ``score'' with Miriam and Aggie, Oscy aggressively pursuing Miriam to the point that she strikes him, although Oscy soon learns that she is the island ``hussy'' and simply playing hard to get.][[0.0]]
[Hermie, meanwhile, finds himself getting unexpected success with Aggie, who allows him to grope her breast for almost twelve minutes; it isn't until after the show Oscy points out to Hermie the reason for Aggie's passivity was that Hermie was in fact fondling her elbow.][[0.0]]
[The following morning, Hermie helps the young bride move boxes into her attic, and when he turns down her offer of monetary compensation, she thanks him for his honesty and friendship and gives him a kiss on the forehead.][[0.0]]
[Later, in preparation for a marshmallow roast on the beach with Aggie and Miriam, Hermie and Oscy make carbon copies from the sex manual; then Hermie goes to the local drugstore, and in a protracted sequence attempts to build up the nerve to ask the pharmacist for condoms.][[0.0]]
[He eventually does so, after purchasing some ice cream, telling the pharmacist that the condoms are for his ``brother'' and he thinks that they are, in fact, a type of water balloon.][[0.0]]
[That night, during the marshmallow roast, Hermie finds himself unable to ``put the moves'' on Aggie, although Oscy is successful in having sex with Miriam between some sand dunes; he is so successful, in fact, he eventually sneaks over to where Hermie and Aggie are roasting marshmallows and asks Hermie to give him some condoms, having run out of his own.][[0.0]]
[Confused as to what's happening, Aggie follows Oscy back between the dunes, where she sees him having sex with Miriam and runs home crying.][[0.0]]
[Hermie, too, sees the act, although he is more mesmerized than anything.][[0.0]]
[The next day, Hermie comes across the young bride sitting outside her house, writing a letter to her husband.][[0.0]]
[Hermie offers to come keep her company that night and she says she looks forward to seeing him, finally revealing that her name is Dorothy.][[0.0]]
[An elated Hermie goes home and puts on a suit, saddle shoes, and a dress shirt, and heads back to Dorothy's house, running into Oscy on the way; Oscy relates Miriam's appendix burst that morning and she's been rushed to the mainland.][[0.0]]
[Hermie, now convinced he is at the brink of adulthood because of his relationship with Dorothy, brushes Oscy off and the two get into a fight.][[0.0]]
[Oscy threatens to tell everyone on the island that Hermie is a homosexual, and storms off.][[0.0]]
[Hermie heads over to Dorothy's house, which he finds eerily quiet.][[0.0]]
[Sneaking in, he discovers an empty bottle of whiskey, several cigarette butts, and a telegram from the U.S. Government, with a time stamp of just an hour prior, saying that Dorothy's husband is dead, his plane having been shot down over France.][[0.0]]
[Dorothy comes out of her bedroom, crying, and Hermie comforts her.][[0.0]]
[She moves to the record player and turns on an album and invites Hermie to dance with her.][[0.0]]
[Near the end of the song, Dorothy kisses Hermie and the two embrace, slowly moving to the bedroom, where she makes love with him.][[0.0]]
[Afterwards, Dorothy puts on her bathrobe and retires to the porch while Hermie dresses alone in her bedroom.][[0.0]]
[He approaches her on the porch, where she can only say ``good night'' to him.][[0.0]]
[Hermie leaves, his last image of Dorothy being that of her leaning against the railing, as she smokes a cigarette and stares off into the night sky.][[0.0]]
[Hermie spends the entire night roaming the island in a state of shock.][[0.0]]
[At dawn he meets Oscy and the two share a silent moment of reconciliation, broken only by Oscy's informing Hermie that Miriam survived her appendix bursting but will remain hospitalized until autumn.][[0.0]]
[Sensing that something traumatic has occurred between Hermie and Dorothy, Oscy, in an uncharacteristic act of sensitivity, lets Hermie be by himself, departing with the words, ``Sometimes life is just one big pain in the ass.''][[0.0]]
[Hermie goes back to Dorothy's house to try to sort out what has happened; he finds it abandoned, Dorothy having fled the island in the night.][[0.0]]
[All that remains is an envelope tacked to her front door with Hermie's name on it.][[1.0]]
[Hermie opens it; inside is a note from Dorothy, saying that she hopes he understands that she must go back home to arrange her husband's funeral and deal with familial obligations.][[0.0]]
[She assures Hermie that she will never forget him, and that she hopes one day he will come to terms with what happened that night.][[0.0]]
[Her note closes with the hope that Hermie may be spared the senseless tragedies of life.][[0.0]]
[In the film's final scene, Hermie is seen looking at Dorothy's old house and the ocean and remembering the day that he, Oscy, and Benjie first saw her, as the adult Herman Raucher sadly recounts that in the ensuing years he has never seen Dorothy again or learned what became of her.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Factual basis The film -LRB-and subsequent novel-RRB- were memoirs written by Herman Raucher; they detailed the events in his life over the course of the summer he spent on Nantucket Island in 1942 when he was fourteen years old.][[1.0]]
[Originally, the film was meant to be a tribute to his friend Oscar ``Oscy'' Seltzer, an Army medic killed in the Korean War.][[0.0]]
[Seltzer was shot dead on a battlefield in Korea whilst attending to a wounded man; this happened on Raucher's birthday, and consequently, Raucher has not celebrated a birthday since.][[0.0]]
[During the course of writing the screenplay, Raucher came to the realization that despite growing up with Oscy and having bonded with him through their formative years, the two had never really had any meaningful conversations or gotten to know one another on a more personal level.][[0.0]]
[Instead, Raucher decided to focus on the first major adult experience of his life, that of falling in love for the first time.][[0.0]]
[The woman -LRB-named Dorothy, like her screen counterpart-RRB- was a fellow vacationer on the island whom Raucher had befriended one day when he helped her carry groceries home; he became a friend of her and her husband and helped her with chores after her husband was called to fight in World War II.][[1.0]]
[Raucher went to bed with her one night when he came to visit her, arriving only minutes after she received notification of her husband's death.][[0.0]]
[The next morning, Raucher discovered that she had left the island, leaving behind a note for him -LRB-which is read at the end of the film and reproduced in the book-RRB-.][[1.0]]
[He never saw her again; his last ``encounter'' with her, recounted on an episode of The Mike Douglas Show, came after the film's release in 1971, when she was one of over a dozen women who wrote letters to Raucher claiming to be ``his'' Dorothy.][[0.0]]
[Raucher recognized the ``real'' Dorothy's handwriting, and she confirmed her identity by making references to certain events only she could have known about.][[0.0]]
[She told Raucher that she had lived for years with the guilt that she had potentially traumatized him and ruined his life.][[0.0]]
[She told Raucher that she was glad he turned out all right, and that they had best not re-visit the past.][[0.0]]
[In a 2002 interview, Raucher lamented never hearing from her again and expressed his hope that she was still alive.][[0.0]]
[Raucher's novelization of the screenplay, with the dedication, ``To those I love, past and present,'' serves more as the tribute to Seltzer that he had intended the film to be, with the focus of the book being more on the two boys' relationship than Raucher's relationship with Dorothy.][[0.0]]
[Consequently, the book also mentions Seltzer's death, which is omitted from the film adaptation.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Production Herman Raucher wrote the film script in the 1950s during his tenure as a television writer, but ``couldn't give it away.''][[0.0]]
[In the 1960s, he met Robert Mulligan, who had just finished directing To Kill a Mockingbird.][[0.0]]
[Raucher showed Mulligan the script, and Mulligan took it to Warner Bros., knowing that the studio was looking for a follow up to Mockingbird.][[0.0]]
[Mulligan argued the film could be shot for the relatively low price of a million dollars, and Warner approved it.][[0.0]]
[They had so little faith in the film becoming a box-office success, though, they shied from paying Raucher outright for the script, instead promising him ten percent of the gross.][[0.0]]
[When casting for the role of Dorothy, Warner Bros. declined to audition any actresses younger than the age of thirty; Jennifer O'Neill's agent, who had developed a fondness for the script, convinced Warner Bros. to audition his client, who was only twenty-two at the time.][[0.0]]
[O'Neill auditioned for the role, albeit hesitantly, not wanting to perform any nude scenes; O'Neill ended up getting the role and Robert Mulligan agreed to find a way to make the film work without blatant nudity.][[1.0]]
[Though the film took place on Nantucket, by the 1970s the island was too far modernized to be convincingly transformed to resemble a 1940s resort, so production was taken to the West Coast of the United States.][[0.0]]
[Shooting took place over eight weeks, during which Jennifer O'Neill was sequestered from the three boys cast as ``The Terrible Trio,'' in order to ensure that they didn't become close and ruin the sense of awkwardness and distance that their characters felt towards Dorothy.][[0.0]]
[Production ran smoothly, finishing on schedule.][[0.0]]
[After production, Warner Bros., still wary about the film only being a minor success, asked Raucher to adapt his script into a book.][[0.0]]
[Raucher wrote it in three weeks, and Warner Bros. released it prior to the film to build interest in the story.][[0.0]]
[The book quickly became a national bestseller, so that when trailers premiered in theatres, the film was billed as being ``based on the national bestseller,'' despite the film having been completed first.][[0.0]]
[Ultimately, the book became one of the best selling novels of the first half of the 1970s, requiring 23 re-prints between 1971 and 1974 to keep up with customer demand.][[1.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Soundtrack The film's soundtrack consists almost entirely of compositions by Michel Legrand, many of which are variants upon ``The Summer Knows'', the film's theme.][[0.0]]
[In addition to Legrand's scoring, the film also features the song ``Hold Tight'' by The Andrews Sisters and the theme from Now, Voyager.][[0.0]]
[Due to this lack of songs, when the soundtrack was released, it contained not only the score to Summer, but also Legrand's composition ``The Picasso Suite.''][[0.0]]
[In spite of this, many issues of the album are still labeled as exclusively being the soundtrack to Summer, while others contain the notation in small print on the album cover ``Also contains `The Picasso Suite'''.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Reception and awards The film became a blockbuster upon its release, grossing twenty-five million dollars, making it the fourth highest grossing film of 1971 and one of the most successful films in history, with an expense to profit ratio of 1:25; beyond that, it is estimated video rentals and purchases in the United States since the 1980s have produced an additional $20.5 million dollars.][[0.0]]
[On this point, Raucher says his ten-percent of the gross, in addition to royalties from book sales, has ``paid bills ever since.''][[0.0]]
[As well as being a commercial success, Summer of '42 also received rave critical reviews.][[0.0]]
[It went on to be nominated for over a dozen awards, including Golden Globe Awards for ``Best Motion Picture - Drama'' and ``Best Director'', and the Academy Award for ``Best Original Screenplay''.][[0.0]]
[Ultimately, the film only won two awards, the ``Best Score'' Oscar'' and the BAFTA Anthony Asquith Award for Film Music, both to Michel Legrand.][[0.0]]
[Still, it counted among its fans Stanley Kubrick, who in a rare moment of pop-culture infusion into his films, had the film play on a television in a scene in The Shining.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Sequel In 1973, the film was followed up with a sequel, Class of '44, a slice-of-life film made up of vignettes about Herman Raucher and Oscar Selzter's experiences in college prior to fighting in the Korean War.][[0.0]]
[The only crew member left from Summer of '42 was Raucher himself, with a new director and composer being brought in to replace Mulligan and Legrand.][[0.0]]
[Of the principal four cast members of Summer of '42, only Jerry Houser and Gary Grimes returned for prominent roles.][[1.0]]
[Oliver Conant did appear in the film, albeit for less than five minutes of screen time.][[0.0]]
[Jennifer O'Neill did not appear in the film at all, nor was the character of Dorothy mentioned.][[0.0]]
[The film met with poor critical reviews; the only three reviews available at rottentomatoes.com are resoundingly negative, with Channel 4 calling it ``a big disappointment,'' and The New York Times stating ``The only things worth attention in `Class of 44' are the period details,'' and ''`Class of '44' seems less like a movie than 95 minutes of animated wallpaper.''][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Influence Legrand's theme song for the film, ``The Summer Knows'', has since become a pop standard, being recorded by such artists as Peter Nero -LRB-who had a charting hit with his 1971 version-RRB-, Tony Bennett, Frank Sinatra, Andy Williams, and Barbra Streisand.][[0.0]]
[The 1973 song ``Summer -LRB-The First Time-RRB-'' by Bobby Goldsboro has almost exactly the same subject and apparent setting, although there is no direct credited link.][[0.0]]
[Bryan Adams has, however, credited the film as being a partial inspiration for his 1985 hit ``Summer of '69''.][[0.0]]
[The Simpsons episode ``Summer of 4 Ft. 2'' -LRB-alternately titled `Summer of 4'2'''-RRB- was largely a parody of Summer of '42.][[0.0]]
[It amalgamated scenes from another early '70s coming-of-age film, American Graffiti -LRB-both acknowledged in the DVD commentary for the episode-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[There are also similarities between Summer of '42 and Malèna, another coming-of-age film set in the context of World War II, and starring Monica Bellucci and Giuseppe Sulfaro.][[0.0]]
[An episode of the 1970s sitcom Happy Days was loosely based upon Summer of '42, with Richie Cunningham befriending a Korean War widow.][[0.0]]
[In Family Guy episode ``Play It Again, Brian'', Brian wins an award for his essay and reads an excerpt: ``She was Grace, in name and in essence.][[0.0]]
[To those she loved, she exuded strength, life, laughter and light, and to me, also sorrow for circumstance that had bound her to my best friend through whom we met in the warmth and serenity of her home.][[0.0]]
[Nothing from the first day I saw her and no one that has happened to me since, has ever been as frightning and as confusing, for no person I've ever known has ever done more to make me feel more sure, more insecure, more important and less significant.''][[0.0]]
[Later in that episode, he admits that he ``ripped off'' most of the essay from Summer of '42.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Remakes and re-releases In the ensuing years since the film's release, Warner Bros. has attempted to buy back Raucher's ten-percent of the film as well as his rights to the story so it could be remade; Raucher has consistently declined.][[0.0]]
[The 1988 film Stealing Home shares numerous similarities not only to Summer of '42 but also Class of '44, with several incidents -LRB-most notably a subplot dealing with the premature death of the protagonist's father and the protagonist's response to it-RRB- appearing to have been directly lifted from Raucher's own life; Jennifer O'Neill stated in 2002 she believes ``Home'' was an attempted remake of ``Summer''.][[0.0]]
[In 2001, Raucher consented to the film being made into an off Broadway musical play.][[0.0]]
[He was on hand opening night, giving the cast a pep-talk which he concluded, ``We've now done it every possible way--except go out and piss it in the snow!''][[0.0]]
[The play met with positive critical and fan response, and was endorsed by Raucher himself, but the play was forced to close down in the aftermath of the 11 September attacks.][[0.0]]
[Nevertheless, the play was enough to spark interest in the film and book with a new generation, prompting Warner to re-issue the book -LRB-which had since gone out of print, along with all of Raucher's other works-RRB- for sale with Barnes & Noble's online bookstore, and to restore the film and release it on DVD.][[1.0]]
[The musical has since been performed across the country, at venues such as Kalliope Stage in Cleveland Heights, Ohio in 2004 -LRB-directed by Paul Gurgol-RRB- and Mill Mountain Theatre in Roanake, VA -LRB-directed by Jere Hodgin and choreographed by Bernard Monroe-RRB-, and was subsequently recorded as a concert by the York Theatre Company in 2006.][[0.0]]
[In 2002, Jennifer O'Neill claimed to have obtained the rights to make a sequel to Summer of '42, based on a short story she wrote, which took place in an alternate reality in which Herman Raucher had a son and divorced his wife, went back to Nantucket in 1962 with a still-living Oscar Seltzer, and encountered Dorothy again and married her.][[0.0]]
[As of 2006, this project--which O'Neill had hoped to produce with Lifetime television, has not been realized, and it is unknown whether O'Neill is still attempting to get it produced, or if Raucher -LRB-who technically has no say-RRB- consented to its production.][[0.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Grand Staircase The rocks exposed in Bryce Canyon are about 100 million years younger than those in nearby Zion National Park, and the rocks exposed in Zion are younger than those in the Grand Canyon to the south.][[1.0]]
[There are, however, shared rock units between all three, creating a supersequence of formations that geologists call the Grand Staircase.][[1.0]]
[Together the formations of the Grand Staircase record nearly 2000 million years of the Earth's history.][[0.0]]
[Bryce Canyon's formations are the youngest known units in the Grand Staircase.][[0.0]]
[Younger rock units, if they ever existed, have been removed by erosion.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Cretaceous Seaway -LSB-edit-RSB- Advance In the Cretaceous a shallow seaway spread into the interior of North America from the Gulf of Mexico in the south into Utah and later to the Arctic Ocean in the far north.][[0.0]]
[Geologists call this shallow sea the Cretaceous Seaway or Western Interior Seaway.][[0.0]]
[Whatever its name, the seaway divided North America into two halves; an eastern portion dominated by the already ancient Appalachian Mountains and a western part composed primarily of the still growing Sevier Mountains; formed from shallow thrust faulting caused by the Sevier orogeny.][[1.0]]
[As the shoreline moved back and forth, the Bryce area alternated from being part of the Sevier landmass to being under the Cretaceous Seaway.][[1.0]]
[Alternating layers of nonmarine, intertidal, and marine sediments lay on top of each other as a result.][[0.0]]
[Conglomerate, siltstone, and fossil-rich sandstone that together are up to 300�feet -LRB-90�m-RRB- thick mark the arrival of the Cretaceous Seaway.][[0.0]]
[Called the Dakota Sandstone, it is the oldest formation exposed in the Bryce Canyon area but the youngest one exposed in the Zion and Kolob canyons area to the southwest.][[0.0]]
[Abundant amounts of petrified wood, oyster beds containing millions of fossils and coal are all found in the Dakota.][[0.0]]
[In the Bryce Canyon area this formation can be seen in the Paria Valley where it is found as a lithified blanket sand that probably accumulated on beaches, in lagoons, and vast coal-producing swamps as the Cretaceous Seaway transgressed -LRB-advanced inland-RRB- over the region and later retreated.][[1.0]]
[It sits unconformably on much older Jurassic formations that are not exposed in the immediate area -LRB-see geology of the Zion and Kolob canyons area for a discussion about these older sediments-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Mud and silt were deposited on top of the Dakota Formation as the seaway became deeper and calmer in the area.][[0.0]]
[The resulting dark gray to black Tropic Shale records the maximum transgression of the seaway into Utah and is 1,000�feet -LRB-300�m-RRB- thick in the Paria Amphitheater.][[0.0]]
[It forms the unvegetated badlands seen in the Tropic Valley and is perhaps the most fossil-rich formation in the area; containing numerous straight-shelled and coiled ammonites.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Retreat The Cretaceous Seaway was already retreating east and to the south by the time the locally 1,700�feet -LRB-520�m-RRB- thick Straight Cliffs Formation was deposited.][[0.0]]
[Its members represent various stages in this process.][[0.0]]
[The cliff-forming sandstone of the Tibbet Canyon Member was conformably deposited on top of the Tropic Shale in shallow marine and later near shore environments.][[1.0]]
[Shale and sandstone from the Smoky Hollow Member were deposited on top of its basal layer of coal-rich mudstone in coastal swamps and lagoons on the shore of the seaway.][[0.0]]
[While the alternating layers of shale and sandstone mixed with massive coal deposits of the John Henry Member were laid down in swamps, lagoons and fluvial environments one member, the Drip Tank, is not found in the Bryce Canyon area.][[0.0]]
[This formation erodes into almost unclimbable cliffs and escarpments of whitish to yellow-gray sandstones with comparatively thin interbedded layers of shale and mudstone.][[0.0]]
[Shark teeth are found in the lower parts of the formation.][[0.0]]
[Lakes and east-flowing rivers became the dominant resting place for sediment following the retreat of the Cretaceous Seaway.][[0.0]]
[The shales and sandstones of the locally 700�feet -LRB-210�m-RRB- thick Wahweap Formation were deposited in moving water -LRB-fluvial setting-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[This formation is part of the Grey Cliffs of the Grand Staircase mentioned previously.][[0.0]]
[It contains abundant fossils of vertebrates, including dinosaurs such as the hadrosaurs.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Continental deposition -LSB-edit-RSB- Flood plains uplift and erode A flood plain crossed by rivers and lakes developed in the area.][[0.0]]
[Mud and sand accumulated in this setting to become the gray sandstones and mudstones of the Kaiparowits Formation.][[0.0]]
[This formation is up to 100�feet -LRB-30�m-RRB- thick in the Bryce Canyon area but other parts of the Kaiparowits in the region are several hundreds of feet -LRB-tens of meters-RRB- thick.][[0.0]]
[Two formations, the Canaan Peak and the Pine Hollow, sit on top of the Kaiparowits elsewhere in the region but are absent in the Bryce Canyon area.][[0.0]]
[The sandstones and conglomerates of these formations record stream and river deposition starting in the Paleocene epoch.][[0.0]]
[Uplift caused by a mountain-building episode called the Laramide orogeny lasted from the late Cretaceous around 70�mya to the early Paleocene.][[1.0]]
[This hoisted the once lower uplands skyward while low-lying basins between them gradually subsided.][[0.0]]
[Compression from the Laramide event deformed the land in the area to form the up to 5° dipping Bryce Canyon Anticline.][[0.0]]
[All of the Canaan Peak, Pine Hollow, Kaiparowits, and Waheap formations, along with part of the underlying Straight Cliffs, were removed from the anticline's crest by erosion before the Claron Formation was deposited.][[0.0]]
[An angular unconformity therefore exists along the anticline's crest.][[0.0]]
[The park also sits on the western gently dipping flank of the much larger Kaibab uplift, which was also formed as a result of the Laramide.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Claron flood plain and lake system Uplift from the Laramide paused briefly in the Eocene.][[0.0]]
[Meandering streams flowed slowly over the resulting broad and almost featureless plains.][[0.0]]
[Periodic but extensive floods inundated large areas perhaps once every 1,000 years; spreading mud, cobbles and fine silt over the plains.][[0.0]]
[Erosion incised these deposits between flood events and plant growth was abundant.][[0.0]]
[Oxidation of the iron in the mud and silt turned the soil into hematite, giving it a pink and red hue.][[0.0]]
[These sediments were later lithified into the up to 700�feet -LRB-210�m-RRB- thick Pink Member of the locally Eocene-aged Claron Formation -LRB-previously called the Wasatch Formation-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Channelized conglomerates of this member can be easily seen in Red Canyon along State Route 12 while its silt and mudstones compose most of the park's fragile and colorful spires called hoodoos.][[0.0]]
[Geologist Clarence Dutton called the iron oxide-rich lower member of the Claron the Pink Cliffs series due to its colorful appearance.][[0.0]]
[A large system of shallow but expansive lakes and associated deltas covered several thousand square miles of what is now northwest Colorado and southwest Utah and Wyoming.][[0.0]]
[These lakes existed from the Paleocene to mid Oligocene but did not spread to the Bryce Canyon area until Eocene time.][[0.0]]
[Large quantities of lakebed sediments were laid down in this system during the 20 million years of its existence from about 60 to 40�mya.][[0.0]]
[Climate change and cycles caused the lakes in the system to expand and shrink through time.][[0.0]]
[As they did so, they left beds of differing thickness and composition stacked atop one another;  The limey ooses and mud were later lithified into the limestone and interbedded siltstone of the up to 300�foot -LRB-90�m-RRB- thick White Member of the Claron.][[0.0]]
[This member erodes into white-colored monoliths that are only found at the highest elevations of the Paunsaugunt Plateau.][[0.0]]
[Fossils are rare in the White Member and mainly consist of freshwater snails and clams, indicating that the lakes supported little life.][[0.0]]
[Most arches and natural bridges in the park, including the famous Natural Bridge, were carved from sandstone beds in the Claron.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Marysvale volcanics A gap in the geologic record following deposition of the Claron Formation was interrupted 34 to 31�mya by eruptions from the nearby Marysvale volcanic field, which is located northwest of the park.][[0.0]]
[Volcanic ash and lava from these flows are found less than 20�miles -LRB-30�km-RRB- from Bryce Canyon but at least some volcanic material was likely deposited directly in the park area only to be later removed by erosion.][[0.0]]
[Most of the activity at the Marysvale volcanic field occurred during three separate intervals; ~34--22�mya, 22--14�mya and 9--5�mya.][[0.0]]
[Dacites and andesites were erupted above an evolving batholith in the first interval.][[0.0]]
[Crystal-rich ash from the 27�million year old -LRB-myo-RRB- Three Creeks caldera, 24�myo Big John caldera and 23�myo Monroe Peak caldera hardened into tuff.][[0.0]]
[The second and third intervals saw eruptions of great quantities of rhyolites.][[0.0]]
[Alkali-rich rhyolite erupted in the second interval from the 19�myo Mount Belknap caldera.][[0.0]]
[The Marysvale volcanic field collapsed under its own weight around 20�mya; likely due to weaknesses in the evaporites of the Carmel Formation some 5,000�feet -LRB-1,500�m-RRB- below.][[0.0]]
[Folding and faulting of the Claron Formation from the collapse created Ruby's Inn thrust.][[0.0]]
[A slight downwarp running east--west and perpendicular to the thrust motion called the Bryce syncline was also created.][[0.0]]
[Volcanic activity in the Marysvale and Bryce area ceased some 500,000 years ago.][[0.0]]
[Basaltic rocks of the same age can be seen along the Sevier Fault near the entrance to Red Canyon; the dark colored volcanic rocks have been displaced by the fault some 900�feet -LRB-300�m-RRB- and are now in direct contact with the much older Claron Formation.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Late Cenozoic tectonics -LSB-edit-RSB- Formation of the High Plateaus Younger rock units were laid down but were mostly removed by subsequent uplift-accelerated erosion.][[0.0]]
[Outcrops of these formations can be found in the northern part of the park and in a few places on the plateau rim.][[0.0]]
[Among these are the 50- to 100-foot-thick -LRB-15 to 30�m-RRB- Oligocene or Miocene-aged Boat Mesa Conglomerate and the Pliocene to early Pleistocene-aged Sevier River Formation.][[0.0]]
[The Boat Mesa is made mostly of conglomerates with minor amounts of sandstone and some limestone from lakes, representing stream and overbank flood deposits.][[0.0]]
[The brownish-gray sandstone and gravels of the Sevier River Formation were laid down in valleys that were part of the ancestral Sevier River drainage system.][[0.0]]
[Around 15�mya in Miocene time, tensional forces in Nevada to the west were so great that the crust was spread thin, creating the Basin and Range Province.][[0.0]]
[These same forces segmented what is now the western part of the Colorado Plateau into nine different smaller plateaus, including the Paunsaugunt that the park sits astride.][[0.0]]
[Long, north--south-trending normal faults were either newly created or reactivated from older pre-existing faults; a plateau rose on one side of each fault while valleys subsided on the other as the crust was extended in an east-west direction.][[0.0]]
[Two of these faults bound the Paunsaugunt Plateau; the Sevier on the west and the Paunsaugunt on the east.][[0.0]]
[Movement along these two faults has displaced the Claron Formation by 2,000�feet -LRB-600�m-RRB- relative to the Paria and Sevier valleys.][[0.0]]
[The Hurricane Fault marks the west edge of the Markagunt Plateau and is the topographic boundary between the Basin and Range and the Colorado Plateaus provinces.][[0.0]]
[Cedar Breaks National Monument, which shares almost the same exposed geology and erosional features as Bryce Canyon National Park, sits on the west edge of the Markagunt.][[0.0]]
[The entire Colorado Plateau then started to uplift from near sea level to several thousand feet -LRB-over a kilometer-RRB- in elevation.][[1.0]]
[An alternate theory is that the Laramide orogeny uplifted what is today the Basin and Range and the Colorado Plateau and that the tensional forces that formed the Basin and Range caused that region to subside relative to the Colorado Plateau.][[0.0]]
[Whatever the order of events were, the High Plateaus region of the Colorado Plateau were by now nearly complete.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Modern drainage and erosion Drainage of the Colorado Plateau was significantly altered by the opening of the Gulf of California.][[1.0]]
[Rifting tore Baja California Peninsula northwestward from the Mexican mainland starting some 10 to 5�mya.][[0.0]]
[The ancestral Colorado River responded to the regional downwarping by taking a shortcut to the sea by flowing into the new gulf.][[0.0]]
[This significantly decreased the distance from the river's headwaters and its delta at the sea.][[0.0]]
[Water in the Colorado and its tributaries moved faster as a result and cut down deeper, creating the canyonland topography.][[0.0]]
[Formation of approximately the current depth of the Colorado River's Grand Canyon by 1.2 mya further caused its tributaries to cut down even deeper.][[0.0]]
[Headward erosion of one of those tributaries, the Paria River, eroded north-northwestward toward what is now Paria Amphitheater.][[0.0]]
[The river took a route roughly parallel to and east of the Paunsaugunt Fault.][[0.0]]
[Erosion from snow and rain that fall directly on the east-facing rim of the Paunsaugunt Plateau forms gullies that widen into alcoves and amphitheaters while differential erosion and frost wedging create the hoodoos.][[0.0]]
[Streams on the plateau do not contribute to the formation of alcoves or amphitheaters because they flow away from the rim.][[0.0]]
[Erosion continues in this fashion today.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Hoodoo formation in Bryce Canyon The Pink Member of the Claron Formation is largely composed of easily eroded and relatively soft limestone.][[0.0]]
[When rain combines with carbon dioxide it forms a weak solution of carbonic acid.][[0.0]]
[This acid helps to slowly dissolve the limestone in the Claron Formation grain by grain.][[0.0]]
[It is this process of chemical weathering that rounds the edges of hoodoos and gives them their lumpy and bulging profiles.][[0.0]]
[In the winter, melting snow seeps into cracks and joints and freezes at night.][[0.0]]
[The force of the expanding ice helps to erode the rock of the Claron Formation.][[0.0]]
[Over 200 of these freeze/thaw cycles occur each year in Bryce Canyon.][[0.0]]
[Frost wedging exploits and widens the nearly vertical joint planes that divide the Pink Member of the Claron Formation.][[0.0]]
[Internal layers of mudstone, conglomerate and siltstone interrupt the limestone horizontally.][[0.0]]
[These layers are more resistant to attack by carbonic acid and they can therefore act as protective capstones of fins, windows and hoodoos.][[0.0]]
[Many of the more durable hoodoos are capped with a type of magnesium-rich limestone called dolomite.][[0.0]]
[Dolomite dissolves at a much slower rate, and consequently protects the weaker limestone underneath.][[0.0]]
[However, the same processes that create hoodoos will also eventually destroy them.][[0.0]]
[In the case of Bryce Canyon, the hoodoos' rate of erosion is 2--4�feet -LRB-0.6--1.3�m-RRB- every 100 years.][[0.0]]
[As the canyon continues to erode to the west it will eventually capture -LRB-in perhaps 3 million years-RRB- the watershed of the East Fork of the Sevier River.][[0.0]]
[Once this river flows through Bryce Amphitheater it will dominate the erosional pattern; replacing hoodoos with a V-shaped canyon and steep cliff walls typical of the weathering and erosional patterns created by rivers.][[0.0]]
[A foreshadowing of this can be observed in Water Canyon while hiking the Mossy Cave Trail.][[1.0]]
[A diversion canal has been taking a portion of the East Fork of the Sevier River through this section of the park for over 100 years.][[1.0]]
