[-LSB-edit-RSB- History For many years, a growing problem in astronomical research -LRB-as in other academic disciplines-RRB- was that the number of papers published in the major astronomical journals was increasing steadily, meaning astronomers were able to read less and less of the latest research findings.][[0.0]]
[During the 1980s, astronomers saw that the nascent technologies which formed the basis of the Internet could eventually be used to build an electronic indexing system of astronomical research papers which would allow astronomers to keep abreast of a much greater range of research.][[0.0]]
[The first suggestion of a database of journal paper abstracts was made at a conference on Astronomy from Large Data-bases held in Garching bei München in 1987.][[0.0]]
[Initial development of an electronic system for accessing astrophysical abstracts took place during the following two years; in 1991 discussions took place on how to integrate ADS with the SIMBAD database, containing all available catalog designations for objects outside the solar system, to create a system where astronomers could search for all the papers written about a given object.][[0.0]]
[An initial version of ADS, with a database consisting of 40 papers, was created as a proof of concept in 1988, and the ADS database was successfully connected with the SIMBAD database in the summer of 1993.][[0.0]]
[The creators believed this was the first use of the Internet to allow simultaneous querying of transatlantic scientific databases.][[0.0]]
[Until 1994, the service was available via proprietary network software, but it was transferred to the nascent World Wide Web early that year.][[0.0]]
[The number of users of the service quadrupled in the five weeks following the introduction of the ADS web-based service.][[0.0]]
[At first, the journal articles available via ADS were scanned bitmaps created from the paper journals, but from 1995 onwards, the Astrophysical Journal began to publish an on-line edition, soon followed by the other main journals such as Astronomy and Astrophysics and the Monthly Notices of the Royal Astronomical Society.][[1.0]]
[ADS provided links to these electronic editions from their first appearance.][[0.0]]
[Since about 1995, the number of ADS users has doubled roughly every two years.][[0.0]]
[ADS now has agreements with almost all astronomical journals, who supply abstracts.][[0.0]]
[Scanned articles from as far back as the early 19th century are available via the service, which now contains over eight million documents.][[0.0]]
[The service is distributed worldwide, with twelve mirror sites in twelve countries on five continents, with the database synchronized by means of weekly updates using rsync, a mirroring utility which allows updates to only the portions of the database which have changed.][[0.0]]
[All updates are triggered centrally, but they initiate scripts at the mirror sites which ``pull'' updated data from the main ADS servers.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Data in the system Papers are indexed within the database by their bibliographic record, containing the details of the journal they were published in and various associated metadata, such as author lists, references and citations.][[0.0]]
[Originally this data was stored in ASCII format, but eventually the limitations of this encouraged the database maintainers to migrate all records to an XML -LRB-Extensible Markup Language-RRB- format in 2000.][[0.0]]
[Bibliographic records are now stored as an XML element, with sub-elements for the various metadata.][[0.0]]
[Since the advent of online editions of journals, abstracts are loaded into the ADS on or before the publication date of articles, with the full journal text available to subscribers.][[1.0]]
[Older articles have been scanned, and an abstract is created using optical character recognition software.][[0.0]]
[Scanned articles from before about 1995 are usually available free, by agreement with the journal publishers.][[0.0]]
[Scanned articles are stored in TIFF format, at both medium and high resolution.][[0.0]]
[The TIFF files are converted on demand into GIF files for on-screen viewing, and PDF or PostScript files for printing.][[0.0]]
[The generated files are then cached to eliminate needlessly frequent regenerations for popular articles.][[0.0]]
[As of 2000, ADS contained 250 GB of scans, which consisted of 1,128,955 article pages comprising 138,789 articles.][[0.0]]
[By 2005 this had grown to 650 GB, and is expected to grow further, to about 900 GB by 2007.][[0.0]]
[No further information has been published.][[0.0]]
[The database initially contained only astronomical references, but has now grown to incorporate three databases, covering astronomy -LRB-including planetary sciences and solar physics-RRB- references, physics -LRB-including instrumentation and geosciences-RRB- references, as well as preprints of scientific papers from arXiv.][[1.0]]
[The astronomy database is by far the most advanced and its use accounts for about 85% of the total ADS usage.][[0.0]]
[Articles are assigned to the different databases according to the subject rather than the journal they are published in, so that articles from any one journal might appear in all three subject databases.][[0.0]]
[The separation of the databases allows searching in each discipline to be tailored, so that words can automatically be given different weight functions in different database searches, depending on how common they are in the relevant field.][[0.0]]
[Data in the preprint archive is updated daily from the arXiv, the main repository of physics and astronomy preprints.][[0.0]]
[The advent of preprint servers has, like ADS, had a significant impact on the rate of astronomical research, as papers are often made available from preprint servers weeks or months before they are published in the journals.][[0.0]]
[The incorporation of preprints from the arXiv into ADS means that the search engine can return the most current research available, with the caveat that preprints may not have been peer reviewed or proofread to the required standard for publication in the main journals.][[0.0]]
[ADS's database links preprints with subsequently published articles wherever possible, so that citation and reference searches will return links to the journal article where the preprint was cited.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Software and hardware The software runs on a system that was written specifically for it, allowing for extensive customization for astronomical needs that would not have been possible with general purpose database software.][[0.0]]
[The scripts are designed to be as platform independent as possible, given the need to facilitate mirroring on different systems around the world, although the growing use of Linux as the operating system of choice within astronomy has led to increasing optimization of the scripts for installation on that platform.][[0.0]]
[The main ADS server is located at the Harvard-Smithsonian Center for Astrophysics in Cambridge, Massachusetts, and is a dual 64-bit X86 Intel server with two quad-core 3.0 GHz CPUs and 32 GB of RAM, running the CentOS 5.4 Linux distribution.][[1.0]]
[Mirrors are located in Brazil, China, Chile, France, Germany, India, Indonesia, Japan, Russia, South Korea, United Kingdom, and the Ukraine.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Indexing ADS currently receives abstracts or tables of contents from almost two hundred journal sources.][[0.0]]
[The service may receive data referring to the same article from multiple sources, and creates one bibliographic reference based on the most accurate data from each source.][[0.0]]
[The common use of TeX and LaTeX by almost all scientific journals greatly facilitates the incorporation of bibliographic data into the system in a standardized format, and importing HTML-coded web-based articles is also simple.][[0.0]]
[ADS utilizes Perl scripts for importing, processing and standardizing bibliographic data.][[0.0]]
[The apparently mundane task of converting author names into a standard Surname, Initial format is actually one of the more difficult to automate, due to the wide variety of naming conventions around the world and the possibility that a given name such as Davis could be a first name, middle name or surname.][[0.0]]
[The accurate conversion of names requires a detailed knowledge of the names of authors active in astronomy, and ADS maintains an extensive database of author names, which is also used in searching the database -LRB-see below-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[For electronic articles, a list of the references given at the end of the article is easily extracted.][[0.0]]
[For scanned articles, reference extraction relies on OCR.][[0.0]]
[The reference database can then be ``inverted'' to list the citations for each paper in the database.][[0.0]]
[Citation lists have been used in the past to identify popular articles missing from the database; mostly these were from before 1975 and have now been added to the system.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Coverage The database now contains over eight million articles.][[0.0]]
[In the cases of the major journals of astronomy -LRB-Astrophysical Journal, Astronomical Journal, Astronomy and Astrophysics, Publications of the Astronomical Society of the Pacific and the Monthly Notices of the Royal Astronomical Society-RRB-, coverage is complete, with all issues indexed from number 1 to the present.][[0.0]]
[These journals account for about two-thirds of the papers in the database, with the rest consisting of papers published in over 100 other journals from around the world.][[0.0]]
[While the database contains the complete contents of all the major journals and many minor ones as well, its coverage of references and citations is much less complete.][[0.0]]
[References in and citations of articles in the major journals are fairly complete, but references such as ``private communication'', ``in press'' or ``in preparation'' cannot be matched, and author errors in reference listings also introduce potential errors.][[0.0]]
[Astronomical papers may cite and be cited by articles in journals which fall outside the scope of ADS, such as chemistry, mathematics or biology journals.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Search engine Since its inception, the ADS has developed a highly complex search engine to query the abstract and object databases.][[0.0]]
[The search engine is tailor-made for searching astronomical abstracts, and the engine and its user interface assume that the user is well-versed in astronomy and able to interpret search results which are designed to return more than just the most relevant papers.][[0.0]]
[The database can be queried for author names, astronomical object names, title words, and words in the abstract text, and results can be filtered according to a number of criteria.][[0.0]]
[It works by first gathering synonyms and simplifying search terms as described above, and then generating an ``inverted file'', which is a list of all the documents matching each search term.][[0.0]]
[The user-selected logic and filters are then applied to this inverted list to generate the final search results.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Author name queries The system indexes author names by surname and initials, and accounts for the possible variations in spelling of names using a list of variations.][[0.0]]
[This is common in the case of names including accents such as umlauts and transliterations from Arabic or Cyrillic script.][[0.0]]
[An example of an entry in the author synonym list is: -LSB-edit-RSB- Object name searches The capability to search for papers on specific astronomical objects is one of ADS's most powerful tools.][[0.0]]
[The system uses data from the SIMBAD, the NASA/IPAC Extragalactic Database, the International Astronomical Union Circulars and the Lunar and Planetary Institute to identify papers referring to a given object, and can also search by object position, listing papers which concern objects within a 10�arcminute radius of a given Right Ascension and Declination.][[0.0]]
[These databases combine the many catalogue designations an object might have, so that a search for the Pleiades will also find papers which list the famous open cluster in Taurus under any of its other catalog designations or popular names, such as M45, the Seven Sisters or Melotte 22.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Title and abstract searches The search engine first filters search terms in several ways.][[0.0]]
[An M followed by a space or hyphen has the space or hyphen removed, so that searching for Messier catalogue objects is simplified and a user input of M45, M 45 or M-45 all result in the same query being executed; similarly, NGC designations and common search terms such as Shoemaker Levy and T Tauri are stripped of spaces.][[0.0]]
[Unimportant words such as AT, OR and TO are stripped out, although in some cases case sensitivity is maintained, so that while and is ignored, And is converted to ``Andromedae'', and Her is converted to ``Herculis'', but her is ignored.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Synonym replacement Once search terms have been pre-processed, the database is queried with the revised search term, as well as synonyms for it.][[0.0]]
[As well as simple synonym replacement such as searching for both plural and singular forms, ADS also searches for a large number of specifically astronomical synonyms.][[0.0]]
[For example, spectrograph and spectroscope have basically the same meaning, and in an astronomical context metallicity and abundance are also synonymous.][[0.0]]
[ADS's synonym list was created manually, by grouping the list of words in the database according to similar meanings.][[0.0]]
[As well as English language synonyms, ADS also searches for English translations of foreign search terms and vice versa, so that a search for the French word soleil retrieves references to Sun, and papers in languages other than English can be returned by English search terms.][[0.0]]
[Synonym replacement can be disabled if required, so that a rare term which is a synonym of a much more common term -LRB-such as `dateline' rather than `date'-RRB- can be searched for specifically.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Selection logic The search engine allows selection logic both within fields and between fields.][[0.0]]
[Search terms in each field can be combined with OR, AND, simple logic or Boolean logic, and the user can specify which fields must be matched in the search results.][[0.0]]
[This allows complex searches to be built; for example, the user could search for papers concerning NGC 6543 OR NGC 7009, with the paper titles containing -LRB-radius OR velocity-RRB- AND NOT -LRB-abundance OR temperature-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Result filtering Search results can be filtered according to a number of criteria, including specifying a range of years such as '1945 to 1975', '2000 to the present day' or `before 1900', and what type of journal the article appears in -- non-peer reviewed articles such as conference proceedings can be excluded or specifically searched for, or specific journals can be included in or excluded from the search.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Search results Although it was conceived as a means of accessing abstracts and papers, ADS provides a substantial amount of ancillary information along with search results.][[0.0]]
[For each abstract returned, links are provided to other papers in the database which are referenced, and which cite the paper, and a link is provided to a preprint, where one exists.][[0.0]]
[The system also generates a link to `also-read' articles -- that is, those which have been most commonly accessed by those reading the article.][[0.0]]
[In this way, an ADS user can determine which papers are of most interest to astronomers who are interested in the subject of a given paper.][[0.0]]
[Also returned are links to the SIMBAD and/or NASA Extragalactic Database object name databases, via which a user can quickly find out basic observational data about the objects analyzed in a paper, and find further papers on those objects.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Impact on astronomy ADS is almost universally used as a research tool among astronomers, and there are several studies that have estimated quantitatively how much more efficient ADS has made astronomy; one estimated that ADS increased the efficiency of astronomical research by 333�full-time equivalent research years per year, and another found that in 2002 its effect was equivalent to 736�full-time researchers, or all the astronomical research done in France.][[1.0]]
[ADS has allowed literature searches that would previously have taken days or weeks to carry out to be completed in seconds, and it is estimated that ADS has increased the readership and use of the astronomical literature by a factor of about three since its inception.][[1.0]]
[In monetary terms, this increase in efficiency represents a considerable amount.][[0.0]]
[There are about 12,000�active astronomical researchers worldwide, so ADS is the equivalent of about 5% of the working population of astronomers.][[0.0]]
[The global astronomical research budget is estimated at between 4,000 and 5,000�million USD, so the value of ADS to astronomy would be about 200--250�million USD annually.][[1.0]]
[Its operating budget is a small fraction of this amount.][[0.0]]
[The great importance of ADS to astronomers has been recognized by the United Nations, the General Assembly of which has commended ADS on its work and success, particularly noting its importance to astronomers in the developing world, in reports of the United Nations Committee on the Peaceful Uses of Outer Space.][[0.0]]
[A 2002 report by a visiting committee to the Center for Astrophysics, meanwhile, said that the service had ``revolutionized the use of the astronomical literature'', and was ``probably the most valuable single contribution to astronomy research that the CfA has made in its lifetime''.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Sociological studies using ADS Because it is used almost universally by astronomers, ADS can reveal much about how astronomical research is distributed around the world.][[0.0]]
[Most users access the system from institutes of higher education, whose IP address can easily be used to determine the user's geographical location.][[0.0]]
[Studies reveal that the highest per-capita users of ADS are France and Netherlands-based astronomers, and while more developed countries -LRB-measured by GDP per capita-RRB- use the system more than less developed countries; the relationship between GDP per capita and ADS use is not linear.][[0.0]]
[The range of ADS usage per capita far exceeds the range of GDPs per capita, and basic research carried out in a country, as measured by ADS usage, has been found to be proportional to the square of the country's GDP divided by its population.][[1.0]]
[ADS usage statistics also suggest that astronomers in more developed countries tend to be more productive than those in less developed countries.][[1.0]]
[The amount of basic research carried out is proportional to the number of astronomers in a country multiplied by the GDP per capita.][[0.0]]
[Statistics also imply that astronomers in European cultures carry out about three times as much research as those in Asian cultures, perhaps suggesting cultural differences in the importance attached to astronomical research.][[0.0]]
[ADS has also been used to show that the fraction of single-author astronomy papers has decreased substantially since 1975 and that astronomical papers with more than 50 authors have become more common since 1990.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Comparision to what the National Library of Medicine has done The National Library of Medicine also has a free to users, supported by tax dollars, online database of scientific publications, PubMed.][[0.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Party backgrounds -LSB-edit-RSB- Australian Labor Party The Australian Labor Party is Australia's oldest political party, founded in 1891.][[0.0]]
[It is a centre-left social democratic party which is formally linked to the trade union labour movement.][[0.0]]
[On a state level, Labor has been in government since 2002, after having been in opposition from 1993 to 2002.][[0.0]]
[Since the 1970 election ending decades of electoral malapportionment of the Playmander, nine of 12 elections have been won by Labor.][[0.0]]
[Labor's premiers in South Australia include Thomas Price in the 1900s, to the reformist Don Dunstan in the 1970s to the factionally nonaligned and pragmatic current premier, Mike Rann.][[0.0]]
[The party's deputy leader, and therefore the Deputy Premier, is Kevin Foley.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Liberal Party of Australia The Liberal Party of Australia is a centre-right conservative liberal party -LRB-see Liberalism in Australia-RRB-, with close links to business and advocating free markets.][[0.0]]
[Whilst primarily a social conservative party, there exists a more social liberal wing, colloquially known as `wet', `moderate' or small-l liberals, highlighted by the short-lived Liberal Movement who first contested the 1975 election as a separate party led by Steele Hall.][[0.0]]
[At state level, the Liberal Party of Australia in 1973 descended from the Liberal and Country League -LRB-LCL-RRB-, which resulted from a merger between the Liberal Federation and the then-Country Party in 1932.][[0.0]]
[The state opposition leader at the 2006 election, Rob Kerin, was factionally nonaligned.][[1.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Nationals SA The Nationals SA are a sub-division of the conservative National Party of Australia -LRB-formerly the Country Party-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[First contesting the 1965 election, they have only held two seats at alternating periods; Flinders -LRB-1973--1993-RRB- and Chaffey -LRB-1997--current-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Their sole member and leader, Karlene Maywald, representing the Riverland district of Chaffey, accepted a cabinet position in the Rann Labor government, as Minister for the River Murray, Minister for Regional Development, Minister for Small Business, and later Minister for Water Security.][[0.0]]
[This informal ALP-NAT coalition -LRB-the first since 1935-RRB- caused uproar, with Christopher Pyne calling for Maywald's expulsion from the Nationals and Patrick Secker calling for a corruption enquiry in to the appointment -- neither eventuated.][[0.0]]
[As the Liberal Party in South Australia is descended from a historical merger from an earlier Country Party, the SA Nationals are not as dominant in rural areas as their eastern state counterparts.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- SA Greens The SA Greens, founded in 1995 are a sub-division of the left-wing Australian Greens.][[0.0]]
[They are based on green politics and consider themselves a new politics party with strong beliefs in ecology, democracy and social justice amongst other issues.][[0.0]]
[Federally and locally they have seen a continued rise in primary votes, in part due to the demise of the Australian Democrats.][[0.0]]
[The 2007 federal election saw 77.28% of preferences flow to Labor over the Liberal Party in SA.][[0.0]]
[The party's leader is Mark Parnell.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Family First Party The Family First Party, founded immediately before the 2002 state election, has a political ideology based on Christian-influenced conservatism.][[0.0]]
[Although officially a secular party, it has close links to the Pentecostal movement, and in particular the Assemblies of God denomination, and its social policies generally mirror conservative Christian values -LRB-but not necessarily politically conservative values-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The 2007 federal election saw 57.10% of preferences flow to the Liberals over the Labor Party in SA.][[0.0]]
[The party's leader at the time of the election was Andrew Evans.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Australian Democrats The Australian Democrats were originally a centrist party, with most current policies based on social liberalism.][[0.0]]
[Federally, the party was founded in 1977 from three different groups, all of which had split from the Liberal Party at different times: the Liberal Movement, which had split from its parent over electoral reform; the Australia Party, which had rebelled against Australia's involvement in the Vietnam War, and initial leader Don Chipp, who left the Liberal Party of Australia, dissatisfied with the increasing underrepresentation of small-l liberals.][[0.0]]
[At the state level it is descended from the New Liberal Movement -LRB-New LM-RRB- of Robin Millhouse, who held the Democrats' only lower house seats, Mitcham and its successor seat Waite.][[0.0]]
[The Democrats have suffered internal problems and leadership scuffles since 1997.][[0.0]]
[The 2007 federal election saw 65.79% of preferences flow to Labor over the Liberal Party in SA.][[0.0]]
[The party's leader is Sandra Kanck.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Electoral system South Australia is governed according to the principles of the Westminster system, a form of parliamentary government based on the model of the United Kingdom.][[0.0]]
[Legislative power rests with the Parliament of South Australia, which consists of The Sovereign -LRB-represented by the Governor of South Australia-RRB-, the House of Assembly -LRB-lower house-RRB- which forms government, and the Legislative Council -LRB-upper house-RRB- as a house of review.][[0.0]]
[Forty-seven members of the lower house represent single-member electorates and are elected under the preferential Instant-runoff voting -LRB-IRV-RRB- system for fixed four-year terms.][[0.0]]
[The independent State Electoral Office, which conducts elections, is responsible for a mandatory redistricting of boundaries before each election to ensure one vote one value.][[1.0]]
[At each election, voters choose half of the 22 upper house members, each of whom serve eight-year terms in a single statewide electorate.][[0.0]]
[The Legislative Council is elected under the preferential Single Transferable Vote -LRB-STV-RRB- system through a means of Group voting tickets.][[0.0]]
[Voters can choose to vote for a ticket by placing the number '1' in one of the ticket boxes ``above the line'' or can vote for individual candidates by numbering all the boxes ``below the line'' -LRB-54 in the 2006 election-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[In above the line voting, ticket votes are distributed according to the party or group voting ticket registered before the election with the election management body.][[0.0]]
[As most ballot papers are above the line, this form of voting often leads to pre-election trading between parties on how each party will allocate later preferences to other parties and candidates.][[0.0]]
[Voting is compulsory once enrolled in South Australian elections, which results in turnout rates above 90 percent.][[0.0]]
[Informal voting, which occurs when a voting slip is not valid, is at a rate of under five percent.][[0.0]]
[Voting slips are informal when they are not filled out correctly, such examples are not numbering subsequent numbers, not filling out all the candidate boxes with numbers -LRB-except the last candidate-RRB-, or in some other way that is verified by the State Electoral Office as illegible.][[0.0]]
[South Australian elections have some features that are unique to the rest of Australia.][[0.0]]
[As elections have fixed four-year terms, the election date of 18 March 2006 was known well ahead of time.][[0.0]]
[The Electoral Act stipulates that the election is to be held on the third Saturday in March every four years.][[0.0]]
[The election campaign must run for a minimum of 25 days or a maximum of 55 days, therefore the Governor would have needed to issue writs for the election by 21 February 2006 at the latest.][[0.0]]
[On 20 February, Premier Mike Rann invited Governor Marjorie Jackson-Nelson to issue writs for the election.][[0.0]]
[In accordance with electoral regulations, the Electoral Commissioner then advertised key dates for the election of the House of Assembly and half of the Legislative Council -- close of rolls on 27 February 2006 at noon, nominations to be received by 2 March 2006 at noon, polling day on 18 March 2006, and the return of writs on or before 28 April 2006.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Election background In the 2002 election, Labor won 23 seats, the Liberals 20, Nationals 1, and conservative Independents won three.][[0.0]]
[As 24 seats are required to govern, the Liberal Party was expected to retain government with the support of all four independents.][[0.0]]
[However, in a surprise decision, one of the conservative independents, Peter Lewis, decided to support Labor in exchange for holding a constitutional convention, making him speaker of the House of Assembly, and concessions for his electorate including the phasing out of commercial fishing in the River Murray, prioritising the eradication of the branched broomrape weed, changing water rates for irrigation, fast-tracking a feasibility study for a weir and lock at Wellington, and improving rural roads.][[0.0]]
[Lewis resigned as speaker in April 2005 after controversy over allegations of paedophilia he had made about a serving MP.][[0.0]]
[However, by this time, Labor had already gained the support of independents Bob Such and Rory McEwen in 2002, as well as Nationals SA member Karlene Maywald in 2004.][[1.0]]
[Such was given the position of speaker for the remainder of the government's term.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Campaign The Labor campaign was heavily based around Premier Mike Rann with Labor's advertising swapping between the mottos ``Building South Australia'' and, to a greater extent, ``RANN Gets Results''.][[0.0]]
[Commentators also argued that the ``presidential'' style of campaign could be seen in Labor's formal campaign launch at the Norwood Town Hall the Sunday before the election, which had some similarities to the nomination conventions that the major parties hold in the United States.][[0.0]]
[Another facet of the Labor campaign was extensive negative campaigning against Liberal leader Rob Kerin, including an advertisement featuring an excerpt of an interview that Kerin had with FIVEaa presenter Keith Conlon where Conlon asked Kerin why he wanted to be leader of the Liberal Party.][[0.0]]
[Kerin stammered for a few seconds and gave the impression that he was uncertain.][[0.0]]
[The advertisement concluded with the question, ``Does Rob Want The Job?''][[0.0]]
[Conlon complained that the advertisement gave the false impression that he was endorsing Labor, but Labor campaign director David Feeney dismissed his concerns.][[0.0]]
[Other negative advertisements run by Labor revolved around the actions of the previous Liberal government -- one advertisement and leaflet reminded voters that while in power, the previous Liberal government closed 65 schools, closed hospital wards, and privatised the Electricity Trust of South Australia.][[0.0]]
[Considered ``strapped for cash'', the Liberal Party ran a very limited television and radio campaign.][[0.0]]
[Businessman Robert Gerard was forced to resign from his Federal Liberal Party-appointed position on the board of the Reserve Bank of Australia due to the party appointing him to the position despite the known fact that he had outstanding tax avoidance issues being dealt with by the Australian Taxation Office, and had thus subsequently pulled out of his traditional role of bankrolling the state division of the party, leaving the party with ``only enough funds for the most basic campaign''.][[0.0]]
[Kerin indicated people would have to ``wait and see'' if there would be any campaign, even asking trade unions for donations, no matter how small.][[0.0]]
[The advertisements that did run argued that Labor was wasting record tax receipts from the GST.][[0.0]]
[A number of embarrassments for the Liberal Party surrounded their television advertisement -- in an early version released to journalists, Labor was spelt ``Labour'' -LRB-Labor cabinet minister King O'Malley dropped the `u' in 1912 to ``modernise'' it as per American English-RRB- and the advertisement alleged that South Australia's hospital waiting lists were the worst in the nation, which Labor successfully disputed to the Electoral Commissioner.][[0.0]]
[During the election campaign, David Pisoni, the Liberal candidate for Unley, made allegations in his advertising that Labor and the Labor candidate Michael Keenan supported controversial urban infill programmes, which Labor flatly denied.][[0.0]]
[Electoral Commissioner Kay Mousley investigated and ordered that the advertisements be withdrawn and corrections be run at Pisoni's expense.][[0.0]]
[The Labor minority government sought to win a majority in the House of Assembly.][[0.0]]
[Opinion polls indicated that this was likely and ABC elections expert Antony Green said that the ``Labor government looks set to be returned with an increased majority''.][[0.0]]
[Centrebet had Labor at $1.01 AUD and the Liberals at $12.00 AUD for a majority government.][[0.0]]
[Most commentators agreed that the Liberal Party had little chance of winning government, and that Kerin would step down from the leadership after the election, a suspicion confirmed in Kerin's concession speech.][[1.0]]
[Martin Hamilton-Smith was considering mounting a leadership challenge, however, he withdrew on 14 October 2005 -LRB-probably for the sake of the impression of party unity-RRB- and subsequently resigned or was pushed from the opposition frontbench.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Issues One of the most publicised issues prior to the election was the tram extension from Victoria Square to the Adelaide Railway Station which the Liberals, despite having proposed the idea in their previous transport plan, now opposed.][[0.0]]
[Construction began in April 2007 and was operational as of October 2007.][[0.0]]
[The Adelaide Airport expansion suffered fuel delivery related delays that Labor was criticised for.][[0.0]]
[Continued delays by Labor to improve the safety of the Britannia roundabout were focused on by the Norwood Liberal candidate.][[0.0]]
[Land and payroll tax cuts worth $1.5 billion were announced by Labor, the largest in the state's history.][[0.0]]
[The tax cuts coincided with South Australia achieving an economic ``Triple A'' rating under the current Labor government.][[0.0]]
[Business SA chief executive Peter Vaughan ``praised'' Labor's economic management.][[0.0]]
[The construction of two bridges over Port River as part of the Port Expressway project had come under criticism,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- which the Government promised would be open-span to allow passage of tugboats and tall ships, thereby preserving the inner harbour's dwindling port functions.][[0.0]]
[Despite criticism coming from the electorate, the media, federal Labor, and road organisations including the Royal Automobile Association-LSB-citation needed-RSB-, The Advertiser revealed details of ``the biggest project of its kind in South Australia's history'', a $1.5 billion redevelopment on the western bank of the inner harbour.][[0.0]]
[The development will include 2000 new homes on government-owned land and new buildings as high as 12 storeys.][[0.0]]
[This followed the awarding of a $6 billion air warfare destroyer contract to the Australian Submarine Corporation, based in the electorate at Osborne.][[0.0]]
[The future of the River Murray has come under threat due to falling water levels, and in an unprecedented move, Nationals MP Karlene Maywald was given a cabinet position as Minister for the River Murray in 2004.][[1.0]]
[Possible nuclear waste dumps were of concern to many Adelaide residents; Premier Rann successfully lobbied against any federal government proposals.][[0.0]]
[Law and order was another key issue, with Labor promising extra police.][[0.0]]
[Tough drink and drug driving laws had also been introduced which included zero tolerance roadside testing for Tetrahydrocannabinol -LRB-THC-RRB- and Methamphetamine, and later MDMA.][[0.0]]
[Labor introduced speed limit reduction legislation which took effect in March 2003 which saw non-arterial non-main roads and most Adelaide CBD roads reduce from 60�km/h to 50�km/h.][[0.0]]
[The Liberals proposed to increase the speed limit back to 60�km/h for several roads, concentrated mainly around the Adelaide Park Lands.][[0.0]]
[Allegations were made over the condition of the state's health system and the capacity to deal with mental health issues.][[0.0]]
[Labor pledged to buy back Modbury Hospital located in the district of Florey, privatised under the Liberal government to alleviate the effect of the State Bank collapse.][[0.0]]
[The need for homosexual law reform was acknowledged by both major parties; however, there was disquiet within the Labor Party over delays.][[0.0]]
[December 2006 saw the Domestic Partners bill pass which provides greater recognition to same sex relationships on a range of issues such as superannuation.][[0.0]]
[The bill was supported by all parties after much negotiation, but in the end was voted against by both members of Family First, as well as Liberal Terry Stephens.][[0.0]]
[Electoral reform policies received little attention, as has the 2010 referendum proposed by the Rann Government to abolish or reform the Legislative Council.][[0.0]]
[WorkCover underfunded liability increases have also received little attention, despite the fact that the liability has climbed from a disputed $67 to $85 million to $700 million since Labor came in to government in 2002 due to a more generous compensation scheme.][[0.0]]
[Labor have since looked in to reform for the scheme including cutting payments to injured workers.][[0.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Polling Newspoll polling is conducted via random telephone number selection in city and country areas.][[0.0]]
[Roy Morgan polling is conducted face-to-face Australia-wide.][[0.0]]
[Sampling sizes consist of 500--1000 electors, Roy Morgan has a sampling tolerance -LRB-the Margin of error-RRB- of ±3.2 percent for a 40 to 60 percent rating in a sample size of 1000 electors, and ±4.5 for 500 electors.][[0.0]]
[The sampling tolerance rate is lower for high and low percentages.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Results -LSB-edit-RSB- House of Assembly The final results for the House of Assembly seats were 28 Labor, 15 Liberal, three independents and one National.][[0.0]]
[First preference and two party preferred statistics for each district are available through the South Australian House of Assembly electoral districts article.][[0.0]]
[Labor won six of eight key seats, the Liberals one of three key seats.][[0.0]]
[Labor's wins included the previously marginal Liberal seats of Hartley, Light, Morialta, Mawson, Bright and Newland.][[0.0]]
[The Liberals regained Peter Lewis' seat of Hammond.][[0.0]]
[National Karlene Maywald and Independents Bob Such, Rory McEwen and Kris Hanna were all re-elected.][[1.0]]
[Hanna was elected at the 2002 election as a Labor candidate; this counted as a loss for Labor, giving Labor a net gain of five seats.][[1.0]]
[Labor, the Liberals and the Greens ran in all 47 seats, the Democrats ran in all but Giles which resulted in a contested seat vote of three percent, Family First ran in all but Ramsay and Croydon with a contested seat vote of 6.1 percent, with the Nationals running in Chaffey, Flinders, Finniss, and MacKillop, with a subsequent contested seat vote of 24.8 percent.][[1.0]]
[Dignity for Disabled ran in ten seats, No Rodeo in seven seats, and One Nation in six seats.][[0.0]]
[Jack Snelling became speaker of the House of Assembly.][[0.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Post-election pendulum The following pendulum is known as the Mackerras Pendulum, invented by psephologist Malcolm Mackerras.][[0.0]]
[The pendulum works by lining up all of the seats held in the House of Assembly according to the percentage point margin they are held by on a two party preferred basis.][[0.0]]
[This is also known as the swing required for the seat to change hands.][[0.0]]
[Given a uniform swing to the opposition or government parties, the number of seats that change hands can be predicted.][[0.0]]
[Marginal 0--5.99 percent, Fairly Safe 6--10 percent, Safe >10 percent.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Legislative Council In the South Australian Legislative Council, Labor won 4 seats, the Liberals won 3 seats, both No Pokies member Nick Xenophon and his running mate Ann Bressington were elected and Family First and the Greens won a seat each.][[1.0]]
[Almost 40 percent of voters deserted the major parties for Nick Xenophon and the minor parties; this percentage had been steadily increasing over time.][[0.0]]
[Labor received a 3.7 percent swing, electing four councillors as in the previous election.][[0.0]]
[Carmel Zollo, Bob Sneath, Russell Wortley and Ian Hunter were all elected, with 4.39 quotas Bob Sneath was elected president of the Legislative Council.][[0.0]]
[On the other hand, the Liberal vote collapsed with a 14.1 percent swing against the Liberal Party.][[0.0]]
[Having received five councillors in 2002, at this election the Liberal Party had just three councillors elected.][[0.0]]
[Rob Lucas, John Dawkins and Michelle Lensink were elected on 3.12 quotas.][[0.0]]

[No Pokies received 20.5 percent of the vote, yielding 2.46 quotas, which translated into seats for both Xenophon and his running mate Ann Bressington.][[0.0]]
[Having been elected at the 1997 election with 2.9 percent of the vote and other independent candidates at the 2002 election on 1.3 percent of the vote -LRB-Xenophon being a sitting member at that election-RRB-, the No Pokies ticket received a swing of 19.2 percent.][[0.0]]
[The Family First Party's first member, Andrew Evans MLC, was elected in 2002.][[0.0]]
[Family First won 5 percent of the upper house vote with only a small swing of 0.98 percent, with candidate Dennis Hood being elected on preferences.][[0.0]]
[The SA Greens won 4.3 percent of the upper house vote meaning a swing of 1.5 percent, narrowly securing Mark Parnell for the last upper house seat on preferences.][[0.0]]
[This is the first time The Greens have won a seat in South Australia.][[0.0]]
[Having secured second spot on the ticket at this election, Sarah Hanson-Young was successful in gaining the first spot on the ticket at the 2007 federal election, which saw the Greens secure their first federal upper house seat in South Australia.][[0.0]]
[The Australian Democrats fell to just one seat in the Legislative Council held by Sandra Kanck, after Kate Reynolds was defeated in her bid for re-election after being appointed in 2003.][[0.0]]
[The Democrats gained only 1.8 percent of the upper house vote after a 5.5 percent swing against them.][[0.0]]
[Kanck has since announced that she will not recontest her seat at the next election, placing serious clouds over the future of the party in the state.][[0.0]]
[Pauline Hanson's One Nation Party gained 0.8 percent of the upper house vote and won none of the six lower house seats they contested.][[0.0]]
[Their highest vote was 4.1 percent in the district of Hammond, followed by 2.7 percent in Goyder, and the other four hovering around 1 percent.][[0.0]]
[Dignity for Disabled ran for the first time and won 0.6 percent of the upper house vote; they won none of the 10 lower house seats they contested.][[0.0]]
[Their best results were Wright as well as Bright, with 2.4 percent in each -LRB-506 and 492 votes respectively-RRB-.][[0.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Legacy After the election, Rob Kerin vacated the position of opposition leader.][[0.0]]
[The party selected conservative Iain Evans -LRB-son of former politician Stan Evans-RRB- for the role, with moderate Vickie Chapman -LRB-daughter of former politician Ted Chapman-RRB- as deputy leader.][[0.0]]

[Over half of polling respondents were unable to name the leader of the Liberal Party.][[0.0]]
[This contradicted Newspolls quarterly polling indicating the Rann Labor government slipping to a two-party preferred figure of 57 percent down four percent, with a preferred premier rating of 52 percent down 14 percent for Rann and a first-time rating of 21 percent for Martin Hamilton-Smith.][[0.0]]
[Poll results also show Rann's satisfaction rating was below 60 percent for the first time since coming to office at 58 percent, with Hamilton-Smith receiving a 33 percent satisfaction rate.][[0.0]]
[Previously unknown quantity Ann Bressington, elected on the back of Nick Xenophon's No Pokies popularity, has proposed mainly conservative policies such as raising the legal drinking age from 18 to 21, zero tolerance of illicit drugs, mandatory twice-annual drug tests of every South Australian school student over the age of 14 regardless of whether parents give their consent, and making the sale of ``drug-taking equipment'' illegal.][[0.0]]
[However, she remains undecided on voluntary euthanasia, calling it ``a personal struggle''.][[0.0]]
[Setting a precedent, Sandra Kanck's pro-euthanasia speech which contained suicide methods was censored from the internet version of Hansard in August 2006 as a result of an upper house motion, with Labor, Family First, Nick Xenophon and Ann Bressington voting for, and the Liberals and SA Greens member Mark Parnell voting against.][[0.0]]
[Despite this, the speech was published on a non-Australian website.][[0.0]]
[The state's budget was released on 21 September 2006.][[0.0]]
[It included 1,600 public service job axings despite an election pledge of only 400, however none of the redundancies will be forced.][[0.0]]
[It also included increases in some fees and charges such as victims of crime levies and Technical and Further Education -LRB-TAFE-RRB- charges.][[0.0]]
[There were increases in funding for health, schools, police and prisons, and the Department of Public Prosecutions.][[0.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Early years According to his older brother, John, James Bowie was born in Logan County, Kentucky, in the spring of 1796.][[1.0]]
[Historian Raymond Thorp gave his birth date as April 10, but Thorp did not provide any documentation for that date.][[0.0]]
[Bowie was the ninth of ten�children born to Elve Ap-Catesby Jones and Rezin Bowie.][[0.0]]
[His father had been injured while fighting in the American Revolution, and in 1782 married the young woman who had nursed him back to health.][[0.0]]
[The Bowies moved frequently, first settling in Georgia, before moving to Kentucky.][[0.0]]
[At the time of Bowie's birth, his father owned eight slaves, eleven head of cattle, seven horses, and one stud horse.][[0.0]]
[The following year the family acquired 200�acres -LRB-80�ha-RRB- along the Red River.][[0.0]]
[They sold that property in 1800 and relocated to Missouri before moving to Spanish Louisiana in 1802, where they settled on Bushley Bayou in Rapides Parish.][[0.0]]
[The Bowie family moved again in 1809, settling on Bayou Teche in Louisiana before finding a permanent home in Opelousas in 1812.][[0.0]]
[The Bowie children were raised on the frontier and even as small children were expected to help clear the land and plant crops.][[0.0]]
[All of the Bowie children learned to read and write in English, but Jim and his elder brother Rezin could also read, write, and speak Spanish and French fluently.][[0.0]]
[The children learned to survive on the frontier, how to fish and run a farm and plantation.][[0.0]]
[Jim Bowie became proficient with pistol, rifle, and knife, and had a reputation for fearlessness.][[0.0]]
[As a boy one of his Indian friends even taught him to rope alligators.][[0.0]]
[In response to Andrew Jackson's plea for volunteers to fight the British in the War of 1812, Bowie and his brother Rezin enlisted in the Louisiana militia in late 1814.][[0.0]]
[The war ended on December 24 of that year with the signing of the Treaty of Ghent, and the Bowie brothers arrived in New Orleans too late to participate in the fighting.][[0.0]]
[After mustering out of the militia, Bowie settled in Rapides Parish, where he supported himself by sawing planks and lumber and floating it down the bayou for sale.][[0.0]]
[In June 1819, he joined the Long expedition, an effort to liberate Texas from Spanish rule.][[0.0]]
[The group encountered little resistance and, after capturing Nacogdoches, declared Texas an independent republic.][[0.0]]
[The extent of Bowie's participation is unclear, but he returned to Louisiana before the invasion was repelled by Spanish troops.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Land speculator Shortly before their father died in 1818 or 1819, he gave ten�slaves, and horses and cattle to both Jim and his brother Rezin.][[0.0]]
[For the next seven�years the brothers worked together to develop several large estates in Lafourche Parish and Opelousas.][[0.0]]
[Louisiana's population was growing rapidly, and the brothers hoped to take advantage of its rising land prices through speculation.][[0.0]]
[Without the capital required to buy large tracts, they entered into a partnership with a pirate, Jean Lafitte, in 1818 to raise money.][[0.0]]
[By then, the United States had outlawed the importation of slaves, and most southern states allowed anyone who informed on a slave trader to receive half of what the imported slaves would earn at auction as a reward.][[0.0]]
[Bowie made three�trips to Lafitte's compound on Galveston Island.][[0.0]]
[On each occasion he bought smuggled slaves and then took them directly to a customhouse to inform on his own actions.][[0.0]]
[When the customs officers offered the slaves for auction, Bowie purchased them and received back half the price he had paid, as allowed by the state laws.][[0.0]]
[He then could legally transport the slaves and resell them at a greater market value in New Orleans or areas farther up the Mississippi River.][[0.0]]
[Using this scheme the brothers collected $65,000 to be used for their land speculation.][[0.0]]
[In 1825, the two brothers joined with their younger brother Stephen to buy Acadia, a plantation near Alexandria.][[0.0]]
[Within two�years they had established the first steam mill in Louisiana to be used for grinding sugar cane.][[0.0]]
[The plantation became known as a model estate, but, on February 12, 1831, they sold it and 65�slaves for $90,000.][[0.0]]
[With their profits, Bowie and Rezin bought a plantation in Arkansas.][[0.0]]
[Bowie and his brother John were involved in a major court case in the late 1820s over their land speculation.][[0.0]]
[When the United States purchased the Louisiana Territory in 1803, it promised to honor all former land grant claims, and for the next 20�years efforts were made to establish who owned what land.][[0.0]]
[In May 1824, Congress authorized the superior courts of each territory to hear suits from people who claimed they had been overlooked.][[0.0]]
[The Arkansas Superior Court received 126�claims in late 1827 from residents who claimed to have purchased land in former Spanish grants from the Bowie brothers.][[0.0]]
[Although the Superior Court originally confirmed most of those claims, the decisions were reversed in February 1831, after further research showed that the land had never belonged to the Bowies, and that the original land grant documentation had been forged.][[0.0]]
[The U.S. Supreme Court upheld the reversal in 1833.][[0.0]]
[When the disgruntled purchasers considered suing the Bowies, they discovered that the documents in the case had been removed from the court; left without evidence, they declined to pursue a case.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Bowie knife Bowie became internationally famous as a result of a feud with Norris Wright, the sheriff of Rapides Parish.][[0.0]]
[Bowie had supported Wright's opponent in the race for sheriff, and Wright, a bank director, had been instrumental in turning down Bowie's loan application.][[0.0]]
[After a confrontation in Alexandria one afternoon, Wright fired a shot at Bowie.][[0.0]]
[The uninjured Bowie was enraged and tried to kill Wright with his bare hands.][[0.0]]
[Wright's friends intervened and stopped the attack, after which Bowie resolved to carry his hunting knife at all times.][[0.0]]
[The knife he carried had a huge blade that was 9.25�inches -LRB-23.5�cm-RRB- long and 1.5�inches -LRB-3.8�cm-RRB- wide.][[0.0]]
[The following year, on September 19, 1827, Bowie and Wright attended a duel on a sandbar outside of Natchez, Mississippi.][[0.0]]
[Bowie supported duelist Samuel Levi Wells III, while Wright supported Wells's opponent, Dr. Thomas Harris Maddox.][[0.0]]
[The duelists each fired two�shots, and, as neither man had been injured, resolved their duel with a handshake.][[0.0]]
[Other members of the groups, who had various reasons for disliking each other, began fighting.][[0.0]]
[Bowie was shot in the hip; after regaining his feet he drew a knife, described as a butcher knife, and charged his attacker.][[0.0]]
[The attacker hit Bowie over the head with his empty pistol, breaking the pistol and knocking Bowie to the ground.][[0.0]]
[Wright shot at and missed the prone Bowie, who returned fire and possibly, hit Wright.][[0.0]]
[Wright then drew his sword cane and impaled Bowie.][[0.0]]
[When Wright attempted to retrieve his blade by placing his foot on Bowie's chest and tugging, Bowie pulled him down and disemboweled Wright with his large knife.][[1.0]]
[Wright died instantly, and Bowie, with Wright's sword still protruding from his chest, was shot again and stabbed by another member of the group.][[0.0]]
[The doctors who had been present for the duel retrieved the bullets and patched Bowie's other wounds.][[0.0]]
[Newspapers picked up the story, which became known as the Sandbar Fight, and described in detail Bowie's fighting prowess and his unusual knife.][[1.0]]
[Witness accounts agreed that Bowie did not attack first, and the others had focused their attack on Bowie because ``they considered him the most dangerous man among their opposition.''][[0.0]]
[The fight cemented Bowie's reputation across the South as a superb knife-fighter.][[1.0]]
[There is disagreement among scholars as to whether the knife used in this fight was the same kind of knife now known as a Bowie knife.][[0.0]]
[Multiple accounts exist of who designed and built the first Bowie knife.][[0.0]]
[Some claim that Bowie designed it, while others attribute the design to noted knife makers of the time.][[0.0]]
[However, in a letter to The Planter's Advocate, Rezin Bowie claimed to have invented the knife, and many Bowie family members as well as ``most authorities on the Bowie knife tend to believe it was invented by'' Rezin.][[0.0]]
[Rezin Bowie's grandchildren, however, claimed that Rezin merely supervised his blacksmith, who was the creator of the knife.][[0.0]]
[After the Sandbar Fight and subsequent battles in which Bowie successfully used his knife to defend himself, the Bowie knife became very popular.][[0.0]]
[Many craftsmen and manufacturers made their own versions, and major cities of the Southwest had ``Bowie knife schools'', which taught ``the art of cut, thrust, and parry.''][[0.0]]
[His fame, and that of his knife, spread to England, and by the early 1830s many British manufacturers were producing Bowie knives for shipment to the United States.][[0.0]]
[The design of the knife continued to evolve, but today a Bowie knife generally is considered to have a blade 8.25�inches -LRB-21.0�cm-RRB- long and 1.25�inches -LRB-3.2�cm-RRB- wide, with a curved point, a ``sharp false edge cut from both sides'', and a cross-guard to protect the user's hands.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Establishment in Texas After recovering from the wounds he suffered in the Sandbar Fight, in 1828 Bowie decided to move to Texas, at that time a state in the Mexican federation.][[0.0]]
[The 1824 Constitution of Mexico banned religions other than Roman Catholicism and gave preference to Mexican citizens in receiving land.][[0.0]]
[Bowie was baptized into the Roman Catholic faith in San Antonio on April 28, 1828, sponsored by the alcalde -LRB-chief administrator-RRB- of the town, Juan Martin de Veramendi and the wife of the administrator, Josefa Navarro.][[0.0]]
[For the next eighteen�months Bowie travelled through Louisiana and Mississippi.][[0.0]]
[In 1829, he became engaged to Cecilia Wells, who died in Alexandria on September 29, two�weeks before their wedding.][[0.0]]
[On January 1, 1830, Bowie left Louisiana for permanent residency in Texas.][[0.0]]
[He stopped at Nacogdoches, at Jared E. Groce's farm on the Brazos River, and in San Felipe, where Bowie presented a letter of introduction to Stephen F. Austin from Thomas F. McKinney, one of the Old Three Hundred colonists.][[0.0]]
[On February 20, Bowie took an oath of allegiance to Mexico and then proceeded to San Antonio de Bexar.][[0.0]]
[At the time the city, known as Bexar, had a population of 2,500�people, mostly of Mexican descent, and Bowie's fluency in Spanish helped him establish himself in the area.][[0.0]]
[Bowie was elected a commander of the Texas Rangers later that year.][[0.0]]
[Although the Rangers would not be organized officially until 1835, Stephen F. Austin had founded the group by employing thirty�men to keep the peace and protect the colonists from attacks by hostile Indians.][[0.0]]
[Other areas assembled similar volunteer militias, and Bowie commanded a group of the volunteers.][[0.0]]
[Bowie became a Mexican citizen on September 30, 1830, after promising to establish textile mills in the province of Coahuila y Tejas.][[1.0]]
[To fulfill his promise, Bowie entered into partnership with Veramendi to build cotton and wool mills in Saltillo.][[0.0]]
[With his citizenship assured, Bowie now had the right to buy up to 11�leagues of public land.][[0.0]]
[He convinced fourteen or fifteen other citizens to apply for land in order to turn it over to him, giving him 700,000�acres -LRB-280,000�ha-RRB- for speculation.][[0.0]]
[Bowie may have been the first to induce settlers to apply for empresario grants which could then be sold in bulk to speculators like Bowie.][[0.0]]
[The Mexican government passed laws in 1834 and 1835 that stopped much of the land speculation.][[0.0]]
[On April 25, 1831 Bowie married 19-year-old Maria Ursula de Veramendi, the daughter of his business partner, who had become the vice-governor of the province.][[0.0]]
[Several days before the ceremony he signed a dowry contract, promising to pay his new bride 15,000�pesos -LRB-approximately $15,000-RRB- in cash or property within two�years of the marriage.][[0.0]]
[At the time Bowie claimed to have a net worth of $223,000, mostly in land of questionable title.][[0.0]]
[Bowie also lied about his age, claiming to be 30 rather than 35.][[0.0]]
[The couple built a house in San Antonio, on land Veramendi had given them near the San José Mission.][[0.0]]
[After a short time, however, they moved into the Veramendi Palace, living with Ursula's parents, who supplied them with spending money.][[0.0]]
[The couple had two�children, Marie Elve, born March 20, 1832, and James Veramendi, born July 18, 1833.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- San Saba Mine Shortly after his marriage Bowie became fascinated with the story of the ``lost'' Los Almagres Mine, said to be west of San Antonio near the ruin of Santa Cruz de San Sabá Mission.][[0.0]]
[The mine had been operated by local Indians before being seized by the Spanish.][[0.0]]
[After Mexico won independence from Spain, government interest in the mines waned.][[0.0]]
[A number of hostile Indian tribes roamed the area, including Comanche, Lipan Apache, and Karankawa, and without government troops to keep the tribes at bay, mining ceased.][[0.0]]
[It was believed that after the Mexican citizens left the area, the Lipan Apaches took over the mines.][[0.0]]
[After obtaining permission from the Mexican government to mount an expedition into Indian territory to search for the legendary silver mine, Bowie, his brother Rezin, and nine�others set out for San Saba on November 2, 1831.][[0.0]]
[Six�miles -LRB-10�km-RRB- from their goal, the group stopped to negotiate with a large Indian raiding party following them.][[1.0]]
[The attempts at parley failed and Bowie and his group fought for their lives for the next 13�hours.][[0.0]]
[When the Indians finally retreated, Bowie reportedly had lost only one�man, while over 40�Indians had been killed and 30 more wounded.][[0.0]]
[In the meantime, a party of friendly Comanche Indians rode into San Antonio, bringing word of the raiding party, which outnumbered the Bowie expedition by 15--to--1.][[0.0]]
[The citizens of San Antonio believed the members of the Bowie expedition must have perished, and Ursula Bowie began wearing widow's weeds.][[0.0]]
[To the surprise of the town, the surviving members of the group returned to San Antonio on December 6.][[0.0]]
[Bowie's report of the expedition, written in Spanish, was printed in several newspapers, further establishing his reputation.][[0.0]]
[He set out again with a larger force the following month, but returned home empty-handed after two and a half months of searching.][[0.0]]
[Bowie never talked of his exploits despite his increasing fame.][[0.0]]
[Captain William Y. Lacey, who spent eight�months living in the wilderness with Bowie, described him as a humble man who never used profanity or vulgarities.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Texas Revolution -LSB-edit-RSB- Texian rumblings Between 1830 and 1832 the Mexican Congress passed a series of laws that seemed to discriminate against Anglo colonists in the province of Coahuila y Tejas, increasing tension between the Anglo citizenry and Mexican officials.][[0.0]]
[In response to the rumblings, Mexican troops established military posts in several locations within the province, including San Antonio de Béxar.][[1.0]]
[Although much of the military supported the administration of President Anastasio Bustamante, Antonio López de Santa Anna led an insurrection against him in 1832.][[0.0]]
[Anglo colonists in Texas supported Santa Anna and General José Antonio Mexía, who led soldiers into Texas to oust commanders loyal to Bustamante.][[0.0]]
[After hearing that the Mexican army commander in Nacogdoches, José de las Piedras, had demanded that all residents in his area surrender their arms, Bowie cut short a visit to Natchez in July 1832 to return to Texas.][[0.0]]
[On August 2, 1832, he joined a group of other Texians and marched into Nacogdoches to ``present their demands'' to Piedras.][[0.0]]
[Before the group reached the building housing the town officials, they were attacked by a force of 100�Mexican cavalry.][[0.0]]
[The Texians returned fire and, after the cavalry retreated, initiated a siege of the garrison.][[0.0]]
[After a second battle in which Piedras lost 33�men, the Mexican army evacuated during the night.][[0.0]]
[Bowie and eighteen�companions ambushed the fleeing army and, after Piedras fled, marched the soldiers back to Nacogdoches.][[0.0]]
[Bowie later served as a delegate to the Convention of 1833, which formally requested that Texas become its own state within the Mexican federation.][[0.0]]
[Several months later, a cholera epidemic struck Texas.][[0.0]]
[Fearing the disease would reach San Antonio, Bowie sent his pregnant wife and their daughter to the family estate in Monclova in the company of her parents and brother.][[0.0]]
[The cholera epidemic instead struck Monclova, and between September 6 and September 14, Ursula, their children, her brother, and her parents all died of the disease.][[0.0]]
[Bowie, on business in Natchez, heard of his family's deaths in November.][[0.0]]
[From then on, he drank heavily and became ``careless in his dress''.][[0.0]]
[The following year the Mexican government passed new laws allowing land sale in Texas, and Bowie returned to land speculation.][[0.0]]
[He was appointed as a land commissioner, tasked with promoting settlement in the area purchased by John T. Mason.][[0.0]]
[His appointment ended in May 1835, when President Antonio López de Santa Anna abolished the Coahuila y Tejas government and ordered the arrest of all Texians -LRB-including Bowie-RRB- doing business in Monclova.][[0.0]]
[Bowie was forced to flee Monclova and return to the Anglo areas of Texas.][[0.0]]
[The Anglos in Texas began agitating for war against Santa Anna, and Bowie worked with William B. Travis, the leader of the War Party, to gain support.][[0.0]]
[Bowie visited several Indian villages in East Texas in an attempt to convince the reluctant tribes to fight against the Mexican government.][[0.0]]
[Santa Anna responded to the rumblings by ordering large numbers of Mexican troops to Texas.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Battle of Concepción The Texas Revolution began on October 2, 1835 with the Battle of Gonzales.][[1.0]]
[Stephen F. Austin formed an army of 500�men to march on the Mexican forces in San Antonio with the cannon that had precipitated the fight.][[0.0]]
[On October 22, Austin asked Bowie, now a colonel in the volunteer militia, and James W. Fannin to scout the area around the missions of San Francisco de la Espada and San José y San Miguel de Aguayo to find supplies for the volunteer forces.][[0.0]]
[The scouting party left with 92�men, many of them members of the New Orleans Grays who had just arrived in Texas.][[0.0]]
[After discovering a good defensive position near Mission Concepción, the group requested that Austin's army join them.][[0.0]]
[On the foggy morning of October 28, Mexican General Domingo Ugartechea led a force of 300�infantry and cavalry soldiers and 2 small cannons against the Texian forces.][[0.0]]
[Although the Mexican army was able to get within 200�yards -LRB-183�m-RRB-, the Texian defensive position protected them from fire.][[0.0]]
[As the Mexicans stopped to reload their cannon, the Texians climbed a bluff and picked off some of the soldiers.][[0.0]]
[The stalemate ended shortly after Bowie led a charge to seize one of the Mexican cannons, at that time only 80�yards -LRB-73�m-RRB- away.][[0.0]]
[Ugartechea retreated with his troops, ending the Battle of Concepción.][[0.0]]
[One�Texian and ten�Mexican troops had been killed.][[0.0]]
[One of the men under Bowie's command during the battle later praised him ``as a born leader, never needlessly spending a bullet or imperiling a life, who repeatedly admonished ... Keep under cover boys, and reserve your fire; we haven't a man to spare.''][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Grass Fight and commission difficulties An hour after the battle ended, Austin arrived with the rest of the Texian army to begin a siege of San Antonio de Béxar, where General Martín Perfecto de Cós, the overall commander of Mexican forces in Texas, and his troops were garrisoned.][[1.0]]
[Two�days later, Bowie resigned from Austin's army because he did not have an official commission in the army, and he disliked the ``minor tasks of scouting and spying''.][[0.0]]
[On November 3, 1835, Texas declared itself an independent state, and a provisional government was formed with Henry Smith of Brazoria elected provisional governor.][[0.0]]
[Austin requested to be relieved of his command of the army, and Sam Houston was named army chief.][[0.0]]
[Edward Burleson was chosen as temporary commander of the troops in San Antonio.][[0.0]]
[Bowie appeared before the council at some point and spoke for an hour, asking for a commission.][[0.0]]
[The council refused Bowie's request, likely because of lingering animosity over his land dealings.][[0.0]]
[Houston offered Bowie a commission as an officer on his staff, but Bowie rejected the opportunity, explaining that he wanted to be in the midst of the fighting.][[0.0]]
[Instead, Bowie enlisted in the army as a private under Fannin.][[0.0]]
[He distinguished himself again in the Grass Fight on November 26.][[0.0]]
[Cós had sent 100�soldiers to cut grass for the horses.][[0.0]]
[As they returned to San Antonio, Bowie took 60�mounted men to intercept the party, which they believed carried valuable cargo.][[0.0]]
[The Mexican troops quickened their pace in the hopes of reaching the safety of the city, but Bowie and his cavalry chased them.][[0.0]]
[At the end of the fight, the Texians had two�wounded men, but had captured many horses and mules.][[0.0]]
[Shortly after Bowie left San Antonio, Ben Milam led an assault on the city.][[0.0]]
[In the ensuing fighting, the Texians suffered only a few casualties, while the Mexican army lost many troops to death and desertion.][[0.0]]
[Cós surrendered and returned to Mexico, taking with him the last Mexican troops in Texas.][[0.0]]
[Believing the war was over, many of the Texian volunteers left the army and returned to their families.][[0.0]]
[In early January 1836, Bowie went to San Felipe and asked the council to allow him to recruit a regiment.][[1.0]]
[He again was turned down, as he ``was not an officer of the government nor army.''][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Battle at the Alamo After Houston received word that Santa Anna was leading a large force to San Antonio, Bowie offered to lead volunteers to defend the Alamo from the expected attack.][[0.0]]
[He arrived with 30�men on January 19, where they found a force of 104�men with a few weapons and a few cannons, but little supplies and gunpowder.][[0.0]]
[Houston knew that there were not enough men to hold the fort in an attack and had given Bowie orders to remove the artillery and blow up the fortification.][[0.0]]
[Bowie and the Alamo captain, James C. Neill, decided they did not have enough oxen to move the artillery, and they did not want to destroy the fortress.][[0.0]]
[On January 26, one of Bowie's men, James Bonham, organized a rally which passed a resolution in favor of holding the Alamo.][[0.0]]
[Bonham signed the resolution first, with Bowie's signature second.][[0.0]]
[Through Bowie's connections because of his marriage and his fluency in Spanish, the predominantly Mexican population of San Antonio often furnished him with information about the movements of the Mexican army.][[0.0]]
[After learning that Santa Anna had 4,500�troops and was heading for the city, Bowie wrote several letters to the provisional government asking for help in defending the Alamo, especially ``men, money, rifles, and cannon powder''.][[0.0]]
[In another letter, to Governor Smith, he reiterated his view that ``the salvation of Texas depends in great measure on keeping Bexar out of the hands of the enemy.][[0.0]]
[It serves as the frontier picquet guard, and if it were in the possession of Santa Anna, there is no stronghold from which to repel him in his march toward the Sabine.''][[0.0]]
[The letter to Smith ended, ``Colonel Neill and myself have come to the solemn resolution that we will rather die in these ditches than give it up to the enemy.''][[0.0]]
[On February 3, William Travis arrived with an additional 30�troops, and several days later Davy Crockett appeared with twelve�Tennesseans.][[0.0]]
[Neill went on furlough on February 17 to visit his sick family, leaving Travis, a member of the regular army, in command.][[0.0]]
[Bowie was older than Travis with a better reputation and considered himself a colonel, thus outranking Travis, a major.][[0.0]]
[He refused to answer to Travis, who called an election for the men to choose their own commander.][[0.0]]
[They chose Bowie, infuriating Travis.][[0.0]]
[Bowie celebrated his appointment by getting very drunk and causing havoc in San Antonio, releasing all prisoners in the local jails and harassing citizens.][[0.0]]
[Travis was disgusted, but two�days later the men agreed to a joint command; Bowie would command the volunteers, and Travis would command the regular army and the volunteer cavalry.][[0.0]]
[Fearing for the safety of his wife's relatives in San Antonio, Bowie invited her cousins Getrudis Navarro and Juana Navarro Alsbury, as well as Alsbury's 18-month-old son, Alijo, to stay inside the walls of the Alamo.][[0.0]]
[Bowie had been ill, and two�doctors, including the fort surgeon, were unable to diagnose his illness.][[0.0]]
[Travis became the sole commander of the forces when Bowie was confined to bed.][[0.0]]
[Santa Anna and his army reached the outskirts of San Antonio de Bexar several days later and began a siege of the Alamo on February 24.][[0.0]]
[The Mexican army raised a red flag to warn the defenders that no quarter would be given.][[0.0]]
[Travis sent Juan Seguin to recruit reinforcements on February 25, and 32 additional men arrived.][[0.0]]
[Thirty-five�years after the Alamo fell, a reporter identified Louis ``Moses'' Rose as the only man to have ``deserted'' the Texian forces at the Alamo.][[0.0]]
[According to the reporter's version of Rose's account, when Travis realized that the Mexican army would likely prevail, he drew a line in the sand and asked those willing to die for the cause to cross the line.][[0.0]]
[At Bowie's request Crockett and several others carried the cot over the line, leaving Rose alone on the other side.][[0.0]]
[After its publication, several other eyewitnesses confirmed the account, but as Rose was deceased the story can only be authenticated by the word of the reporter, who admitted to embellishing other articles, ``and thus many historians refuse to believe it.''][[0.0]]
[Bowie perished with the rest of the Alamo defenders on March 6, when the Mexicans attacked.][[1.0]]
[Most of the noncombatants in the fort, including Bowie's relatives, survived.][[0.0]]
[Santa Anna ordered the alcalde of San Antonio, Francisco Antonio Ruiz, to confirm the identities of Bowie, Travis, and Crockett.][[0.0]]
[After first ordering that Bowie be buried, as he was too brave a man to be burned like a dog, Santa Anna later had Bowie's body placed with those of the other Texians on the funeral pyre.][[0.0]]
[When Bowie's mother was informed of his death, she calmly stated, ``I'll wager no wounds were found in his back.''][[0.0]]
[Various eyewitnesses to the battle gave conflicting accounts of Bowie's death.][[0.0]]
[A newspaper article claimed that a Mexican soldier saw Bowie carried from his room on his cot, alive, after the conclusion of the battle.][[0.0]]
[The soldier maintained that Bowie verbally castigated a Mexican officer in fluent Spanish, and the officer ordered Bowie's tongue cut out and his still-breathing body thrown onto the funeral pyre.][[0.0]]
[This account has been disputed by numerous other witnesses, and it is thought to have been invented by the reporter.][[0.0]]
[Other witnesses maintained that they saw several Mexican soldiers enter Bowie's room, bayonet him, and carry him, alive, from the room.][[0.0]]
[Various other stories circulated, with some witnesses claiming that Bowie shot himself and others saying he was killed by soldiers while too weak to lift his head.][[0.0]]
[Alcalde Ruiz said that Bowie was found ``dead in his bed.''][[0.0]]
[According to Wallace O Chariton, The ``most popular, and probably the most accurate'' version is that Bowie died on his cot, ``back braced against the wall, and using his pistols and his famous knife.''][[1.0]]
[One�year after the battle, Juan Seguin returned to the Alamo and gathered the remaining ashes from the funeral pyre.][[0.0]]
[He placed these in a coffin inscribed with the names of Bowie, Travis, and Crockett.][[0.0]]
[The ashes were interred at the Cathedral of San Fernando.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Legacy Despite his continual pronouncements of wealth, Bowie's estate was found to be very small.][[0.0]]
[His possessions were auctioned for only $99.50.][[0.0]]
[His larger legacy is his position as ``one of the legendary characters of the American frontier''.][[1.0]]
[Bowie left a ``frustratingly sparse paper trail'' of his life, and, for many, ``where history failed, the legends prevailed.''][[0.0]]
[Although Bowie's name and his knife were well-known during his lifetime, his legend grew after October 1852, when DeBow's Review published an article written by his brother John Jones Bowie, called ``Early Life in the Southwest--The Bowies.''][[0.0]]
[The article focused primarily on the exploits of Jim Bowie.][[0.0]]
[Beginning with that article, ``romanticized stories'' about Bowie began appearing in national press.][[0.0]]
[In many cases, ``these stories were pure melodrama, with Bowie rescuing some naïve planter's son or damsel in distress.''][[0.0]]
[Jim Bowie posthumously was inducted into the Blade Magazine Cutlery Hall of Fame at the 1988 Blade Show in Atlanta, Georgia in recognition for the impact that his eponymous design made upon generations of knife makers and cutlery companies.][[0.0]]
[A number of films have depicted the events of the Battle of the Alamo, and Bowie has appeared as a character in each.][[0.0]]
[From 1956--1958, Bowie was the subject of a television show, The Adventures of Jim Bowie, which was primarily set in 1830s Louisiana, although later episodes ventured into the Mexican province of Texas.][[0.0]]
[The show, which starred Scott Forbes, was based on the 1946 novel Tempered Blade.][[0.0]]
[Bowie also is the namesake of rock star David Bowie, who was born David Robert Jones.][[0.0]]
[Jones changed his name in the 1960s because he feared his name was too similar to Davy Jones, a member of already famous The Monkees.][[0.0]]
[He chose the surname Bowie because he admired James Bowie and the Bowie knife.][[0.0]]
[Both Bowie, Texas and Bowie County, Texas are named in honor of Jim Bowie.][[0.0]]
