[-LSB-edit-RSB- Background -LSB-edit-RSB- Gulag A year before the uprising, the Soviet dictator Joseph Stalin died.][[0.0]]
[His death raised great hopes among the prisoners of amnesty or, failing that, prison reform, and this hope was further emboldened by the subsequent downfall of Stalin's right hand man and state security chief, Lavrenty Beria.][[0.0]]
[Beria, who was the chief of the entire Soviet security and police apparatus and architect of some of the most hated policies relating to the camps, was declared an ``enemy of the people'' and executed by those who succeeded Stalin.][[0.0]]
[Beria's newly besmirched name became a liability to others in both the upper and lower echelons of the Soviet hierarchy, and anybody who was associated with or spoke too much in favour of Beria was similarly at risk of being denounced as a traitor and persecuted.][[0.0]]
[The camp administration were not excluded from this risk, and this fact in turn significantly weakened their position vis à vis the prisoners.][[0.0]]
[Writing about the strikes which were taking place at the time, Solzhenitsyn described this issue: Prisoners all over gulag, for this reason and others, were becoming increasingly bold and impudent in the months preceding the uprising, with hunger strikes, work stoppages, large-scale insubordination, and punitive violence becoming more and more common.][[0.0]]
[In Kengir in particular, camp authorities were rapidly losing all control over their charges, and the communiques periodically sent by commanders up the camp hierarchy, in which they expressed their horror at the frequent incidents of unrest, powerful underground organizations, the growing ``crisis'' afflicting their network of informants, and their desperate attempts to reassert control, attest to this.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Kengir -LSB-edit-RSB- Thieves The uprising's roots can be traced back to a large in-shipment of ``thieves'' -- the accepted slang term for the habitual criminals who were also imprisoned in Gulag along with the political prisoners.][[0.0]]
[Traditionally thieves and politicals had been antagonists, with the thieves exercising virtually unchecked dominance over the politicals, robbing and abusing them at will, and with the politicals remaining too disunited to muster a credible defense.][[0.0]]
[This situation was facilitated by a variably complacent and actively encouraging camp administration, which recognized the potential of thieves as an effective means of suppressing the politicals and preventing them from uniting in a common cause.][[0.0]]
[Indeed, the infusion of roughly 650 thieves into the roughly 8,000-strong body of political prisoners at Kengir at the beginning of May was specifically for this purpose, as the Kengir prisoners had organized strikes before on a smaller scale and were becoming increasingly restless.][[0.0]]
[The camp authorities hoped that these thieves would, as they had in the past, help reverse this trend.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Stoolies It is important to note that, while the Gulag labour camps were founded in the early 1920s, only in the early 1950s were the politicals and thieves finally separated into different camp systems.][[0.0]]
[With the thieves out of the way, the politicals began to unite in ways unprecedented in Gulag.][[0.0]]
[The building blocks of this process were national, religious, and ethnic groups -LRB-Ukrainians, Kazakhs, Chechens, Armenians, Estonians, Muslims, etc.-RRB- who quickly consolidated into strong groups and led the way towards the building of a camp-wide coalition, primarily by launching huge campaigns of murder against camp ``stoolies'' -LRB-or stool pigeons-RRB--- a widely used term for snitches or prisoners who otherwise colluded in any way with the camp administration.][[0.0]]
[Along with the thieves, the stoolies were the primary impediment to the politicals uniting together in the past.][[0.0]]
[The stoolies kept their identities secret, denounced fellow prisoners often, and worked assiduously to root out and finger potentially troublesome prisoners.][[0.0]]
[Because of this, a massive chilling effect was created among prisoners, who feared opening up to or trusting each other.][[0.0]]
[These national and ethnic blocks, though, began the fight against the stoolies, systematically fishing out and killing them with a vigour and efficiency so great that the remaining, unidentified stoolies fled to the camp administration for protection.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Weaponry and organization Of these above mentioned ethnic blocks, the Ukrainians, many of whom were exiled members of the Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists -LRB-by some estimates making up over a half of the camps' population-RRB- were undoubtedly the most important, and they quickly asserted a leadership role amongst the prisoners.][[0.0]]
[Members of this ``Ukrainian Centre'', as it was often called, were the primary proponents of stoolie extermination and later would prove essential to dealing with the newly-arrived thieves.][[0.0]]
[Along with this effective elimination of stoolies, the prisoners began fashioning relatively high quality shivs, which were previously the exclusive territory of thieves.][[0.0]]
[In addition, many incidents took place -LRB-usually including the wanton murder of some well-liked prisoners by guards-RRB- during the previous months that came to fuel resentment and justify extreme action on behalf of the prisoners.][[0.0]]
[Protests and collective refusals to work were increasing in frequency and the prisoners were learning the ropes of how to plan and maintain large-scale disturbances, mainly by creating systems of communication between camp divisions and, more importantly, by establishing command hierarchies.][[0.0]]
[Into this changed climate the thieves were injected and, to the surprise of the camp authorities, they instantly joined forces with the politicals, meeting secretly on the first night with the Ukrainian Centre and establishing a pact.][[0.0]]
[This was due both to the fact that they recognized their odds against the almost 8,000 strong body of well-armed and united political prisoners, and because thieves across the whole Gulag caught wind of the politicals' campaign against the stoolies and began to admire and respect them.][[1.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- The camp compound The entire Kengir camp complex formed a large rectangle, divided up width-wise into four distinct areas: the women's camp, the ``service yard'', where all the workshops and storerooms were located, and two camps for men, each with its own jailhouse for punishing prisoners or hiding stoolies.][[1.0]]
[The women's camp was blocked off both from access and sight to the mens' camp.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Seizing of the camp The formative stage of the uprising began on the evening of 16 May, a Sunday and thus a day off for all the prisoners.][[0.0]]
[The thieves contrived to break into the service yard, where all the food was stored, and from there break into the women's camp, which was easier to do from that location.][[0.0]]
[This they initially did, but they were shortly chased off by guards.][[0.0]]
[At nightfall, though, the thieves regrouped, shot out all of the lights in range with their slingshots, and broke through the barrier between the men's camp and service yard with an improvised battering ram.][[0.0]]
[It was at this point the Kengir uprising proper started when the guards opened fire on the thieves, killing 13 and wounding 43.][[0.0]]
[The remaining thieves retreated and an uneasy peace followed.][[0.0]]
[During the night, though, thieves, now joined by the politicals, started breaking up their bunks and cells, trying to add to their cache of shivs and arm those without weapons, while the camp authorities posted machine gunners at the hole in the wall.][[0.0]]
[After a tense standoff, the camp authorities, in a surprise gesture, ordered the withdrawal of all guards from the compound.][[0.0]]
[Despite appearances, this was a strictly tactical move on the part of the authorities.][[0.0]]
[The following day they feigned acquiescence to the prisoners demands and, while the prisoners then agreeably went off to work outside the camp, the guards busied themselves patching up the broken-down wall.][[1.0]]
[Nevertheless this was a strategic error on their part because it exposed the bad faith of the guards and eliminated all remaining trust the prisoners had in their word.][[0.0]]
[More importantly, though, the prisoners had, for one whole day, tasted total freedom -LRB-within the confines of the camp compound-RRB-, mingling freely with the female prisoners, eating their fill, and fraternizing as they pleased, and this put in them a desire for freedom that would not be so easily quenched.][[0.0]]
[This time also saw the first propaganda offensive by the camp authorities -LRB-they re-enacted, in full prisoner costume, the alleged rape of the women prisoners and photographed themselves, releasing the photographs and declaring that the revolt was in fact a cover for debauchery and hedonism-RRB-, setting the tone for the many that would follow.][[1.0]]
[After realizing these sleights of hand on the part of the camp authorities, the prisoners quickly and forcefully reasserted themselves, running amok and sending the guards fleeing from the camp again.][[0.0]]
[They then proceeded to re-destroy the wall that had just been repaired and release the prisoners from the camp's solitary confinement cells.][[0.0]]
[The camp had been seized and would remain in the control of the prisoners for the next 40 days.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- The new camp society -LSB-edit-RSB- Culture With the entire camp at their disposal, and with feelings of fellowship and good-will in abundance, prisoners took part in a hurried romp through the joys of normal, human, everyday life that had been denied to them for so long.][[0.0]]
[As Solzhenitsyn and others retold, men and women from different camp divisions who had romantically conversed in secret for years, but had never seen each other, finally met.][[0.0]]
[Imprisoned priests presided over a number of improvised weddings.][[0.0]]
[Prisoners retrieved what remained of their civilian clothing from the storeroom -LRB-the guards regularly stole and sold prisoners' items-RRB-, and soon prisoners were seen adorned with fur coats and assorted colourful clothing, in addition to the religious wear that had been banned.][[0.0]]
[Business, as well, resumed as best it could, with one Polish aristocrat opening up a ``café'' serving ersatz ``coffee'', which proved to be quite popular with the prisoners.][[0.0]]
[In short order, a number of organized recreational activities also sprung up.][[0.0]]
[Because of the large number of political prisoners in Gulag, almost every camp boasted an enviable selection of highly-skilled and trained engineers, scientists, intellectuals, and artists, and advanced lectures were delivered for the enjoyment of the educated classes and philistines alike.][[0.0]]
[Art flourished as well, with poetry recitals and even hastily-prepared plays being performed.][[0.0]]
[Hymns, penned by the Ukrainians, were performed en masse.][[0.0]]
[One hymn in particular, with its simultaneously mournful and celebratory tone and its stirring demand for freedom, stands as representative of the prevailing themes in the works produced during the uprising: In addition to the renewed presence of religious regalia, religious practices were also given new life.][[0.0]]
[Notably, one of the religious sects massed at the original hole broken into the dividing wall on the first night of the uprising, claiming that their prophet had predicted its destruction and the freedom that followed.][[0.0]]
[They, according to former prisoners, then sat on mattresses for several days by the hole, praying and waiting to be taken to heaven.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Government Soon after the camp was taken over, the prisoners congregated into the mess hall and decided to elect a new leader, and a former Red Army Colonel, Kapiton Kuznetsov, was chosen.][[0.0]]
[A major reason for this choice was that the Ukrainian Center insisted on having Russian leadership of the rebellion and, indeed, on having the entire government be as multiethnic and multinational as possible.][[0.0]]
[This was done mainly to avoid the appearance of the rebellion being anti-Russian in character, but also as an enlightened attempt to create a harmonious camp society and government.][[0.0]]
[Kuznetsov and his administration were originally delegated to conduct negotiations with the camp authorities on behalf of the prisoners, but as the prisoners' control of the camp lasted beyond expectation and as demand for law, order, and efficiency increased, the jurisdiction of this government increased in turn.][[0.0]]
[Therefore, various government departments were quickly created:  -LSB-edit-RSB- Propaganda The first expansion of the government's authority came as a natural extension of its role as mouthpiece of the prisoners: propaganda.][[0.0]]
[A theme was carefully set by Kuznetsov and taken over by his Lithuanian deputy, Knopkus.][[0.0]]
[The theme crucially undercut the main argument that would have been used by the camp authorities to crush the rebellion, which was that the rebellion was anti-Soviet in nature.][[0.0]]
[Even with Stalin dead, this represented a red-line that was not to be crossed.][[0.0]]
[Instead, Knopkus schemed to portray the guards as ``Beria-ites'' -LRB-a deadly charge at the time-RRB- and the rebellion as a patriotic, vanguard movement against them.][[0.0]]
[Soon placards were raised declaring such sentiments as ``Long live the Soviet constitution!''][[0.0]]
[and ``Down with murdering Beria-ites!''][[0.0]]
[As the new state of affairs continued, the Propaganda department's activities grew.][[0.0]]
[At first they were all largely defensive in intent -- literally just responding to allegations hurled at them across the fence.][[0.0]]
[The guards broadcast propaganda over loudspeakers into the camp, urging surrender and decrying the loss of days of valuable prison labor and the alleged detrimental effect it was having on the Soviet economy.][[0.0]]
[In response, the prisoners, using a modified loudspeaker, broadcast back a whole set of mock radio programmes, complete with comedy programs and skits, written by the Agitation and Propaganda department and announced by a charismatic female prisoner.][[0.0]]
[One of the guard's stenographers recorded some of the broadcasts, and these records made their way into the Soviet archives.][[0.0]]
[An excerpt of one broadcast: Later, with the help of the Technical Department, their schemes became increasingly ambitious.][[0.0]]
[The prisoners, realizing the precariousness of their situation, endeavored to publicize their rebellion and demands to the village adjacent to the camp, hoping to incite its citizens to supportive action.][[0.0]]
[To do this, they first employed specially rigged, hot air balloons with slogans written on them -LRB-these were shot down by the guards-RRB- and, later, kites manufactured by the Chechens, who turned out to be specialists in the field.][[0.0]]
[The kites were successful for a time.][[0.0]]
[In favorable winds, they dropped packets of leaflets to the settlements below, but the authorities soon sent up their own kites to tangle the prisoner's kite's lines.][[0.0]]
[At last, seizing on a solid, successful strategy, the prisoners fixed leaflets to carrier pigeons, releasing dozens into the blue.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Defense Along with propaganda, defense came to the fore of the new government's list of priorities.][[0.0]]
[Before the exiled camp authorities cut off the camp's electricity, the smiths and lathe-operators in the camp fashioned all manner of weaponry in the service yard's workshops -- long pikes from prison bars, sabers, staves, and clubs amongst them.][[0.0]]
[In addition to this, the prisoners ground glass into dust and placed buckets of this dust throughout the camp, hoping to blind oncoming troops with it.][[0.0]]
[Barricades were established at key points, and responsibility for manning them was divided up amongst the camp barracks -LRB-renamed ``detachments'' by the Defense department-RRB-, with set shifts and procedures.][[0.0]]
[The Technical Department contributed to this effort as well, namely by creating improvised explosive devices and incendiary bombs, both of which, according to Solzhenitsyn, saw use during the actual invasion in June, the latter bringing down a guard tower.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Technical Department In addition to the above mentioned innovations, the Technical Department dealt with any number of problems that arose.][[0.0]]
[When the exiled camp authorities cut off the camp's electrical supply, the electricians among the prisoners siphoned electricity from the wires passing overhead just outside the perimeter fence.][[0.0]]
[This too was terminated by the authorities after a few days, and thereafter the prisoners used a modified motor as a generator and even improvised a running tap ``hydroelectric station'' to supply power to the government headquarters and medical barracks.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Negotiations Negotiations between the authorities and rebels began almost immediately, as was becoming the custom with prisoner disturbances, but were from the beginning wrought with difficulty.][[0.0]]
[The camp authorities again immediately acquiesced to virtually all of the prisoners demands, but this time, with the past deceit still fresh in their minds, the prisoners did not accept this solution as sufficient and demanded a written agreement.][[1.0]]
[A draft was written up by the authorities, passed around the camp and widely panned.][[0.0]]
[From here negotiations cooled until higher ranking officers came in from other cities.][[0.0]]
[Solzhenitsyn explained: To these generals and others were presented the same set of demands: punishment of the soldiers responsible for the murder of various prisoners and beating of women prisoners; that prisoners who had been transferred to other camps as punishment for participating in a strike be brought back; that prisoners no longer had to wear degrading number patches or be locked into their dormitories at night; that the walls separating camp divisions -LRB-namely between the men's and women's camps-RRB- not be rebuilt; that an eight-hour work day be instituted; that limits be taken off the number of letters they could send and receive; that certain hated camp guards and officials be removed from Kengir; and that, most importantly, their cases be reviewed.][[0.0]]
[None of these demands were unconstitutional.][[0.0]]
[The original regulation specifically provided for all that the prisoners were asking, and that a simple reinstatement of those rights was all that was being requested.][[0.0]]
[The generals, now with Sergei Yegorov, deputy chief of the MVD, and Ivan Dolgikh, division commander of Gulag, among them, once again agreed to the prisoners demands as whole, but, still failing to match a written contract to their words, they were once again rejected by the prisoners.][[0.0]]
[The discussions then further broke down into threats and counter-threats.][[0.0]]
[The prisoners, out of a lack of trust in their current negotiating partners, demanded that a member of the Central Committee be sent and this was flatly refused.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Sowing discord Prior to the raid, attempts were made by the camp authorities to sow civil violence within the camp, both so that the prisoners would slaughter each other and make the job easier for the invading troops, and to provide an ostensible justification for the massive armed intervention to begin with.][[0.0]]
[Direct requests were made to high ranking prisoners that they ``provoke racial bloodbath'' and, in exchange, get to keep their lives -LRB-any prisoner that publicly occupied a high post in the camp's provisional government was sure to be tried and executed when captured, as the prisoners themselves knew-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Banking on the still-running current of paranoia and distrust of Jews in Russia, the authorities even attempted to spread rumours in the camp that a pogrom was imminent as a way of dividing prisoners against each other.][[0.0]]
[While these efforts largely failed, another objective of the authorities -- to draw out orthodox Communists and Soviet loyalists -- was successful and a number of them fled the camp in the days before the raid, including a high ranking member of the prisoner's government who would later reappear as a voice urging surrender on the guards' propaganda loudspeakers.][[0.0]]
[Nevertheless, this outflow was shortly halted by Internal Security, which captured those speaking favorably of the authorities or of surrender and locked them in the camp's jail.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Suppression -LSB-edit-RSB- Prelude In the days prior to the raid, small, token incursions were made.][[0.0]]
[First, this was done to test the preparedness and defensive capabilities of the prisoners -- alarms were sounded and prisoners quickly assumed battle positions -- but later it was done for the sake of running film cameras.][[0.0]]
[This footage later became important to the authorities in their effort to identify and punish all those who participated directly in the uprising, as well as secure their justification for the raid.][[0.0]]
[At this time, the morale of the prisoners was also dropping.][[0.0]]
[Many came to have a dawning sense of the futility of their own struggle, and this attitude proved infectious.][[0.0]]
[The leader of the prisoners, Kuznetsov, even betrayed his wariness in a speech, retold by Solzhenitsyn: Making matters worse for the prisoners, the day before the raid it was announced on the guards' loudspeakers that their demand to meet with a member of the Central Committee was to be granted.][[0.0]]
[This had the effect of lowering the prisoners guard and creating a less hostile and more favourable disposition towards the camp authorities, who were planning to violently crush the prisoners all the while.][[0.0]]
[In addition, Solzhenitsyn recalls that the prisoners heard for days before the raid what they thought were the sounds of tractors running on the distance, out of sight.][[0.0]]
[These turned out to be tanks, a weapon the prisoners did not anticipate being used against them.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- The raid In the dawn of 25 June, flares were shot up into the sky and the raid began.][[0.0]]
[Snipers quickly picked off the sentries on the rooftops before they could sound the alarm, and the tanks rolled through the perimeter fence.][[0.0]]
[Five tanks, 90 dogs, and 1,700 troops in full battle-gear stormed the camp complex.][[0.0]]
[What followed was panic and chaos.][[0.0]]
[While some `detachments' vigorously fought back, launching numerous counter-attacks despite heavy losses and throwing improvised sulfur bombs at the tanks, other prisoners hid or committed suicide.][[0.0]]
[The tanks, T-34s, alternately ran over prisoners or brought down barrack walls where prisoners were hiding, and used blank rounds of ammunition to strike terror and confusion into the prisoners.][[0.0]]
[The hundreds of helmeted Red Army soldiers that flooded the camp were using live ammunition, though, and with these many prisoners were killed.][[0.0]]
[Some tanks carried in barbed wire-laden trestles, and these were immediately set down as a means of quickly dividing up the camp and hindering the prisoners' freedom of movement.][[0.0]]
[The leaders of the uprising were specifically targeted by designated squads of soldiers and they were taken into custody alive, many of whom were later tried and executed.][[0.0]]
[After ninety minutes of violence, the remaining live prisoners, most of whom were in hiding, were ordered to come out on the promise that they wouldn't be shot, which was, to everyone's surprise, a promise kept.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Aftermath According to a number of survivors of the camp, five to seven hundred prisoners were either killed or wounded in the uprising, with an additional six of the highest ranking prisoners later being executed, Knopkus among them.][[1.0]]
[Figures found in the Soviet archives, though, suggest that only 37 were killed, not including those who later died of their wounds or were executed, and with 106 prisoners and 40 soldiers wounded.][[0.0]]
[Kuznetsov, however, had his death sentence commuted to 25 years and found himself released and fully rehabilitated after 5 years of imprisonment.][[0.0]]
[Theories abound as to why, but most attribute this to the full, detailed 43-page confession he wrote in which he denounced scores of fellow prisoners.][[0.0]]
[This confession also proved to be an invaluable source for many of the studies conducted on the Kengir uprising, although some question its veracity.][[0.0]]
[In keeping with the prevailing theme of their story, the camp administration is said to have planted weapons on the corpses of those who didn't already have them for the sake of the photographers, who were brought in expressly for this purpose.][[0.0]]
[On the day following the raid, almost a thousand prisoners were shipped off to different camps and the remaining prisoners were occupied with the task of, once again, rebuilding the destroyed wall, sealing themselves back into a life of imprisonment.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Significance Among the strikes and rebellions that were taking place in Gulags across the Soviet Union in this period, the uprising at Kengir was perhaps the most significant.][[1.0]]
[While Stalin's death, Beria's fall, and Khrushchev's rise bore much promise for the prisoners, who had long expected general amnesties and rehabilitation to follow these events, the role of the Kengir uprising in hastening this process cannot be overlooked.][[0.0]]
[The uprising further demonstrated to the authorities that Stalinism was not a sustainable policy option and that mass injustices such as those taking place in Gulag would not stand in perpetuity without significant cost.][[1.0]]
[In a shift that foreboded poorly for the Soviet regime, many of the prisoners took part knowing full well that they were doing so at the cost of their lives, and prisoners in other camps, namely in the nearby Rudnik camp, had joined with the Kengir prisoners in solidarity, launching their own short-lived strikes.][[0.0]]
[The significance of the temporary freedom enjoyed by those prisoners was not lost on many.][[0.0]]
[In a 1978 review of Solzhenitsyn's book, Hilton Kramer of The New York Times declared that the uprising ``restored a measure of humane civilization to the prisoners before the state was able to assert its implacable power again.''][[0.0]]
[At a 2004 reunion of Kengir prisoners, a survivor of the camp mentioned that, despite the brutality and loss of life that came with the uprising's suppression, the 40 days engendered the prisoners with ``a great feeling of freeing one's spirit'', and another prisoner recalled that ``I had not before then, and have not since, felt such a sense of freedom as I did then'' -- both sentiments echoed often by Solzhenitsyn.][[1.0]]
[Indeed, Solzhenitsyn would later dedicate a screenplay he had written to the bravery of the Kengir rebels, entitled Tanks Know the Truth -LRB-Знают истину танки-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Most remarkably, as George Mason University historian Steven A. Barnes noted in a 2005 edition of Slavic Review, the prisoners' campaign was belied with a certain pragmatism, and their propaganda with a level of skill, that was all but unprecedented.][[0.0]]
[As noted, instead of making explicit their hostility to the Soviet regime and handing an excuse to the authorities to invade, they ostensibly expressed approval of the state while, meekly, asking for the restoration of the rights and privileges afforded to them in the Soviet constitution.][[0.0]]
[This message was itself spread not only to the camp authorities and any of the MVD-brass that would visit the camp for negotiations, but, crucially, to the civilian population surrounding the camp.][[0.0]]
[Before the authorities came up with the idea of using their own rival kites to tangle and bring down the prisoner's kites with, they kept a large retinue of guards and warders, on horseback and motorcycle, waiting for the leaflets to be dropped from the kites so that they could, literally, chase down and retrieve them before they could be read by members of the public.][[0.0]]
[The tact, cohesion, and ingenuity displayed in the uprising was a troubling sign to the authorities of what was perhaps to come.][[0.0]]
[Nevertheless, any potential effect the uprising could have had was strictly circumscribed by the nature of the Soviet regime, which was quick to use massive force to quell even the most humble of threats.][[0.0]]
[In the same Times review, Kramer issued an important caveat to his previous claim:][[0.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Description Gorgosaurus was smaller than Tyrannosaurus or Tarbosaurus, closer in size to Albertosaurus and Daspletosaurus.][[0.0]]
[Adults reached 8 or 9�meters -LRB-26 to 30�ft-RRB- from snout to tail.][[0.0]]
[Paleontologists have estimated full-grown adults to weigh more than 2.4�tonnes -LRB-2.7�short tons-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The largest known skull measures 99�centimeters -LRB-39�in-RRB- long, just slightly smaller than that of Daspletosaurus.][[0.0]]
[As in other tyrannosaurids, the skull was large compared to its body size, although chambers within the skull bones and large openings -LRB-fenestrae-RRB- between bones reduced its weight.][[0.0]]
[Albertosaurus and Gorgosaurus share proportionally longer and lower skulls than Daspletosaurus and other tyrannosaurids.][[0.0]]
[The end of the snout was blunt, and the nasal and parietal bones were fused along the midline of the skull, as in all other members of the family.][[0.0]]
[The eye socket was circular rather than oval or keyhole-shaped as in other tyrannosaurid genera.][[0.0]]
[A tall crest rose from the lacrimal bone in front of each eye, similar to Albertosaurus and Daspletosaurus.][[0.0]]
[Differences in the shape of bones surrounding the brain set Gorgosaurus apart from Albertosaurus.][[0.0]]
[Gorgosaurus teeth were typical of all known tyrannosaurids.][[1.0]]
[The eight premaxillary teeth at the front of the snout were smaller than the rest, closely packed and D-shaped in cross section.][[0.0]]
[In Gorgosaurus, the first tooth in the maxilla was also shaped like the premaxillary teeth.][[0.0]]
[The rest of the teeth were oval in cross section, rather than blade-like as in most other theropods.][[0.0]]
[Along with the eight premaxillary teeth, Gorgosaurus had 26 to 30�maxillary teeth and 30 to 34�teeth in the dentary bones of the lower jaw.][[0.0]]
[This number of teeth is similar to Albertosaurus and Daspletosaurus but is fewer than those of Tarbosaurus or Tyrannosaurus.][[0.0]]
[Gorgosaurus shared its general body plan with all other tyrannosaurids.][[0.0]]
[Its massive head was perched on the end of an S-shaped neck.][[0.0]]
[In contrast to its large head, its forelimbs were very small.][[0.0]]
[The forelimbs had only two digits, although a third metacarpal is known in some specimens, the vestigial remains of the third digit seen in other theropods.][[0.0]]
[Gorgosaurus had four digits on each hindlimb, including a small first toe -LRB-hallux-RRB- which did not contact the ground.][[0.0]]
[Tyrannosaurid hindlimbs were long relative to overall body size compared with other theropods.][[0.0]]
[The largest known Gorgosaurus femur measured 105�centimeters -LRB-41�in-RRB- long.][[0.0]]
[In several smaller specimens of Gorgosaurus, the tibia was longer than the femur, a proportion typical of fast-running animals.][[0.0]]
[The two bones were of equal length in the largest specimens.][[0.0]]
[The long, heavy tail served as a counterweight to the head and torso and placed the center of gravity over the hips.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Classification and systematics Gorgosaurus is classified in the theropod subfamily Albertosaurinae within the family Tyrannosauridae.][[0.0]]
[It is most closely related to the slightly younger Albertosaurus.][[1.0]]
[These are the only two definite albertosaurine genera that have been described, although other undescribed species may exist.][[0.0]]
[Appalachiosaurus was described as a basal tyrannosauroid just outside Tyrannosauridae, although American paleontologist Thomas Holtz published a phylogenetic analysis in 2004 which indicated it was an albertosaurine.][[0.0]]
[More recent, unpublished work by Holtz agrees with the original assessment.][[0.0]]
[All other tyrannosaurid genera, including Daspletosaurus, Tarbosaurus and Tyrannosaurus, are classified in the subfamily Tyrannosaurinae.][[0.0]]
[Compared to the tyrannosaurines, albertosaurines had slender builds, with proportionately smaller, lower skulls and longer bones of the lower leg -LRB-tibia-RRB- and feet -LRB-metatarsals and phalanges-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The close similarities between Gorgosaurus libratus and Albertosaurus sarcophagus have led many experts to combine them into one genus over the years.][[1.0]]
[Albertosaurus was named first, so by convention it is given priority over the name Gorgosaurus, which is sometimes considered its junior synonym.][[0.0]]
[William Diller Matthew and Barnum Brown doubted the distinction of the two genera as early as 1922.][[0.0]]
[Gorgosaurus libratus was formally reassigned to Albertosaurus -LRB-as Albertosaurus libratus-RRB- by Dale Russell in 1970, and many subsequent authors followed his lead.][[0.0]]
[Combining the two greatly expands the geographical and chronological range of the genus Albertosaurus.][[0.0]]
[Other experts maintain the two genera as separate.][[0.0]]
[Canadian paleontologist Phil Currie claims there are as many anatomical differences between Albertosaurus and Gorgosaurus as there are between Daspletosaurus and Tyrannosaurus, which are almost always kept separate.][[1.0]]
[He also notes that undescribed tyrannosaurids discovered in Alaska, New Mexico and elsewhere in North America may help clarify the situation.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Discovery and naming Gorgosaurus libratus was first described by Lawrence Lambe in 1914.][[0.0]]
[Its name is derived from the Greek γοργος/gorgos -LRB-``fierce'' or ``terrible''-RRB- and σαυρος/saurus -LRB-``lizard''-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The type species is G. libratus; the specific epithet ``balanced'' is the past participle of the Latin verb librare, meaning ``to balance''.][[1.0]]
[The holotype of Gorgosaurus libratus -LRB-NMC 2120-RRB- is a nearly complete skeleton associated with a skull, discovered in 1913 by Charles M. Sternberg.][[0.0]]
[This specimen was the first tyrannosaurid found with a complete hand.][[0.0]]
[It was found in the Dinosaur Park Formation of Alberta and is housed in the Canadian Museum of Nature in Ottawa.][[1.0]]
[Prospectors from the American Museum of Natural History in New York City were active along the Red Deer River in Alberta at the same time, collecting hundreds of spectacular dinosaur specimens, including four complete G. libratus skulls, three of which were associated with skeletons.][[0.0]]
[Matthew and Brown described four of these specimens in 1923.][[0.0]]
[Matthew and Brown also described a fifth skeleton -LRB-AMNH 5664-RRB-, which Charles H. Sternberg had collected in 1917 and sold to their museum.][[0.0]]
[It was smaller than other Gorgosaurus specimens, with a lower, lighter skull and more elongate limb proportions.][[0.0]]
[Many sutures between bones were unfused in this specimen as well.][[0.0]]
[Matthew and Brown noted that these features were characteristic of juvenile tyrannosaurids, but still described it as the holotype of a new species, G. sternbergi.][[0.0]]
[Today's paleontologists regard this specimen as a juvenile G. libratus.][[0.0]]
[Dozens of other specimens have been excavated from the Dinosaur Park Formation and are housed in museums across the United States and Canada.][[0.0]]
[G. libratus is the best-represented tyrannosaurid in the fossil record, known from a virtually complete growth series.][[1.0]]
[In 1856, Joseph Leidy described two tyrannosaurid premaxillary teeth from Montana.][[0.0]]
[Although there was no indication of what the animal looked like, the teeth were large and robust, and Leidy gave them the name Deinodon.][[0.0]]
[Matthew and Brown commented in 1922 that these teeth were indistinguishable from those of Gorgosaurus, but in the absence of skeletal remains of Deinodon, opted not to synonymize the two genera.][[0.0]]
[Although Deinodon teeth are very similar to those of Gorgosaurus, tyrannosaurid teeth are extremely uniform, so it cannot be said for certain which animal they belonged to.][[0.0]]
[Deinodon is regarded as a nomen dubium today.][[0.0]]
[Several tyrannosaurid skeletons from the Judith River Formation of Montana probably belong to Gorgosaurus, although it remains uncertain whether they belong to G. libratus or a new species.][[0.0]]
[One specimen from Montana -LRB-TCMI 2001.89.1-RRB-, housed in the Children's Museum of Indianapolis, shows evidence of severe pathologies, including healed leg, rib, and vertebral fractures, osteomyelitis -LRB-infection-RRB- at the tip of the lower jaw resulting in permanent tooth loss, and possibly a brain tumor.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Misassigned species Several species were incorrectly assigned to Gorgosaurus in the twentieth century.][[0.0]]
[A complete skull of a small tyrannosaurid -LRB-CMNH 7541-RRB-, found in the younger, late Maastrichtian-age Hell Creek Formation of Montana, was named Gorgosaurus lancensis by Charles Whitney Gilmore in 1946.][[0.0]]
[This specimen was renamed Nanotyrannus by Bob Bakker and colleagues in 1988.][[0.0]]
[Today, most paleontologists recognize Nanotyrannus as a juvenile Tyrannosaurus rex.][[0.0]]
[Similarly, Evgeny Maleev created the names Gorgosaurus lancinator and Gorgosaurus novojilovi for two small tyrannosaurid specimens -LRB-PIN 553-1 and PIN 552-2-RRB- from the Nemegt Formation of Mongolia in 1955.][[0.0]]
[Ken Carpenter renamed the smaller specimen Maleevosaurus novojilovi in 1992, but both are now considered juveniles of Tarbosaurus bataar.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Paleobiology -LSB-edit-RSB- Coexistence with Daspletosaurus In the Dinosaur Park Formation, Gorgosaurus lived alongside a rarer species of the tyrannosaurine Daspletosaurus.][[1.0]]
[This is one of the few examples of two tyrannosaur genera coexisting.][[0.0]]
[Similar-sized predators in modern predator guilds are separated into different ecological niches by anatomical, behavioral or geographical differences that limit competition.][[0.0]]
[Niche differentiation between the Dinosaur Park tyrannosaurids is not well-understood.][[1.0]]
[In 1970, Dale Russell hypothesized the more common Gorgosaurus actively hunted fleet-footed hadrosaurs, while the rarer and more troublesome ceratopsians and ankylosaurians -LRB-horned and heavily armoured dinosaurs-RRB- were left to the more heavy-built Daspletosaurus.][[1.0]]
[However, a specimen of Daspletosaurus -LRB-OTM 200-RRB- from the contemporaneous Two Medicine Formation of Montana preserves the digested remains of a juvenile hadrosaur in its gut region.][[0.0]]
[Unlike some other groups of dinosaurs, neither genus was more common at higher or lower elevations than the other.][[0.0]]
[However, Gorgosaurus appears more common in northern formations like the Dinosaur Park, with species of Daspletosaurus more abundant to the south.][[0.0]]
[The same pattern is seen in other groups of dinosaurs.][[0.0]]
[Chasmosaurine ceratopsians and hadrosaurine hadrosaurs are also more common in the Two Medicine Formation of Montana and in southwestern North America during the Campanian, while centrosaurine and lambeosaurines dominate in northern latitudes.][[0.0]]
[Holtz has suggested this pattern indicates shared ecological preferences between tyrannosaurines, chasmosaurines and hadrosaurines.][[0.0]]
[At the end of the later Maastrichtian stage, tyrannosaurines like Tyrannosaurus rex, hadrosaurines like Edmontosaurus and chasmosaurines like Triceratops were widespread throughout western North America, while albertosaurines and centrosaurines went extinct, and lambeosaurines were rare.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Life history Gregory Erickson and colleagues have studied the growth and life history of tyrannosaurids using bone histology, which can determine the age of a specimen when it died.][[1.0]]
[A growth curve can be developed when the ages of various individuals are plotted against their sizes on a graph.][[0.0]]
[Tyrannosaurids grew throughout their lives, but underwent tremendous growth spurts for about four years, after an extended juvenile phase.][[0.0]]
[Sexual maturity may have ended this rapid growth phase, after which growth slowed down considerably in adult animals.][[0.0]]
[Examining five Gorgosaurus specimens of various sizes, Erickson calculated a maximum growth rate of about 110�kilograms -LRB-50�lb-RRB- during the rapid growth phase, slower than in tyrannosaurines like Daspletosaurus and Tyrannosaurus, but comparable to Albertosaurus.][[0.0]]
[Gorgosaurus spent as much as half its life in the juvenile phase before ballooning up to near-maximum size in only a few years.][[0.0]]
[This, along with the complete lack of predators intermediate in size between huge adult tyrannosaurids and other small theropods, suggests these niches may have been filled by juvenile tyrannosaurids.][[0.0]]
[This is seen in modern Komodo dragons, where hatchlings start off as tree-dwelling insectivores and slowly mature into massive apex predators capable of taking down large vertebrates.][[0.0]]
[Other tyrannosaurids, including Albertosaurus, have been found in aggregations that some have suggested to represent mixed-age packs, but there is no evidence of gregarious behavior in Gorgosaurus.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Paleoecology All known specimens of Gorgosaurus libratus have been recovered from the Dinosaur Park Formation in Alberta.][[0.0]]
[This formation dates to the middle of the Campanian, between 76.5 and 74�million years ago.][[1.0]]
[At this time, the area was a coastal plain along the western edge of the Western Interior Seaway, which divided North America in half.][[0.0]]
[The Laramide Orogeny had begun uplifting the Rocky Mountains to the west, from which flowed great rivers that deposited eroded sediment in vast floodplains along the coast.][[0.0]]
[The climate was subtropical with marked seasonality, and periodic droughts sometimes resulted in massive mortality among the great herds of dinosaurs, as represented in the numerous bonebed deposits preserved in the Dinosaur Park Formation.][[0.0]]
[Conifers formed the forest canopy, while the understory plants consisted of ferns, tree ferns and angiosperms.][[0.0]]
[Around 73�million years ago, the seaway began to expand, transgressing into areas formerly above sea level and drowning the Dinosaur Park ecosystem.][[0.0]]
[This transgression, called the Bearpaw Sea, is recorded by the marine sediments of the massive Bearpaw Shale.][[0.0]]
[The Dinosaur Park Formation preserves a great wealth of vertebrate fossils.][[0.0]]
[A wide variety of fish swam the rivers and estuaries, including gars, sturgeons, sharks and rays, among others.][[0.0]]
[Frogs, salamanders, turtles, crocodilians and champsosaurs also dwelled in the aquatic habitats.][[0.0]]
[Azhdarchid pterosaurs and neornithine birds like Apatornis flew overhead, while the enantiornithine bird Avisaurus lived on the ground alongside multituberculate, marsupial and placental mammals.][[0.0]]
[A number of species of terrestrial lizards were also present, including whiptails, skinks, monitors and alligator lizards.][[0.0]]
[Dinosaur fossils in particular are found with unrivaled abundance and diversity.][[0.0]]
[Huge herds of ceratopsids roamed the floodplains alongside equally large groups of hadrosaurine and lambeosaurine hadrosaurs.][[1.0]]
[Other herbivorous groups like ornithomimids, therizinosaurs, pachycephalosaurs, small ornithopods, nodosaurids and ankylosaurids were also represented.][[0.0]]
[Small predatory dinosaurs like oviraptorosaurs, troodonts and dromaeosaurs hunted smaller prey than the huge tyrannosaurids, Daspletosaurus and Gorgosaurus, which were two orders of magnitude larger in mass.][[0.0]]
[Intervening predatory niches may have been filled by young tyrannosaurids.][[0.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Origins Both geologic and climatic events helped to make Australia's fauna unique.][[1.0]]
[Australia was once part of the southern supercontinent Gondwana, which also included South America, Africa, India and Antarctica.][[0.0]]
[Gondwana began to break up 140�million years ago -LRB-MYA-RRB-; 50 MYA Australia separated from Antarctica and was relatively isolated until the collision of the Indo-Australian Plate with Asia in the Miocene era 5.3 MYA.][[0.0]]
[The establishment and evolution of the present-day fauna was apparently shaped by the unique climate and the geology of the continent.][[0.0]]
[As Australia drifted, it was, to some extent, isolated from the effects of global climate change.][[1.0]]
[The unique fauna that originated in Gondwana, such as the marsupials, survived and adapted in Australia.][[1.0]]
[After the Miocene, fauna of Asian origin were able to establish themselves in Australia.][[0.0]]
[The Wallace Line--the hypothetical line separating the zoogeographical regions of Asia and Australasia--marks the tectonic boundary between the Eurasian and Indo-Australian plates.][[0.0]]
[This continental boundary prevented the formation of land bridges and resulted in a distinct zoological distribution, with limited overlap, of most Asian and Australian fauna, with the exception of birds.][[0.0]]
[Following the emergence of the circumpolar current in the mid-Oligocene era -LRB-some 15 MYA-RRB-, the Australian climate became increasingly arid, giving rise to a diverse group of arid-specialised organisms, just as the wet tropical and seasonally wet areas gave rise to their own uniquely adapted species.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Mammals Australia has a rich mammalian fossil history, as well as a variety of extant mammalian species, dominated by the marsupials.][[0.0]]
[The fossil record shows that monotremes have been present in Australia since the Early Cretaceous 145--99 MYA, and that marsupials and placental mammals date from the Eocene 56--34 MYA, when modern mammals first appeared in the fossil record.][[0.0]]
[Although marsupials and placental mammals did coexist in Australia in the Eocene, only marsupials have survived to the present.][[0.0]]
[The placental mammals made their reappearance in Australia in the Miocene, when Australia moved closer to Indonesia, and bats and rodents started to appear reliably in the fossil record.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- The marsupials evolved to fill specific ecological niches, and in many cases they are physically similar to the placental mammals in Eurasia and North America that occupy similar niches, a phenomenon known as convergent evolution.][[1.0]]
[For example, the top predator in Australia, the Tasmanian Tiger, bore a striking resemblance to canids such as the Gray Wolf;-LSB-citation needed-RSB- gliding possums and flying squirrels have similar adaptations enabling their arboreal lifestyle;-LSB-citation needed-RSB- and the Numbat and anteaters are both digging insectivores.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Birds Australia and its territories are home to around 800 species of bird; about 350 of these are endemic to the zoogeographic region that covers Australia, New Guinea and New Zealand.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- The fossil record of birds in Australia is patchy; however, there are records of the ancestors of contemporary species as early as the Late Oligocene.][[0.0]]
[Birds with a Gondwanan history include the flightless ratites -LRB-the Emu and Southern Cassowary-RRB-, megapodes -LRB-the Malleefowl and Australian Brush-turkey-RRB-, and a huge group of endemic parrots, order Psittaciformes.][[0.0]]
[Australian parrots comprise a sixth of the world's parrots, including many cockatoos and galahs.][[0.0]]
[The Kookaburra is the largest species of the kingfisher family, known for its call, which sounds uncannily like loud, echoing human laughter.][[0.0]]
[The passerines of Australia, also known as songbirds or perching birds, include wrens, robins, the magpie group, thornbills, pardalotes, the huge honeyeater family, treecreepers, lyrebirds, Birds of Paradise and bowerbirds.][[1.0]]
[The Satin Bowerbird has attracted the interest of evolutionary psychologists; it has a complex courtship ritual in which the male creates a bower filled with blue, shiny items to woo mates.][[0.0]]
[Relatively recent colonists from Eurasia are swallows,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- larks, thrushes, cisticolas, sunbirds, and some raptors, including the large Wedge-tailed Eagle.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- A number of bird species have been introduced by humans; some, like the European Goldfinch and Greenfinch, coexist happily with Australian species,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- while others, such as the Common Starling, Common Blackbird, House Sparrow and Indian Mynah, are destructive of some native bird species and thus destabilise the native ecosystem.][[0.0]]
[About 200 species of seabird live on the Australian coast, including many species of migratory seabird.][[0.0]]
[Australia is at the southern end of the East Asian-Australasian flyway for migratory water birds, which extends from Far-East Russia and Alaska through Southeast Asia to Australia and New Zealand.][[0.0]]
[About two million birds travel this route to and from Australia each year.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- One very common large seabird is the Australian Pelican, which can be found in most waterways in Australia.][[0.0]]
[The Little Penguin is the only species of penguin that breeds on mainland Australia.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Amphibians and reptiles Australia has four families of native frogs and one introduced toad, the Cane Toad.][[0.0]]
[In 1935 the Cane Toad was introduced to Australia in a failed attempt to control pests in sugarcane crops.][[0.0]]
[It has since become a devastating pest, spreading across northern Australia.][[0.0]]
[As well as competing with native insectivores for food, the Cane Toad produces a venom that is toxic to native fauna, as well as to humans.][[0.0]]
[The Myobatrachidae, or southern frogs, are Australia's largest group of frogs, with 120 species from 21 genera.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- A notable member of this group is the colourful and endangered Corroboree Frog.][[0.0]]
[The tree frogs, from family Hylidae, are common in high rainfall areas on the north and east coasts; there are 77 Australian species from three genera.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- The 18 species from two genera-LSB-citation needed-RSB- of the Microhylidae frogs are restricted to the rainforests; the smallest species, the Scanty Frog, is from this family.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- There is a single species from the world's dominant frog group, family Ranidae -- the Australian Wood Frog -- which only occurs in the Queensland rainforests.][[0.0]]
[As elsewhere, there has been a precipitous decline in Australia's frog populations in recent years.][[0.0]]
[Although the full reasons for the decline are uncertain, it can be at least partly attributed to the fatal amphibian fungal disease chytridiomycosis.][[0.0]]
[Australia has both saltwater and freshwater crocodiles.][[0.0]]
[The Saltwater Crocodile, known colloquially as the ``salty,'' is the largest living crocodile species; reaching over 7�m, and weighing over 1,000�kg, they can and do kill people.][[0.0]]
[They live on the coast and in the freshwater rivers and wetlands of northern Australia, and they are farmed for their meat and leather.][[0.0]]
[Freshwater Crocodiles, found only in northern Australia, are not considered dangerous to humans.][[0.0]]
[The Australian coast is visited by six species of sea turtle: the Flatback, Green Sea, Hawksbill, Olive Ridley, Loggerhead and the Leatherback Sea Turtles; all are protected in Australian waters.][[0.0]]
[There are 29 species of Australian freshwater turtles from eight genera of family Chelidae.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- The Pig-nosed Turtle is the only Australian turtle not of that family.][[0.0]]
[Australia and Antarctica are the only continents without any living species of land tortoise.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Australia is the only continent-LSB-citation needed-RSB- where venomous snakes outnumber their non-venomous cousins.][[0.0]]
[Australian snakes belong to seven families.][[0.0]]
[Of these, the most venomous species,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- including the Fierce Snake, Eastern Brown Snake, Taipan and Eastern Tiger Snake are from the family Elapidae.][[0.0]]
[Of the 200 species of elapid, 86 are found only in Australia.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Thirty-three sea snakes from family Hydrophiidae inhabit Australia's northern waters; many are extremely venomous.][[0.0]]
[Two species of sea snake from the Acrochordidae also occur in Australian waters.][[0.0]]
[Australia has only 11 species from the world's most significant snake family Colubridae; none are endemic, and they are considered to be relatively recent arrivals from Asia.][[0.0]]
[There are 15 python species and 31 species of insectivorous blind snake.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- There are more lizards in Australia than anywhere else in the world,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- with representatives of five families.][[0.0]]
[There are 114 species in 18 genera of gecko found throughout the Australian continent.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- The Pygopodidae is a family of limbless lizards endemic to the Australian region; of the 34 species from eight genera, only one species does not occur in Australia.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- The Agamidae or Dragon lizards are represented by 66 species in 13 genera,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- including the Thorny Devil, Bearded Dragon and Frill-necked Lizard.][[0.0]]
[There are 26 species of monitor lizard,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- family Varanidae, in Australia, where they are commonly known as goannas.][[0.0]]
[The largest Australian monitor is the Perentie, which can reach up to 2�m in length.][[0.0]]
[There are 389 species of skink from 38 genera, comprising about 50% of the total Australian lizard fauna;-LSB-citation needed-RSB- this group includes the blue-tongued lizards.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Fish More than 4,400 species of fish inhabit Australia's waterways; of these, 90% are endemic.][[0.0]]
[However, because of the relative scarcity of freshwater waterways, Australia has only 170 species of freshwater fish.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Two families of freshwater fish have ancient origins: the arowana or ``bony tongues,'' and the Queensland lungfish.][[0.0]]
[The Queensland lungfish is the most primitive of the lungfish, having evolved before Australia separated from Gondwana.][[0.0]]
[One of the smallest freshwater fish, peculiar to the southwest of Western Australia, is the salamanderfish, which can survive desiccation in the dry season by burrowing into mud.][[0.0]]
[Other families with a potentially Gondwanan origin include the Retropinnidae, Galaxiidae, Aplochitonidae and Percichthyidae.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB-Apart from the ancient freshwater species, 70% of Australia's freshwater fish have affinities with tropical Indo-Pacific marine species that have adapted to freshwater.][[0.0]]
[Nevertheless, fossil evidence indicates that many of these freshwater species are still ancient in origin.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- These species include freshwater lampreys, herrings, catfish, rainbowfish, and some 50 species of gudgeon, including the Sleepy Cod.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Native freshwater game fish include the Barramundi, Murray Cod, and Golden Perch.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Two species of endangered freshwater shark are found in the Northern Territory.][[0.0]]
[Several exotic freshwater fish species, including brown, brook and rainbow trout, Atlantic and Chinook salmon, redfin perch, carp and mosquitofish, have been introduced to Australian waterways.][[0.0]]
[The mosquitofish is a particularly aggressive species known for harassing and nipping the fins of other fish.][[0.0]]
[It has been linked to declines and localised extinctions of several small native fish species.][[0.0]]
[The introduced trout species have had serious negative impacts on a number of upland native fish species including trout cod, Macquarie perch and galaxias species as well as other upland fauna such as the Spotted Tree Frog.][[0.0]]
[The carp is strongly implicated in the dramatic loss in waterweed, decline of small native fish species and permanently elevated levels of turbidity in the Murray-Darling Basin of southwest Australia.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Most of Australia's fish species are marine.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Groups of interest include the moray eels and squirrelfish, as well as the pipefish and seahorses, whose males incubate their partner's eggs in a specialised pouch.][[0.0]]
[There are 80 species of grouper in Australian waters,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- including one of the world's biggest bony fish, the Giant Grouper, which can grow as large as 2.7�m and weigh up to 400�kg.][[0.0]]
[The trevally, a group of 50 species of silver schooling fish, and the snappers are popular species for commercial fishing.][[0.0]]
[The Great Barrier Reef supports a huge variety of small- and medium-sized reef fish, including the damselfish, butterflyfish, angelfish, gobies, cardinalfish, wrassees, triggerfish and surgeonfish.][[0.0]]
[There are several venomous fish, among them several species of stonefish and pufferfish and the red lionfish, all of which have toxins that can kill humans.][[0.0]]
[There are 11 venomous species of stingray,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- the largest of which is the smooth stingray.][[0.0]]
[The barracudas are one of the reef's largest species.][[0.0]]
[However, large reef fish should not be eaten for fear of ciguatera poisoning.][[0.0]]
[Sharks inhabit all the coastal waters and estuarine habitats of Australia's coast.][[0.0]]
[There are 166 species, including 30 species of requiem shark, 32 of catshark, six of wobbegong shark, and 40 of dogfish shark.][[0.0]]
[There are three species from the family Heterodontidae: the Port Jackson shark, the zebra bullhead shark and the crested bullhead shark.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- In 2004, there were 12 unprovoked shark attacks in Australia, of which two were fatal.][[0.0]]
[Only 3 species of shark pose a significant threat to humans: the bull shark, the tiger shark and the great white shark.][[0.0]]
[Some popular beaches in Queensland and New South Wales are protected by shark netting, a method that has reduced the population of both dangerous and harmless shark species through accidental entanglement.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- The overfishing of sharks has also significantly reduced shark numbers in Australian waters, and several species are now endangered.][[1.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- A megamouth shark was found on a Perth beach in 1988; very little is known about this species, but this discovery may indicate the presence of the species in Australian coastal waters.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Invertebrates Of the estimated 200,000 animal species in Australia, about 96% are invertebrates.][[0.0]]
[While the full extent of invertebrate diversity is uncertain, 90% of insects and molluscs are considered endemic.][[0.0]]
[Invertebrates occupy many ecological niches and are important in all ecosystems as decomposers, pollinators, and food sources.][[0.0]]
[The largest group of invertebrates is the insects, comprising 75% of Australia's known species of animals.][[0.0]]
[The most diverse insect orders are the Coleoptera, with 28,200 species of beetles and weevils, the Lepidoptera with 20,816 species-LSB-citation needed-RSB- including butterflies and moths, and 12,781 species of Hymenoptera,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- including the ants, bees and wasps.][[0.0]]
[Order Diptera, which includes the flies and mosquitoes, comprises 7,786 species,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Order Hemiptera, including bugs, aphids and hoppers, comprises 5,650 species; and there are 2,827 species-LSB-citation needed-RSB- of order Orthoptera, including grasshoppers, crickets and katydids.][[0.0]]
[Introduced species that pose a significant threat to native species include the European wasp, the red fire ant, the yellow crazy ant and feral honeybees which compete with native bees.][[0.0]]
[Australia has a wide variety of arachnids, including 135 species of spider that are familiar enough to have common names.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- There are numerous highly venomous species, including the notorious Sydney funnel-web and redback spiders, whose bites can be deadly.][[0.0]]
[There are thousands of species of mites and ticks from order Acarina.][[0.0]]
[Australia also has eight species of pseudoscorpion and nine scorpion species.][[1.0]]
[In the Annelida -LRB-sub-RRB-class Oligochaeta there are many families of aquatic worms, and for native terrestrial worms: the Enchytraeidae -LRB-pot worms-RRB- and the ``true'' earthworms in families Acanthodrilidae, Octochaetidae and Megascolecidae.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- The latter includes the world's largest earthworm, the giant Gippsland earthworm, found only in Gippsland, Victoria.][[0.0]]
[On average they reach 80�cm in length, but specimens up to 3.7�m in length have been found.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- The large family Parastacidae includes 124 species of Australian freshwater crayfish.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- These include the world's smallest crayfish, the swamp crayfish, which does not exceed 30�mm in length, and the world's largest crayfish, the Tasmanian giant freshwater crayfish, measuring up to 76�cm long and weighing 4.5�kg.][[0.0]]
[The crayfish genus Cherax includes the common yabby, in addition to the farmed species marron and Queensland red claw.][[0.0]]
[Species from the genus Engaeus, commonly known as the land crayfish, are also found in Australia.][[0.0]]
[Engaeus species are not entirely aquatic, because they spend most of their lives living in burrows.][[0.0]]
[Australia has seven species of freshwater crab from the genus Austrothelphusa.][[0.0]]
[These crabs live burrowed into the banks of waterways and can plug their burrows, surviving through several years of drought.][[0.0]]
[The extremely primitive freshwater mountain shrimp, found only in Tasmania, are a unique group, resembling species found in the fossil record from 200 MYA.][[0.0]]
[A huge variety of marine invertebrates are found in Australian waters, with the Great Barrier Reef an important source of this diversity.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Families include the Porifera or sea sponges, the Cnidaria -LRB-includes the jellyfish, corals and sea anemones, comb jellies-RRB-, the Echinodermata -LRB-includes the sea urchins, sea stars, brittle stars, sea cucumbers, the lamp shells-RRB- and the Mollusca -LRB-includes snails, slugs, limpets, squid, octopus, cockles, oysters, clams, and chitons-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Venomous invertebrates include the box jellyfish, the blue-ringed octopus, and ten species of cone snail,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- which can cause respiratory failure and death in humans.][[1.0]]
[The crown-of-thorns starfish usually inhabits the Reef at low densities.][[0.0]]
[However, under conditions that are not yet well understood, they can reproduce to reach an unsustainable population density when coral is devoured at a rate faster than it can regenerate.][[0.0]]
[This presents a serious reef management issue.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Other problematic marine invertebrates include the native species purple sea-urchin and the white urchin, which have been able to take over marine habitats and form urchin barrens due to the over harvesting of their natural predators which include abalone and rock lobster.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Introduced invertebrate pests include the Asian mussel, New Zealand green-lipped mussel, black-striped mussel and the Northern Pacific seastar, all of which displace native shellfish.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- There are many unique marine crustaceans in Australian waters.][[0.0]]
[The best-known class, to which all the edible species of crustacean belong, is Malacostraca.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- The warm waters of northern Australia are home to many species of decapod crustaceans, including crabs, false crabs, hermit crabs, lobsters, shrimps, and prawns.][[0.0]]
[The Peracarids, including the amphipods and isopods, are more diverse in the colder waters of southern Australia.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Less-well-known marine groups include the classes Remipedia, Cephalocarida, Branchiopoda, Maxillopoda -LRB-which includes the barnacles, copepods and fish lice-RRB-, and the Ostracoda.][[0.0]]
[Notable species include the Tasmanian giant crab, the second largest crab species in the world,-LSB-citation needed-RSB- found in deep water, and weighing up to 13�kg, and the Australian spiny lobsters, such as the Western rock lobster, which are distinct from other lobster species as they do not have claws.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Invasive species Introduction of exotic fauna in Australia by design, accident and natural processes has led to a considerable number of invasive, feral and pest species which have flourished and now impact the environment adversely.][[0.0]]
[Introduced organisms affect the environment in a number of ways.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- Rabbits render land economically useless by eating everything.][[0.0]]
[Red Foxes affect local endemic fauna by predation while the cane toad poisons the predators by being eaten.][[0.0]]
[The invasive species include birds -LRB-Indian Mynah-RRB- and fish -LRB-common carp-RRB-, insects -LRB-red imported fire ant-RRB- and molluscs -LRB-Asian mussel-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The problem is compounded by invasive exotic flora as well as introduced diseases, fungi and parasites.][[0.0]]
[Costly, laborious and time-consuming efforts at control of these species has met with little success and this continues to be a major problem area in the conservation of Australia's biodiversity.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Human impact and conservation For at least 40,000 years, Australia's fauna played an integral role in the traditional lifestyles of Indigenous Australians, who exploited many species as a source of food and skins.][[0.0]]
[Vertebrates commonly harvested included macropods, opossums, seals, fish and the Short-tailed Shearwater, most commonly known as the Muttonbird.][[0.0]]
[Invertebrates used as food included insects such as the Bogong moth and larvae collectively called witchetty grubs and molluscs.][[0.0]]
[The use of fire-stick farming, in which large swathes of bushland were burnt to facilitate hunting, modified both flora and fauna -- and are thought to have contributed to the extinction of large herbivores with a specialised diet, such as the flightless birds from the genus Genyornis.][[0.0]]
[The role of hunting and landscape modification by aboriginal people in the extinction of the Australian megafauna is debated.][[0.0]]
[The impact of Aborigines on native species populations is widely considered to be less significant than that of the European settlers, whose impact on the landscape has been on a relatively large scale.][[0.0]]
[Since European settlement, direct exploitation of native fauna, habitat destruction and the introduction of exotic predators and competitive herbivores has led to the extinction of some 27 mammal, 23 bird and 4 frog species.][[1.0]]
[Much of Australia's fauna is protected by legislation;-LSB-citation needed-RSB- a notable exception is kangaroos, which are prolific and are regularly culled.][[0.0]]
[The federal Environment Protection and Biodiversity Conservation Act 1999 was created to meet Australia's obligations as a signatory to the 1992 Convention on Biological Diversity.][[0.0]]
[This act protects all native fauna and provides for the identification and protection of threatened species.][[0.0]]
[In each state and territory, there is statutory listing of threatened species.][[0.0]]
[At present, 380 animal species are classified as either endangered or threatened under the EPBC Act, and other species are protected under state and territory legislation.][[0.0]]
[More broadly, a complete cataloguing of all the species within Australia has been undertaken, a key step in the conservation of Australian fauna and biodiversity.][[0.0]]
[In 1973, the federal government established the Australian Biological Resources Study -LRB-ABRS-RRB-, which coordinates research in the taxonomy, identification, classification and distribution of flora and fauna.][[0.0]]
[The ABRS maintains free online databases cataloguing much of the described Australian flora and fauna.][[0.0]]
[Impacts such as the illegal setting of traps in rivers affect animals such as the Australian platypus, along with lack of awareness each year an average of 2--5 Australians lose their lives to what is presumed a safe creature.][[0.0]]
[The key is understanding of Australia's diverse wildlife and fauna; what seems safe is often deadly.][[0.0]]
[Australia is a member of the International Whaling Commission and is strongly opposed to commercial whaling--all Cetacean species are protected in Australian waters.][[0.0]]
[Australia is also a signatory to the CITES agreement and prohibits the export of endangered species.][[0.0]]
[Protected areas have been created in every state and territory to protect and preserve the country's unique ecosystems.][[0.0]]
[These protected areas include national parks and other reserves, as well as 64 wetlands registered under the Ramsar Convention and 16 World Heritage Sites.][[0.0]]
[As of 2002, 10.8% -LRB-774,619.51�km²-RRB- of the total land area of Australia is within protected areas.][[1.0]]
[Protected marine zones have been created in many areas to preserve marine biodiversity; as of 2002, these areas cover about 7% -LRB-646,000�km²-RRB- of Australia's marine jurisdiction.][[0.0]]
[The Great Barrier Reef is managed by the Great Barrier Reef Marine Park Authority under specific federal and state legislation.][[0.0]]
[Some of Australia's fisheries are already overexploited, and quotas have been set for the sustainable harvest of many marine species.][[0.0]]
[The State of the Environment Report, 2001, prepared by independent researchers for the federal government, concluded that the condition of the environment and environmental management in Australia had worsened since the previous report in 1996.][[0.0]]
[Of particular relevance to wildlife conservation, the report indicated that many processes--such as salinity, changing hydrological conditions, land clearing, fragmentation of ecosystems, poor management of the coastal environment, and invasive species--pose major problems for protecting Australia's biodiversity.][[1.0]]
