[-LSB-edit-RSB- Background By the early 3rd century, the Han Dynasty, which had ruled China for almost four centuries -LRB-albeit with a 16-year interruption, dividing the dynasty into its Western and Eastern periods-RRB-, was crumbling.][[0.0]]
[Emperor Xian had been a political figurehead since 189, with no control over the actions of the various warlords controlling their respective territories.][[0.0]]
[One of the most powerful rulers in northern China was the warlord Cao Cao, who, by the year 207, had unified northern China and retained total control of the North China Plain.][[0.0]]
[He then completed a successful campaign against the Wuhuan in the winter of the same year, thus securing his northern frontier.][[0.0]]
[Upon his return in 208, he was proclaimed to be the Imperial Chancellor of Han, a position that granted him absolute authority over the entire imperial government -LRB-de Crespigny 1969:253, 465 6n-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Shortly afterwards, in the autumn of 208, his army began a Southern Campaign -LRB-Eikenberry 1994; de Crespigny 2003-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The Yangtze River in the area of Jing province -LRB-which roughly corresponded to modern Hubei and Hunan provinces-RRB- was key to the success of this strategy.][[0.0]]
[If Cao Cao were to have any hope of reuniting the sundered Han empire, he had to achieve naval control of the middle Yangtze and command the strategic naval base at Jiangling as a means of access to the southern region -LRB-de Crespigny 2003-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Two warlords controlled the regions of the Yangtze that were key to Cao Cao's success: Liu Biao, Governor of Jing Province, controlled the river west of the mouth of the Han, roughly encompassing the area around the city of Xiakou and all territory south of that region.][[1.0]]
[Sun Quan controlled the river east of the Han and the southeastern territories abutting it -LRB-de Crespigny 2007:773-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[A third ally, Liu Bei, was living in refuge with Liu Biao at the garrison in Fancheng -LRB-modern Xiangfan-RRB-, having fled from the northeast to the Jing Province following a failed plot to assassinate Cao Cao and restore power to the imperial dynasty -LRB-de Crespigny 2007:480; de Crespigny 1969:258-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The initial stages of the campaign were an unqualified success for Cao Cao, as the command of the Jing Province had been substantially weakened and the Jing armies exhausted by conflict with Sun Quan to the south -LRB-de Crespigny 2007:486-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Factions had arisen supporting either of Liu Biao's two sons in a struggle for succession.][[0.0]]
[The younger son prevailed, and Liu Biao's dispossessed eldest son, Liu Qi, departed to assume a commandery in Jiangxia -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:241-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Liu Biao died of illness only a few weeks later, while Cao Cao was advancing from the north and, under these circumstances, Liu Biao's younger son and successor, Liu Cong, quickly surrendered.][[0.0]]
[Cao Cao thus captured a sizeable fleet and secured the naval base at Jiangling.][[0.0]]
[This provided him with a key strategic military depot and forward base to harbour his ships -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:246,250,255-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[When Jing fell, Liu Bei quickly fled south, accompanied by a refugee population of civilians and soldiers.][[0.0]]
[This disorganised exodus was pursued by Cao Cao's elite cavalry, and was surrounded and decisively beaten at the Battle of Changban -LRB-near the modern-day city of Dangyang in Hubei-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Liu Bei escaped, however, and fled further east to Xiakou, where he liaised with Sun Quan's emissary Lu Su.][[0.0]]
[At this point historical accounts are inconsistent; Lu Su may have successfully encouraged Liu Bei to move even further east, to Fankou -LRB-樊口-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[In either case, Liu Bei was later joined by Liu Qi and levies from Jiangxia -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:255-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Liu Bei's main advisor, Zhuge Liang, was sent to Chaisang -LRB-柴桑-RRB- to negotiate forming a mutual front against Cao Cao with the state of Wu -LRB-de Crespigny 1969:263-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[By the time Zhuge Liang arrived, Cao Cao had already sent Sun Quan a letter boasting of commanding 800,000 men and demanding Sun Quan's surrender.][[0.0]]
[The faction led by Sun Quan's Chief Clerk, Zhang Zhao, advocated surrender, citing Cao Cao's overwhelming numerical advantage.][[0.0]]
[However, on separate occasions, Lu Su, Zhuge Liang, and Wu's chief commander, Zhou Yu, all presented arguments to persuade Sun Quan to agree to the alliance against the northerners.][[0.0]]
[Sun Quan finally decided upon war, chopping off a corner of his desk during an assembly and stating: ``Anyone who still dares argue for surrender will be -LSB-treated-RSB- the same as this desk.''][[0.0]]
[He then assigned Zhou Yu, Cheng Pu, and Lu Su with 30,000 men to aid Liu Bei against Cao Cao -LRB-de Crespigny 1996-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Although Cao Cao had boasted command of 800,000 men, Zhou Yu estimated Cao Cao's actual troop strength to be closer to 220,000.][[0.0]]
[Furthermore, this total included 70,000 impressed troops from the armies of the recently defeated Liu Biao, so the loyalty and morale of a large number of Cao Cao's force was uncertain -LRB-Eikenberry 1994:60-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[With the 20,000 soldiers that Liu Bei had gathered, the alliance consisted of approximately 50,000 marines who were trained and prepared for battle -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:252;255-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Battle The Battle of Red Cliffs unfolded in three stages: an initial skirmish at Red Cliffs followed by a retreat to the Wulin battlefields on the northwestern bank of the Yangtze, a decisive naval engagement, and Cao Cao's disastrous retreat along Huarong Road.][[1.0]]
[The combined Sun-Liu force sailed upstream from either Xiakou or Fankou to Red Cliffs, where they encountered Cao Cao's vanguard force.][[0.0]]
[Plagued by disease and low morale due to the series of forced marches they had undertaken on the prolonged Southern Campaign -LRB-de Crespigny 2003-RRB-, Cao Cao's men could not gain an advantage in the small skirmish which ensued, so Cao Cao retreated to Wulin -LRB-north of the Yangtze River-RRB- and the allies pulled back to the south -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:257-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Cao Cao had moored his ships from stem to stern, possibly aiming to reduce seasickness in his navy, which comprised mostly northerners who were not used to living on ships.][[0.0]]
[Observing this, divisional commander Huang Gai sent Cao Cao a letter feigning surrender and prepared a squadron of capital ships described as mengchong doujian -LRB-蒙衝鬥艦-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The ships had been converted into fire ships by filling them with bundles of kindling, dry reeds, and fatty oil.][[0.0]]
[As Huang Gai's ``defecting'' squadron approached the midpoint of the river, the sailors applied fire to the ships before taking to small boats.][[0.0]]
[The unmanned fire ships, carried by the southeastern wind, sped towards Cao Cao's fleet and set it ablaze.][[0.0]]
[Within a short time smoke and flames stretched across the sky, and a large number of men and horses either burned to death or drowned -LRB-Chen c. 280:54.1262-63-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Following the initial shock, Zhou Yu and the allies led a lightly armed force to capitalise on the assault.][[0.0]]
[The northern army was thrown into confusion and was utterly smashed.][[0.0]]
[Seeing the situation was hopeless, Cao Cao then issued a general order of retreat and destroyed a number of his remaining ships before withdrawing -LRB-Chen c. 280-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Cao Cao's army attempted a retreat along Huarong Road, including a long stretch passing through marshlands north of Dongting Lake.][[0.0]]
[Heavy rains had reduced the track to a thick mire, making the road so treacherous that many of the sick soldiers had to carry bundles of grass on their backs and use them to fill the road, to allow the horsemen to cross.][[0.0]]
[Many of these soldiers drowned in the mud or were trampled to death in the effort.][[0.0]]
[To the misery of Cao Cao's army, the allies, led by Zhou Yu and Liu Bei, gave chase over land and water until they reached Nan Commandery -LRB-南郡-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Combined with famine and disease, this decimated Cao Cao's remaining forces.][[0.0]]
[Cao Cao then retreated north to his home base of Ye, leaving Cao Ren and Xu Huang to guard Jiangling, Yue Jin stationed in Xiangyang, and Man Chong in Dangyang -LRB-Chen c. 280-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The allied counterattack might have vanquished Cao Cao and his forces entirely.][[0.0]]
[However, the crossing of the Yangtze River dissolved into chaos as the allied armies converged on the riverbank and fought over the limited number of ferries.][[0.0]]
[To restore order, a detachment led by the allied general Gan Ning established a bridgehead in Yiling to the north, and only a staunch rearguard action by Cao Ren prevented further catastrophe -LRB-Eikenberry 1994:60; de Crespigny 2007:239-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Analysis A combination of Cao Cao's strategic errors and the effectiveness of Huang Gai's ruse had resulted in the allied victory at the Battle of Red Cliffs.][[0.0]]
[Zhou Yu had previously observed that Cao Cao's generals and soldiers comprised mostly cavalry and infantry, and few had any experience in naval warfare.][[0.0]]
[Cao Cao also had little support among the people of Jing province, and thus lacked a secure forward base of operations -LRB-Eikenberry 1994:60-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Despite the strategic acumen Cao Cao had displayed in earlier campaigns and battles, in this case he had simply assumed that numerical superiority would eventually defeat the Sun and Liu navy.][[0.0]]
[Cao's first tactical mistake was converting his massive army of infantry and cavalry into a marine corps and navy: with only a few days of drills before the battle, Cao Cao's troops were ravaged by sea-sickness and lack of experience on water.][[0.0]]
[Tropical diseases, to which the southerners had long been immune, also plagued the soldiers of the north with the debilitating effects of sickness rampant in Cao Cao's camps.][[0.0]]
[Although numerous, Cao Cao's men were already exhausted by the unfamiliar environment and the extended southern campaign, as Zhuge Liang observed: ``Even a powerful arrow at the end of its flight cannot penetrate a silk cloth'' -LRB-Military Documents 1979:193-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The uncharacteristically poor preparation and miscalculations displayed by Cao Cao during this campaign may have been partly due to the recent death of his strategist and advisor Guo Jia.][[0.0]]
[Cao Cao himself had commented: ``Had Guo Jia been with us, I would never have got into such trouble'' -LRB-Chen c. 280:14:433-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Another key advisor, Jia Xu, had recommended after the surrender of Liu Cong that the overtaxed armies be given time to rest and replenish before engaging the armies of Sun Quan and Liu Bei, but Cao Cao disregarded the advice -LRB-Eikenberry 1994:60-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Cao Cao's own thoughts regarding his failure at Red Cliffs suggest that he held his own actions and misfortunes responsible for the defeat, rather than the strategies utilised by his enemy during the battle: ''...it was only because of the sickness that I burnt my ships and retreated.][[0.0]]
[It is out of all reason for Zhou Yu to take the credit for himself.''][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Aftermath By the end of 209, the post Cao Cao had established at Jiangling fell to Zhou Yu.][[0.0]]
[The borders of the land under Cao Cao's control contracted about 160�kilometres -LRB-100�miles-RRB-, to the area around Xiangyang -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:291-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Liu Bei, on the other hand, had gained territory by taking over the four commanderies south of the Yangtze River.][[0.0]]
[Sun Quan's troops had suffered far greater casualties than Liu Bei's in the extended conflict against Cao Ren following the Battle of Red Cliffs -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:291--292-RRB-, and the death of Zhou Yu in 210 resulted in a drastic weakening of Sun Quan's strength in the Jing province -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:297-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Liu Bei also occupied the Jing province that Cao Cao had recently lost--a strategic and naturally fortified area on the Yangtze River that Wu claimed for itself.][[0.0]]
[The control of Jing provided Liu Bei with virtually unlimited access to the passage into Shu and important waterways into Wu, as well as dominion of the southern Yangtze River.][[1.0]]
[Never again would Cao Cao command so large a fleet as he had at Jiangling, nor would a similar opportunity to destroy his southern rivals present itself again -LRB-de Crespigny 2007:37-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The Battle of Red Cliffs and the capture of Jing province by Liu Bei confirmed the separation of Southern China from the northern heartland of the Yellow River valley, and also foreshadowed a north-south axis of hostility which would resonate for centuries -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:260-RRB-.][[1.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Location The precise location of the Red Cliffs battlefield has long been the subject of both popular and academic debates, but has never been conclusively established.][[0.0]]
[Scholarly debates have continued for at least 1,350 years -LRB-Zhang 2006:215-RRB-, and a number of arguments in favour of alternative sites have been put forward.][[0.0]]
[There are clear grounds for rejecting at least some of these proposals, but four alternative locations are still advocated.][[0.0]]
[According to Zhang -LRB-2006-RRB-, many of the current debates stem from the fact that the course and length of the Yangtze River between Wuli and Wuhan has changed since the Sui and Tang dynasties -LRB-Zhang 2006:225-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The modern-day debate is also complicated by the fact that the names of some of the key locations have changed over the following centuries.][[0.0]]
[For example, although modern Huarong city is located in Hunan, south of the Yangtze, in the 3rd century the city of that name was due east of Jiangling, considerably north of the Yangtze -LRB-Zhang 2006:229; de Crespigny 2004:256 78n-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Moreover, one candidate site, Puqi -LRB-蒲圻-RRB-, was renamed ``Chibi City'' -LRB-赤壁市-RRB- in 1998 in a direct attempt to tie this location to the historical battlefield.][[0.0]]
[Historical records state that Cao Cao's forces retreated north across the Yangtze after the initial engagement at Red Cliffs, unequivocally placing the battle site on the south bank of the Yangtze.][[0.0]]
[For this reason, a number of sites on the north bank have been discounted by historians and geographers.][[0.0]]
[Historical accounts also establish east and west boundaries for a stretch of the Yangtze which encompasses all possible sites for the battlefield.][[0.0]]
[The allied forces travelled upstream from either Fankou or Xiakou.][[0.0]]
[Since the Yangtze flows roughly eastward towards the ocean -LRB-with northeast and southeast meanders-RRB-, Red Cliffs must at least be west of Fankou, which is farther downstream.][[0.0]]
[The westernmost boundary is also clear, since Cao Cao's eastern advance from Jiangling included passing Baqiu -LRB-modern Yueyang city in Hunan province-RRB- on the shore of Dongting Lake.][[1.0]]
[The battle must also have been downstream -LRB-northeast-RRB- of that location -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:256--257; Zhang 2006:217-RRB-.][[1.0]]
[One popular candidate for the battle site is Chibi Hill in Huangzhou, sometimes referred to as ``Su Dongpo's Red Cliffs'' or the ``Literary Red Cliffs'' -LRB-文赤壁-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Support for this conjecture arises largely due to the famous 11th-century poem ``First Rhapsody on the Red Cliffs,'' which equates the Huangzhou Hill with the battlefield location.][[0.0]]
[The pinyin Romanization of this cliff's name is ``Chibi'', the same as the pinyin for Red Cliffs.][[0.0]]
[However, the Chinese characters are completely different -LRB-赤鼻-RRB- as is their meaning -LRB-``Red Nose Hill''-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[This site is also on the north bank of the Yangtze, and is directly across from Fankou rather than upstream from it -LRB-Zhang 2006:215-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Moreover, if the allied Sun/Liu forces left from Xiakou rather than Fankou, as the oldest historical sources suggest, then the hill in Huangzhou would have been downstream from the point of departure, a possibility which cannot be reconciled with historical sources.][[0.0]]
[Puqi, now named Chibi City, is perhaps the most widely accepted candidate.][[0.0]]
[To differentiate from Su Dongpo's Red Cliffs, the site is also referred to as the ``Military Red Cliffs'' -LRB-武赤壁-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[It is directly across the Yangtze from Wulin.][[0.0]]
[This argument was first proposed in the early Tang Dynasty -LRB-Zhang 2006:217-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[There are also characters engraved in the cliffs -LRB-see image at the top of this page-RRB- suggesting that this is the site of the battle.][[0.0]]
[The origin of the engraving can be dated to between the Tang and Song dynasties, making it at least 1,000 years old -LRB-Zhang 2006:219;228-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Some sources mention the south banks of the Yangtze in Jiayu County -LRB-嘉鱼县-RRB- in the prefecture-level city of Xianning in Hubei province as a possible location.][[0.0]]
[This would place the battlefield downstream from Puqi -LRB-Chibi City-RRB-, a view that is supported by scholars of Chinese history such as Rafe de Crespigny, Wang Li and Zhu Dongrun, following the Qing Dynasty historical document Shui Jing Zhu -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:256-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Another candidate is Wuhan, which straddles the Yangtze at the confluence of the Yangtze and Han rivers.][[0.0]]
[It is east of both Wulin -LRB-and Chibi City across the river-RRB- and Jiayu.][[0.0]]
[This metropolis was incorporated by joining three cities.][[0.0]]
[There is a local belief in Wuhan that the battle was fought at the junction of the rivers, southwest of the former Wuchang city, which is now part of Wuhan -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:256 n 78-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Zhang -LRB-2006:215;223-RRB- asserts that the Chibi battlefield was one of a set of hills in Wuchang that were levelled in the 1930s so that their stone could be used as raw material.][[0.0]]
[Citing several historical-geographical studies, Zhang -LRB-2006-RRB- shows that earlier accounts place the battlefield in Wuchang.][[0.0]]
[Sheng Honzhi's 5th-century Jingzhou ji in particular places the Chibi battlefield a distance of 160�li -LRB-approximately 80�kilometres -LRB-50�mi-RRB--RRB- downstream from Wulin, but since the Paizhou and Luxikou meanders increased the length of the Yangtze River between Wuli and Wuchang by 100�li -LRB-approximately 50�kilometres -LRB-31�mi-RRB-; see map-RRB- some time in the Sui and Tang dynasties -LRB-Zhang 2006:225-RRB-, later works do not regard Wuchang as a possible site.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Fictionalised account The romantic tradition that originated with the Romance of the Three Kingdoms differs from historical accounts in many details.][[1.0]]
[For example, Cao Cao's army strength was exaggerated to over 800,000 men.][[0.0]]
[This may be attributed to the ethos of later times, particularly of the Southern Song Dynasty -LRB-de Crespigny 2007:483-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The Shu kingdom in particular was viewed by later literati as the ``legitimate'' successor to the Han empire, so fictionalised accounts assign greater prominence than the historical records warrant to the roles of Liu Bei, Zhuge Liang and other heroes from Shu.][[0.0]]
[This is generally accomplished by minimising the importance of Wu commanders and advisors such as Zhou Yu and Lu Su -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:xi-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[While historical accounts describe Lu Su as a sensible advisor and Zhou Yu as an eminent military leader and ``generous, sensible and courageous'' man, the Romance of the Three Kingdoms depicts Lu Su as unremarkable and Zhou Yu as cruel and cynical -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:300; 305--306 29n-RRB-.][[1.0]]
[Both are depicted as being inferior to Zhuge Liang in every respect -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:264-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The romances added wholly fictional and fantastical elements to the historical accounts and these were repeated in popular plays and operas.][[0.0]]
[Examples from the Romance of the Three Kingdoms include Zhuge Liang using magic to call forth favourable winds for the fire ship attack, his strategy of ``using straw boats to borrow arrows'', and Guan Yu capturing and releasing Cao Cao at Huarong Trail.][[0.0]]
[The fictionalised accounts also name Zhuge Liang as a military commander in the combined forces, which is not historically accurate -LRB-de Crespigny 2004:260-264-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Modern and cultural impact Modern day Chibi City in Hubei province was formerly named Puqi.][[0.0]]
[In 1998, the Chinese State Council approved the renaming of the city in celebration of the battle at Red Cliffs.][[0.0]]
[Cultural festivals held by the city have dramatically increased tourism.][[0.0]]
[In 1983, a statue of prominent Song Dynasty poet, Su Shi, was erected at the Huangzhou site of `Su Dongpo's Red Cliffs' in tribute to his writings regarding Red Cliff -LRB-Xinhua 1983-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Popular video games based around the Three Kingdoms era -LRB-such as the Dynasty Warriors series, Sangokushi Koumeiden, Destiny of an Emperor and Kessen II-RRB- have scenarios that include the battle.][[0.0]]
[Other games utilise the Battle of Red Cliffs as their central focus.][[0.0]]
[These include titles popular in Asia, such as the original Japanese version of Warriors of Fate and Dragon Throne: Battle of Red Cliffs.][[0.0]]
[A 2008 film, directed by John Woo and titled Red Cliff, was intended to showcase the Red Cliff legacy and became a massive box-office success in China.][[0.0]]
Document 28 169
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Gameplay Ōkami has the player controlling the main character, Amaterasu, in a woodcut, watercolor style, cel-shaded environment, which looks like an animated Japanese ink-illustration -LRB-known as sumi-e-RRB- with other styles of art.][[0.0]]
[The gameplay style is a mix of action, platform, and puzzle gaming genres, and has been noted by many reviewers to have numerous similarities in overall gameplay style to The Legend of Zelda series, an inspiration that director Hideki Kamiya, a self-proclaimed Zelda-fan, has admitted has influenced his general game design.][[0.0]]
[The main story is primarily linear, directed through by Amaterasu's guide Issun, though numerous side quests and optional activities allow for players to explore the game world and take the story at their own pace.][[0.0]]
[By completing quests, side quests and small additional activities -LRB-such as making trees bloom into life or feeding wild animals-RRB-, Amaterasu earns Praise, which can then be spent to increase various statistics of the character, such as the amount of health and number of ink wells for Celestial Brush techniques.][[0.0]]
[Combat is staged in a ghostly virtual arena, and Amaterasu can fight enemies using a combination of weapons, fighting techniques and Brush methods to dispatch the foes.][[0.0]]
[At the end of combat, money -LRB-as yen-RRB- is rewarded to Amaterasu, with bonuses for completing a battle quickly and without taking damage.][[0.0]]
[The money can be spent on numerous items from merchants across the land, including healing goods, better weapons, tools and key items for completing quests.][[0.0]]
[The money can also be used to buy new combat techniques at dojos throughout the land.][[0.0]]
[Additionally, rare Demon Fangs can be earned through combat which can be traded for additional, unique items that are beneficial in gameplay but not required to complete the game.][[0.0]]
[Weapons inspired by the Imperial Regalia of Japan, the Reflector, the Rosaries and the Glaive can be equipped on Amaterasu as either a main or sub-weapon, and used in addition to other melee attacks that the player can have Amaterasu learn through the course of the game.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Celestial Brush Unique to Ōkami is the Celestial Brush.][[0.0]]
[Players can bring the game to a pause and call up a canvas, where the player can draw onto the screen, either using the left analog stick on the PlayStation 2's DualShock controller or pointing with the Wii Remote.][[0.0]]
[This feature is used in combat, puzzles and as general gameplay.][[0.0]]
[For example, the player can create strong wind by drawing a loop, cut enemies by drawing a line through them or create bridges by painting one, amongst many other abilities.][[0.0]]
[These techniques are learned through the course of the game by completing constellations to release the Celestial Brush gods -LRB-inspired by the Chinese zodiac-RRB- from their hiding spots.][[0.0]]
[It is also possible to upgrade or modify certain Brush powers later in the game.][[0.0]]
[For example, the Celestial Brush power Inferno can gain a new power called Fireburst, which has a different drawing pattern, and allows players to create flames without relying on torches or other related items.][[0.0]]
[The player's ink for drawing is limited by the amount available in special ink wells, preventing the player from solely using Brush techniques to defeat enemies; ink is restored in the wells over time when the Brush is not used.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Plot -LRB-Note: Most character names below are the shortened names of the U.S. version.-RRB-][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Story The game is set in Nippon based on Japanese classic history, and begins with a flashback to events 100 years prior to the game's present, and describes how Shiranui, a pure white wolf, and Nagi, a swordsman, together fought the eight-headed demon Orochi to save Kamiki Village and the maiden Nami, Nagi's beloved.][[0.0]]
[Shiranui and Nagi are unable to defeat Orochi but manage to seal the demon away.][[0.0]]
[In the game's present, Susano, a descendant of Nagi and self-proclaimed greatest warrior, breaks Orochi's seal due to the fact that he does not believe in the legend, and Orochi escapes and curses the lands, sapping the life from every living being.][[0.0]]
[Sakuya, the wood sprite and guardian of Kamiki Village, calls forth Amaterasu, the sun goddess, known to the villagers as the reincarnation of the white wolf Shiranui, and pleads her to remove the curse that covers the land.][[0.0]]
[Accompanied by the artist Issun -LRB-an inch-high Poncle-RRB-, Amaterasu is able to restore the land to its former beauty.][[0.0]]
[Throughout the journey, Amaterasu is hounded by Waka, a strange but powerful individual that seems to have the gift of foresight, and further teases Amaterasu and Issun to his own mysterious ends.][[0.0]]
[Additionally, Amaterasu locates several Celestial Gods who have hidden in the constellations that bestow upon the goddess powers of the Celestial Brush to aid in her quest.][[0.0]]
[Soon, Amaterasu, along with Susano, must battle Orochi to protect Kamiki Village and rescue Susano's beloved, Kushi, recreating events from 100 years prior.][[0.0]]
[This time, the duo are able to fully conquer the demon, causing a black, evil spirit to float northward.][[0.0]]
[Amaterasu and Issun then embark on a journey across Nippon and continue to remove Orochi's curse on the land through defeating other demons that release similar dark presences floating northward.][[0.0]]
[As Amaterasu travels to find the source of these evil spirits, she is brought to the wreckage of a ship able to travel through the stars: the ``Ark of Yamato''.][[0.0]]
[Waka appears and reveals himself as a member of the Moon Tribe, a race that had supplied the Ark of Yamato to the Celestial Beings, who used it to escape from Orochi's assault on the Celestial Plain and sail the heavens, unaware of the evil spirits imprisoned on the Ark which attacked and killed all but himself, resulting in the Ark crashing to earth.][[0.0]]
[Amaterasu defeats Yami, the demon controlling all the evil spirits, and rids both the Ark and Nippon of these evil beings forever.][[0.0]]
[With her mission done, Amaterasu departs with Waka on the Ark to sail back to the Celestial Plain together.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Characters The player controls Ōkami Amaterasu, the goddess of the sun, in the form of a white wolf.][[1.0]]
[While Amaterasu is referred to in the Japanese and European version of the game as a female, the North American version never states Amaterasu as a specific sex.][[0.0]]
[Some characters, however, will refer to Amaterasu in either a feminine or masculine method, but neither are shown to be correct nor incorrect.][[0.0]]
[While Amaterasu, when endowed with ink power, is seen by the player with red markings, cloud-like fur on her shoulders, and weapons on her back, most of the human characters in the game only see her as a plain white wolf; some believe Amaterasu to be the reincarnation of Shiranui -LRB-the white wolf that fought Orochi 100 years prior to the game's present-RRB-, and do not recognize her spiritual nature.][[0.0]]
[If the player depletes their power by overuse of the celestial brush, Amaterasu will temporarily revert to this mundane white form.][[0.0]]
[Issun, an arrogant, inch-tall ``wandering artist'' seeking out the 13 Celestial Brush techniques for himself, accompanies Amaterasu -LRB-whom he calls ``Ammy'' or ``furball''-RRB- and serves as a guide, dialog proxy, and as comic relief He grows in character along with Ammy throughout the game, eventually becoming her true friend, inspiration, and eventually her savior.][[0.0]]
[While there is not a main singular antagonist within the game, two characters reappear several times within the quest.][[0.0]]
[Waka appears as a young flute-playing man to Amaterasu several times in the game, aware of the goddess's form of the white wolf and foretelling of her future and at times battling with her; his dialogue, dropping French affectionate terms at times, conveys a sense of familiarity with Amaterasu, as it turns out that Waka is much older than he appears and has walked with Amaterasu on the Celestial Plain hundreds of years ago.][[0.0]]
[The other is Orochi, the eight-headed demon and a major villain within the game which the player will encounter several times.][[0.0]]
[Orochi repeatedly has threatened Kamiki village, demanding a sacrifice of a young woman.][[0.0]]
[Each of its eight heads is infused with a different elemental magic power, but the entire demon is susceptible to a special brew of sake available only at Kamiki Village, allowing Amaterasu to defeat it while in its stupor.][[0.0]]
[Throughout the game, the player encounters several other characters that are inspired from Japanese folklore.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Development Ōkami resulted from the combined ideas of Clover Studio.][[0.0]]
[The game was originally built around ``depict-LSB-ing-RSB- a lot of nature'', but had no central concept or theme, according to lead designer Hideki Kamiya.][[0.0]]
[Kamiya eventually created a minute-long demonstration movie showing a wolf running about a forest, with flowers blossoming in its wake, but still lacked any gameplay.][[0.0]]
[Kamiya and other members of the team introduced ideas around the nature aspect and eventually led to the game's initial prototype, which Kamiya admitted was ``incredibly boring to play''.][[0.0]]
[Kamiya suggested that he allowed so many ideas from the team that resulted in the development moving off-target, including creating more of a simulation.][[0.0]]
[Eventually, they settled onto the gameplay found in the final product.][[0.0]]
[The art in Ōkami is highly inspired by Japanese watercolor and wood carving art of the Ukiyo-e style, such as the work of Hokusai.][[0.0]]
[Ōkami was originally planned to be rendered in a more photorealistic 3D style.][[1.0]]
[However, Clover Studio determined that the more colorful sumi-e style allowed them to better convey Amaterasu's association with nature and the task of restoring it.][[0.0]]
[The change was also influenced by limitations in the PS2 hardware to render the photorealistic 3D graphics.][[0.0]]
[As a result of the switch to the watercolor style, the idea of the Celestial Brush came about.][[0.0]]
[Atsushi Inaba, CEO of Clover, noted that ``Once we fixed ourselves on a graphical style and got down to the brushwork, we thought `Wouldn't it be great if we could somehow get the player involved and participate in this artwork instead of just watching it?'][[0.0]]
[That's how the idea of the Celestial Brush was born''.][[0.0]]
[Original concepts for enemies included the use of dinosaurs, but the designs settled onto more demon-like characters.][[0.0]]
[Amaterasu's initial designs were aimed to avoid having the character look like ``your pet wearing clothing''.][[0.0]]
[The developers had considered having Amaterasu change into a dolphin when in the water and a falcon when jumping off a cliff, but dropped these ideas.][[0.0]]
[Sakuya, designed around a peach motif, was envisioned with what were called ``level 2'' and ``level 3'' designs where the character would wear less clothing as the story progressed, but the ``level 3'' appearance, effectively naked, was vetoed by Inaba.][[0.0]]
[Waka's character was aimed to be a Tatsunoko-like character, with the hood designed to be reminiscent of those worn by the Gatchaman.][[0.0]]
[Orochi in Japanese mythology is a gigantic creature, so lead character designer Takeyasu Sawaki designed the back of the demon to include a garden and palace; this inspired the game designers to include a bell in those structures that would be Orochi's fatal weakness in the game.][[0.0]]
[The localization team had to translate 1500 pages of text to make sure it made sense in a ``native check'', due to lack of plurals in the Japanese language and the large number of characters and conditional conversations that the player could interact with.][[0.0]]
[The team recognized that certain elements of the game would not be recognized by Western audiences, but left enough text and details to allow the players to look up the information for themselves.][[0.0]]
[Only one puzzle in the game had to be changed as it required knowledge of the steps in drawing a kanji character which would be readily known for Japanese audiences; for the Western release, these steps were demonstrated in the game.][[0.0]]
[The team noted that personalities of characters could be easily conveyed in Japanese text simply by the way sentences were constructed or slurred, a feature that could not directly be applied to localization.][[0.0]]
[Instead, working with Kamiya, the team scripted the localization to either recreate the personality to match the Japanese version, or to create a whole new set of mannerisms for the characters as appropriate.][[0.0]]
[Ōkami was shown at the 2005 E3 Convention, approximately 30% complete, with a planned release in 2006.][[0.0]]
[At this point, the game had much of the core gameplay, including the Celestial Brush and the combat system in place.][[0.0]]
[The game was released a year later in 2006.][[0.0]]
[However, just a few weeks following its release in North America to strong critical reception, Capcom announced the closure of Clover Studio.][[0.0]]
[The Ōkami: Official Complete Works art book was published by Udon in May 2008.][[0.0]]
[The game was re-released under Sony's ``Greatest Hits'' in Japan in August 2008.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Naming and allusions The title of the game is a pun; the word ōkami -LRB-狼-RRB- in Japanese means ``wolf''.][[0.0]]
[However, the kanji characters used as the title of this game -LRB-大神-RRB-, pronounced identically, mean ``great deity'', so the main character is a great wolf deity.][[0.0]]
[The same characters -LRB-大神-RRB- are also used to write the full name of the sun goddess Amaterasu Ōmikami.][[0.0]]
[The localization team opted to use shorter versions of Japanese names -LRB-for example, a boy named ``Mushikai'' was localized as ``Mushi''-RRB- instead of replacing the names with Western-style ones.][[0.0]]
[Issun's informal name for Amaterasu in the Western translation, ``Ammy'', was inspired by Kamiya, and is similar in tone with the Japanese informal name, ``Ammako''.][[0.0]]
[Throughout the game, Ōkami includes several references -LRB-in visual effects, animation, or dialogue-RRB- to other Capcom titles such as Viewtiful Joe, which Clover Studios also developed.][[0.0]]
[For example, Mrs. Orange's technique for making cherry cake parodies Street Fighter's Akuma's Shun Goku Satsu, complete with a kanji word displayed on screen with her back facing the screen.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Audio All of the music in Ōkami is original and inspired by classical Japanese works.][[0.0]]
[The final song, played over the credit sequence, ``Reset'', is sung by Ayaka Hirahara.][[0.0]]
[Capcom has released an official 5-disc soundtrack for Ōkami, which is available exclusively in the Japanese market.][[0.0]]
[In the US and European release, the player can unlock a jukebox to hear the in-game music upon completion of the game.][[0.0]]
[At the 2008 BAFTA Video Games Awards Ōkami won Best Score.][[0.0]]
[Suleputer has also published another album, a piano arrangement, entitled Ōkami Piano Arrange.][[0.0]]
[It was released on 30 March 2007.][[0.0]]
[Mika Matsūra both arranged the 10 songs, and performed it on the piano.][[0.0]]
[The characters' speech in the game is actually created by scrambling samples of voice actors' speech, with more emotional lines being created from voice work given in that emotion.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Wii version The gameplay function of ``drawing'' or ``painting'' strokes on the screen led several journalists and gamers alike to believe that Ōkami would be well-suited for the Nintendo DS or Wii, both of which feature controls capable of creating drawing motions freely.][[0.0]]
[After the game's release, industry rumors of the game being ported to either console persisted, despite Atsushi Inaba of Clover Studio feeling that Ōkami's action-based gameplay would not translate well to the console and statements from Capcom that there were ``no plans for Ōkami on Wii''.][[1.0]]
[However, at the 2007 UK Gamers Day, Capcom announced that Ready at Dawn would oversee porting and development of a Wii version of Ōkami originally scheduled for release in March 2008 but subsequently pushed back to April 2008.][[0.0]]
[Christian Svensson, Capcom's Vice-President of Strategic Planning and Business Development, stated that Capcom had received numerous requests from fans for the development of the Wii version, and that the ported game ``specifically exists because of that direct communication, especially those we receive on our message boards -LRB-even if they're sometimes mean to us-RRB-.''][[0.0]]
[Ready at Dawn president Didier Malenfant has stated that, aside from the control scheme, the Wii version will be ``an exact port of the PS2 version.''][[0.0]]
[The lack of enhancements for the game caused several complaints from gamers, to which Svensson addressed, stating that Svensson reported that the original game assets given to them from Capcom Japan were incomplete, and even after requesting old hard drives and computers to recover more assets, Ready at Dawn was still required to recreate some from scratch.][[0.0]]
[Furthermore, the game had to be recoded to change optimizations that were made for the PlayStation 2 version; Svensson stated that ``part of the reason we didn't show it until we started showing it was because, if we showed it in a form that was anything less than near-perfect, people were going to freak out''.][[0.0]]
[On 15 November 2007, Svensson noted that the engine had been ported to the Wii, writing that ``There are still several systems getting set up properly but there's most definitely a Wii-driven Amaterasu running around Wii-rendered environments as we speak.''][[0.0]]
[A listing posted at Capcom's website for the game on 15 February 2008 revealed that the Wii version would support 480p and widescreen output, and IGN confirmed that the motion sensing of the Wii Remote would be used to perform the Celestial Brush features within the game.][[1.0]]
[IGN's hands-on also cited small changes to the game such as additional motion-sensing controls using both the Wii Remote and Nunchuck attachment, and the ability to skip cutscenes, but reported no other changes in content of the game.][[0.0]]
[Svennson noted that Capcom would not use television advertising for Ōkami on the Wii, but would use online marketing, including art contests and a new website with ``all sorts of things for fans to use to make stuff''.][[0.0]]
[This site was made live on 3 April 2008, featuring wallpapers, character artwork and fan-created art for the game.][[0.0]]
[Svennson further noted that ``If -LSB-Ōkami for the Wii-RSB- did the numbers that we did on the PS2, I'd be very happy.][[0.0]]
[This doesn't need to be a mainstream success for this to be a success for the company.''][[0.0]]
[A ``paper parchment'' filter applied to all on-screen elements that was readily apparent in the PlayStation 2 version was still included in the Wii port, but the effect was made much less significant.][[0.0]]
[To help with drawing with the Celestial Brush, two different buttons on the Wii controllers were given brush functionality; one button was assigned to provide free-form strokes, while the other was set to draw a straight line from the starting point.][[0.0]]
[The final credits movie that was in the PlayStation 2 version of the game was removed from the Wii version, much to Kamiya's regret as it removed the omoi--``a combination of thoughts, emotions, and messages'' -- from the game: ''-LSB-The staff roll was-RSB- the omoi of everyone who worked on the project, put together in a moment of bliss held out just for those who completed the journey.][[0.0]]
[It was a special staff roll for a special moment.][[0.0]]
[And now it is gone.][[0.0]]
[...It's incredibly disappointing and sad.''][[0.0]]
[A Capcom representative noted that the credits, a pre-rendered movie, had the Clover Studio logo within it, and they had ``no legal right to use the Clover logo in a game they were not involved with directly''.][[1.0]]
[Since they also lacked the source to the credits, they opted to remove them entirely from the game.][[0.0]]
[Ready at Dawn's co-founder Didier Malenfant stated that the Wii version of Ōkami took up much more space on the game media than the PlayStation 2 version, and that the movie was cut in order to fit everything on a single game disk.][[0.0]]
[The credit sequence was restored in the Japanese release of the Wii version.][[0.0]]
[Players have discovered that the cover of the North American Wii version of Ōkami includes a watermark from IGN, and traced the source to an image taken from IGN's site.][[0.0]]
[To make up for the error, Capcom offered for a limited time to replace the cover with one of three high-resolution covers free of charge to users in North America.][[0.0]]
[Due to delays in fulfilling the offer, Capcom shipped copies of all three covers to those that registered.][[0.0]]
[They have since discontinued the offer, but have made the cover images available worldwide in high-quality PDF files for users to download and print themselves.][[0.0]]
[The European PAL version of the cover has no such error.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Sequel Sales of Ōkami were considered poor for justifying a sequel; in July 2008, in response to users' questions on the possibility of a sequel, Svensson stated that ``I think we need a lot more people buying the current version before we seriously consider a sequel''.][[0.0]]
[However, after the appearance of a Japanese trademark by Capcom on the word ``Ōkamiden'' a few months before the Wii version of Ōkami in Japan, many speculated that a sequel was pending.][[0.0]]
[The September 2009 issue of Famitsu announced that Ōkamiden: Chīsaki Taiyō -LRB-大神伝～小さき太陽～?][[1.0]]
[Ōkami Chronicles: Tiny Sun-RRB- was indeed a sequel to Ōkami for the Nintendo DS, to be released by Capcom in Japan in 2010.][[1.0]]
[The game takes place three months after the end of Ōkami, with the player in control of Chibiterasu, another wolf like Amaterasu, and will feature the same style of gameplay, including the Celestial Brush using the DS's touchscreen controls.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Reception -LSB-edit-RSB- Reviews Ōkami has received overwhelmingly positive reviews from critics with an average score of 93 percent on Game Rankings, making it the eighth highest overall game of 2006 and second for the PS2, behind Konami's Metal Gear Solid 3: Subsistence.][[0.0]]
[GameSpot gave it a 9 out of 10 and selected it as an Editor's Choice, citing that its ``visual design instantly stands out, but it turns out to be just one of many inspired aspects of this impressive action adventure game.''][[0.0]]
[IGN gave the game a 9.1 out of 10, as being ``beautiful, charismatic, engaging and one of the most original games you'll play anytime soon.''][[0.0]]
[Electronic Gaming Monthly's three reviewers gave it a 9, 9.5, and 9 out of ten, one saying: ``I'll be surprised if you can find a better game on any system this fall.''][[0.0]]
[Newtype USA named Ōkami its Game of the Month for October 2006, heralded the pacing as ``nearly flawless'' and proclaimed ``Ōkami is that rarest of beasts: a game without any obvious flaws.][[0.0]]
[Clover's creativity and attention to detail are on full display here.][[0.0]]
[Shame on any gamer who passes up this divine adventure.''][[0.0]]
[Eurogamer.net scored the game 10/10 saying ``Right from the start it conjures an atmosphere of being something special, but to keep that level of quality up consistently over 60 hours ensures that this will be a game that will be talked about for years to come''.][[0.0]]
[In 2007, Ōkami was named eighteenth best PlayStation 2 game of all time in IGN's feature reflecting on the PlayStation 2's long lifespan.][[0.0]]
[Famitsu gave the game a near perfect score of 39 out of 40, the 15th game to date to receive this score from the publication.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-citation needed-RSB- However, the game was noted to have some flaws.][[0.0]]
[Many reviews commented on the lack of difficulty within the game.][[0.0]]
[Reviewers have also noted some difficulty in getting the game to recognize the correct Celestial Brush patterns, as well as excessive amounts of dialog, particularly at the introduction, which was also hampered by the computer-generated voices used in lieu of voice acting.][[0.0]]
[The Wii version of Ōkami has received generally similar praise to the PlayStation 2 version, with GameSpot stating that the support for widescreen and the Wii controls ``make it even more relevant today than it was in 2006''.][[1.0]]
[The use of the Wii Remote for the Celestial Brush was well received; in GameSpot's review, they noted that the Wii functionality with the Brush ``improves the pace of the game''.][[0.0]]
[However, other aspects to the controls were found to be weaker, particularly in combat.][[0.0]]
[In their review, Nintendo Power recommended the PlayStation 2 version of the game over the Wii, stating that ``Though you can overcome the drawing and attacking issues with practice -LRB-and by sticking to whip-style weapons-RRB-, it's a hurdle you shouldn't have to leap.''][[0.0]]
[It was a nominee for multiple awards from IGN in its 2008 video game awards, including Best Artistic Design and Best Use of the Wii-Mote.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Awards Ōkami's initial showing at the 2005 E3 Convention garnered severals awards and recognition, including 1UP's Best PS2 Game, 2nd Best Game of Show, and 3rd Best Action Game; IGN's Best PS2 Game of Show, and runner-up for Best of Show and Most Innovative Design; and X-Play's Most Original Game.][[0.0]]
[GameSpy recognized it as the 5th best game showing for the convention.][[0.0]]
[Upon release, Ōkami appeared as the Game of the Month for IGN, Electronic Gaming Monthly, and Game Informer.][[0.0]]
[IGN, Edge Magazine and Game Revolution rated it as the best overall game of 2006, while Game Trailers and Official PlayStation Magazine, named it best PS2 game for 2006.][[0.0]]
[IGN further awarded the game the Best Overall and PS2 Adventure Game, the Best Overall and PS2 Artistic Design, the Overall and PS2 Most Innovative Design, and the Best Overall Story.][[0.0]]
[GameSpot awarded the game for the Best Artistic Graphics for 2006.][[0.0]]
[IGN named Ōkami the ninetieth top game of all time in a December 2007 Top 100 list.][[0.0]]
[Ōkami has also won awards from outside the mainstream gaming press.][[0.0]]
[The game earned the Best Character Design and only one of three Innovation Awards at the 2007 Game Developers Choice Awards.][[0.0]]
[Ōkami won the Grand Prize in the Entertainment Division of the 2006 Japan Media Arts Festival.][[0.0]]
[It was also awarded the best Animation in a Game Engine, Art Direction in a Game Engine, Outstanding Original Adventure Game, and Game of the Year in the 2006 awards by the National Academy of Video Game Testers and Reviewers -LRB-NAVIGaTR-RRB-.][[1.0]]
[Ōkami was given an ``Award for Excellence'' from the Japanese Computer Entertainment Supplier's Association -LRB-CESA-RRB- at the Japan Game Awards 2007 and was later given 2009 CESA Developers Conference -LRB-CEDEC-RRB- award for ``Visual Arts''.][[0.0]]
[The game was awarded the Best Anthropomorphic Video Game in the 2006 Ursa Major awards.][[0.0]]
[It also won the 2007 BAFTA awards for Artistic Achievement and Original Score.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Sales Ōkami sold 200,000 copies in North America in 2006, grossing approximately USD$8 million and ranking as the 100th best selling game of the year in the region.][[0.0]]
[By March 2007, the total sales of the PlayStation 2 version were near 270,000.][[0.0]]
[By comparison, Ōkami sold 66,000 copies in Japan for 2006.][[0.0]]
[While it was initially thought that poor sales of Ōkami and God Hand -LRB-another Clover title released in the same time frame-RRB- were the cause of the closure of Clover Studio, it was later revealed that three key developers within Capcom and Clover Studios, Shinji Mikami -LRB-Resident Evil series-RRB-, Hideki Kamiya -LRB-Devil May Cry series-RRB-, and Inaba, had left the company, and the studio was dissolved, such that ``now all the resources should be used more effectively and more efficiently since they are centralized.''][[1.0]]
[Inaba, Mikami, and Kamiya went on to form the video game development company ``Seeds Inc'', later merging with a company called ``ODD'' to become ``Platinum Games''.][[0.0]]
[On 30 July 2008, Capcom revealed that the Wii version of Ōkami had sold approximately 280,000 copies in North America and Europe since its release date.][[0.0]]
[The Wii version debuted in Japan with a modest 24,000 copies sold in its first week in the region.][[1.0]]
[Total sales for the game remained under 600,000 total units by March 2009, and was named the ``least commercially successful winner of a game of the year award'' in the 2010 version of the Guinness World Records Gamer's Edition.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Legacy Ben Mattes, producer for the 2008 Prince of Persia video game, cites Ōkami as well as Ico and Shadow of the Colossus as influences on the gameplay and artwork for the game.][[0.0]]
[Capcom's Street Fighter IV is also stated to have models influenced by Ōkami with hand-drawn images and brushstroke-like effects.][[0.0]]
[An upcoming video game, Epic Mickey, uses similar drawing aspects as Ōkami allowing the player to draw and modify parts of levels to proceed.][[0.0]]
[The final boss, Yami, appears as a boss character in the crossover fighting game, Tatsunoko vs. Capcom: Ultimate All Stars.][[1.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Seasonal forecasts On May�22, 2006, the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration -LRB-NOAA-RRB- released their forecasts for the 2006 Atlantic, East Pacific, and Central Pacific hurricane seasons.][[1.0]]
[The Pacific season was expected to be hindered by the decades-long cycle that began in 1995, which generally increased wind shear across the basin.][[0.0]]
[NOAA predicted a below-normal level of activity in the Eastern Pacific, with 12--16�named storms, of which 6--8 were expected to become hurricanes, and 1--3 expected to become major hurricanes.][[1.0]]
[The Central Pacific basin was also expected to be below average, with only two to three tropical cyclones expected to form or cross into the area.][[1.0]]
[They expected that neither El Niño nor La Niña would affect conditions significantly.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Storms -LSB-edit-RSB- May and June On May�15, the hurricane season began in the Eastern Pacific basin, which is the area of the northern Pacific Ocean east of 140ºW.][[1.0]]
[Twelve days later, an area of disturbed weather developed into the first tropical depression of the season, about 190�mi -LRB-310�km-RRB- south of Acapulco, Mexico.][[0.0]]
[It quickly intensified into a tropical storm, and upon doing so was named Aletta.][[0.0]]
[The storm drifted northeastward toward the coast, bringing light rainfall before turning southward.][[0.0]]
[Wind shear weakened the storm, and on May�31 Aletta dissipated about 200�mi -LRB-320�km-RRB- west-northwest of where it formed.][[0.0]]
[On June�1, the season began in the Central Pacific basin, which is the region between 140ºW and the International Dateline; however, no storms occurred in the basin until July.][[0.0]]
[In the Eastern Pacific, Tropical Depression Two-E formed on June�3 about 145�mi -LRB-245�km-RRB- southwest of Zihuatanejo, Mexico.][[0.0]]
[It tracked eastward and brought heavy rainfall to the coastline, with a report of about 11�inches -LRB-280�mm-RRB- in Acapulco.][[0.0]]
[Land interaction weakened the depression, and it dissipated on June�5.][[0.0]]
[No tropical storms developed in June in the basin, which was unusual compared to the average of two storms forming during the month.][[0.0]]
[Since 1966, there have been only three other seasons in which a tropical storm did not form in June, these being 1969, 2004, and 2007.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- July After about a month of no storms, the basin became active in July.][[0.0]]
[The first storm of the month was Hurricane Bud, which developed early on July�11 about 805�mi -LRB-1300�km-RRB- south of Cabo San Lucas.][[0.0]]
[Moving west-northwestward, it encountered conditions for quick strengthening, and within 24�hours of forming it attained hurricane status.][[0.0]]
[Bud continued strengthening, reaching major hurricane status, or Category�3 status on the Saffir-Simpson scale, and peak winds of 125�mph -LRB-205�km/h-RRB- on July�13.][[0.0]]
[Thereafter, cooler waters and stable air caused the hurricane to quickly weaken.][[0.0]]
[On July�14, Bud weakened to tropical storm status, and two days later it degenerated into a remnant low pressure area.][[0.0]]
[The remnants of Bud dissipated on July�17 about 750�mi -LRB-1210�km-RRB- east-southeast of Hawaii.][[0.0]]
[One day after Bud formed, a tropical disturbance organized into a tropical depression about 290�mi -LRB-465�km-RRB- off the coast of Mexico, which would later become Hurricane Carlotta.][[0.0]]
[A large cyclone, its outer rainbands brushed the coastline of Mexico, as it steadily intensified to reach tropical storm and later hurricane status within 30�hours of forming.][[0.0]]
[Outflow from Hurricane Bud prevented Carlotta from strengthening much further, though for a period of about 60�hours it fluctuated between strong tropical storm status and minimal hurricane status.][[0.0]]
[Cooler waters weakened the storm, and on July�16 Carlotta degenerated into a remnant low.][[0.0]]
[Its low-level circulation persisted for three days before dissipating.][[0.0]]
[As the previous two storms were dissipating, a new tropical depression formed off the southwest coast of Mexico on July�16, which would later become Hurricane Daniel.][[0.0]]
[It moved westward, gradually intensifying under favorable conditions.][[0.0]]
[On July�22, it attained peak winds of 150�mph -LRB-240�km/h-RRB-, a Category�4 on the Saffir-Simpson scale and making Daniel the strongest hurricane during the season in the NHC area of responsibility.][[0.0]]
[Maintaining Category�4 status for about three days, the hurricane subsequently weakened quickly due to cooler waters.][[0.0]]
[Daniel was briefly forecast to move through the Hawaiian Islands as a tropical storm; however, the storm continued to weaken, degenerating into a remnant low on July�27 about 800�mi -LRB-1290�km-RRB- east-southeast of Hilo, Hawaii.][[0.0]]
[Its remnants brought moderate rainfall to the region, though no damage or deaths were reported.][[0.0]]
[Another tropical depression formed off the coast of Mexico on July�21.][[0.0]]
[It tracked northward toward the coast, strengthening into Tropical Storm Emilia and attaining peak winds of 65�mph -LRB-105�km/h-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[It briefly developed an eye, though weakened due to increased wind shear as it turned away from the coast.][[0.0]]
[Emilia later turned to the north, restrengthening to its peak intensity before weakening and paralleling the coastline of the Baja California peninsula.][[0.0]]
[After dropping moderate rainfall along the peninsula, it weakened further as it turned out to sea, and on July�27 degenerated into a remnant low.][[0.0]]
[The final storm of the month formed on July�31 from a tropical wave, well to the southwest of Mexico.][[0.0]]
[It maintained a steady westward track throughout its duration, and quickly intensified into Tropical Storm Fabio.][[0.0]]
[On August�1 it attained peak winds of 50�mph -LRB-85�km/h-RRB-, but subsequently began gradually weakening due to wind shear.][[0.0]]
[Fabio degenerated into a remnant low on August�4, and a few days later brought locally heavy rainfall to Hawaii.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- August Within the basin, more tropical cyclones developed in August than in any other month.][[0.0]]
[The first storm of the month was Tropical Storm Gilma, which in terms of winds was tied with Rosa for the weakest named storm of the season.][[0.0]]
[Gilma developed on August�1 off the southwest coast of Mexico, attaining peak winds of 40�mph -LRB-65�km/h-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[The storm was disorganized due to persistent wind shear, which prevented further strengthening.][[0.0]]
[On August�5 the cyclone dissipated without ever having affected land.][[0.0]]
[After a period of inactivity lasting a week and a half, a tropical depression formed southwest of Mexico on August�15.][[0.0]]
[It tracked generally west-northwestward for its entire duration, eventually becoming Hurricane Hector.][[0.0]]
[On August�18, it attained peak winds of 110�mph -LRB-175�km/h-RRB-, before gradually weakening due to cooler waters.][[0.0]]
[Weakening to a tropical storm on August�20, it later turned sharply to the west, degenerating into a remnant low on August�23 and dissipating the next day without affecting land.][[0.0]]
[The strongest hurricane of the season was Hurricane Ioke, which formed on August�20 far to the south of Hawaii.][[0.0]]
[It was the first central Pacific named storm since Hurricane Huko in 2002.][[0.0]]
[Encountering warm waters and little wind shear, and maintaining well-defined outflow, Ioke intensified from a tropical depression to Category�4 status on the Saffir-Simpson scale within 48�hours.][[0.0]]
[Late on August�22 it rapidly weakened to Category�2 status before crossing over Johnston Atoll, where 12�people rode out the storm in a hurricane-proof bunker.][[0.0]]
[Two days later, favorable conditions again allowed for rapid strengthening, and Ioke attained Category�5 status on August�25 before crossing the International Date Line.][[0.0]]
[As it continued westward its intensity fluctuated, and on August�31 it passed near Wake Island with winds of 155�mph -LRB-249�km/h-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Ioke gradually weakened as it turned northwestward and northward, and by September�6 transitioned into an extratropical cyclone.][[0.0]]
[The remnants of Ioke accelerated northeastward and ultimately crossed into Alaska.][[1.0]]
[On August�21 shortly after the previous storm formed, Hurricane Ileana developed off the southwest coast of Mexico.][[0.0]]
[It generally paralleled the coastline throughout its duration, ultimately reaching peak winds of 120�mph -LRB-195�km/h-RRB- before weakening.][[0.0]]
[Around the time of peak intensity, the hurricane passed near Socorro Island, where it produced hurricane-force wind gusts.][[0.0]]
[On August�27, Ileana degenerated into a remnant low, and two days later dissipated well offshore.][[0.0]]
[The next tropical depression, which would eventually become Hurricane John, formed on August�28 about 250�mi -LRB-400�km-RRB- off the coast of Mexico.][[0.0]]
[With favorable environmental conditions, the system quickly organized, becoming a hurricane within 36�hours of forming.][[0.0]]
[Hurricane John continued rapid intensification and reached peak winds of 135�mph -LRB-215�km/h-RRB- on August�30 while just off the Mexican coast.][[0.0]]
[Land interaction weakened the hurricane, and still tracking northwestward it struck the eastern portion of the Baja California peninsula on September�2 as a Category�2 hurricane.][[0.0]]
[John dissipated on September�4, though its remnants brought rainfall to the southwest United States.][[0.0]]
[The last storm to develop in August was Hurricane Kristy, which formed on August�30 about 935�mi -LRB-1505�km-RRB- west-northwest of Hurricane John.][[0.0]]
[It initially tracked northwestward, reaching peak winds of 80�mph -LRB-130�km/h-RRB- within 36�hours of forming.][[0.0]]
[Outflow from Hurricane John caused Kristy to weaken, and at the same time, the storm's motion became nearly stationary as steering currents collapsed.][[0.0]]
[On September�2 it turned to a southeast drift, and degenerated into a tropical depression around the same time.][[0.0]]
[Kristy later turned to the west, oscillating between tropical depression and tropical storm status until dissipating on September�9.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- September Hurricane Lane developed from a tropical wave on September�13 to the south of Mexico.][[0.0]]
[It moved northwestward parallel to the coast of Mexico, and steadily intensified in a favorable environment.][[0.0]]
[After turning to the northeast Lane attained peak winds of 125�mph -LRB-205�km/h-RRB-, and made landfall in the Mexican state of Sinaloa at peak strength.][[0.0]]
[It rapidly weakened and dissipated on September�17, and later brought precipitation to southern Texas.][[0.0]]
[An area of disturbed weather associated with the Intertropical Convergence Zone spawned a tropical depression on September�16 off the coast of Mexico.][[0.0]]
[Despite being disorganized, it quickly strengthened into Tropical Storm Miriam.][[0.0]]
[The storm was sheared throughout its duration, and after encountering cooler waters Miriam dissipated on September�18 near the Baja California peninsula.][[0.0]]
[On September�18, an area of disturbed weather in the central Pacific became sufficiently organized and was designated Tropical Depression Two-C.][[0.0]]
[Vertical wind shear caused the depression to weaken into a remnant low on September�20, it never having attained tropical storm status.][[0.0]]
[The depression was initially thought to be a regeneration of earlier Hurricane Kristy.][[0.0]]
[On September�26, another area of disturbed weather in the Central Pacific near the International Date Line became organized and was designated Tropical Depression Three-C.][[0.0]]
[However, wind shear and the presence of dry air to the west inhibited further development, and the system dissipated 12�hours later; at around the same time, the system crossed into the Western Pacific.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- October The first cyclone to develop in the month of October was Tropical Storm Norman, which formed well off the coast of Mexico on October�9.][[1.0]]
[It quickly reached peak winds of 50�mph -LRB-85�km/h-RRB-, though almost as quickly the cyclone degenerated into a remnant low due to wind shear.][[0.0]]
[Its remnants turned to the east, and on October�15 regenerated into a tropical cyclone just off the coast of Mexico after merging with another disturbance.][[0.0]]
[Norman quickly dissipated as unfavorable conditions returned, although it brought heavy rainfall to the Mexican coastline.][[0.0]]
[Tropical Storm Olivia formed on October�9 about 700�mi -LRB-1120�km-RRB- west of Norman.][[0.0]]
[Tracking northeastward and attaining tropical storm status, it failed to strengthen significantly due to wind shear.][[0.0]]
[Olivia weakened to tropical depression status on October�11, and turning to the east-southeast degenerated into a remnant low two days later.][[0.0]]
[Its remnants were later absorbed by a larger disturbance that included the remnants of Norman.][[0.0]]
[The final cyclone to develop within the CPHC area of responsibility was Tropical Depression Four-C, which formed on October�13 to the southwest of Hawaii.][[0.0]]
[Within 24�hours of forming, it degenerated into a remnant disturbance due to unfavorable wind shear.][[0.0]]
[Moisture from the depression contributed to heavy rainfall in Hawaii.][[0.0]]
[The strongest hurricane during the month was Hurricane Paul.][[0.0]]
[Forming on October�21, it did not strengthen much initially due to the presence of wind shear.][[0.0]]
[However, a decrease in shear allowed Paul to strengthen rapidly, and in a 24-hour period it developed from a moderate tropical storm to a 105�mph -LRB-170�km/h-RRB- hurricane, its peak intensity.][[0.0]]
[By that time, it had turned northeastward and entered an unfavorable environment, which caused Paul to steadily weaken to tropical storm status.][[0.0]]
[After passing south of the Baja California peninsula it deteriorated to tropical depression status and moved ashore in northwestern Sinaloa.][[0.0]]
[On October�26 shortly after Paul dissipated, another tropical depression formed off the southwest coast of Mexico.][[0.0]]
[Moving southwestward, it encountered unfavorable wind shear, which prevented strengthening.][[0.0]]
[On October�28 it degenerated into a remnant low, and the next day dissipated without affecting land.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Unclassified storm An extratropical storm persisted in the extreme northern central Pacific Ocean in late October.][[0.0]]
[It drifted over unusually warm waters up to 3.6°F -LRB-2°C-RRB- above normal, and gradually developed convection near the center.][[0.0]]
[By November�2, QuikSCAT satellite suggested the system attained winds of up to 60�mph -LRB-95�km/h-RRB- about 900�mi -LRB-1450�km-RRB- west of Oregon.][[0.0]]
[The system also developed an eye and an eyewall.][[0.0]]
[The cyclone tracked northeastward as it gradually weakened, and dissipated on November�4.][[0.0]]
[NASA considered the cyclone to be a subtropical storm.][[0.0]]
[However, as it formed outside of the territory of any monitoring organization, it was not named.][[0.0]]
[Operationally, the United States Navy treated the system as a tropical disturbance, numbered 91C.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- November Tropical activity within the basin in November�2006 was the most active on record, based on the Accumulated Cyclone Energy -LRB-ACE-RRB- Index.][[0.0]]
[Three tropical cyclones formed, of which two became tropical storms; only one other season on record, 1966, produced two tropical storms in the month of November.][[1.0]]
[The first storm of the month was Tropical Storm Rosa, which formed on November�8 as a tropical depression off the southwest coast of Mexico.][[1.0]]
[Immediate development was hampered by wind shear, although an increase in thunderstorms on November�9 brought the depression to tropical storm status.][[0.0]]
[Continued shear prevented intensification, and Rosa dissipated on November�10.][[0.0]]
[Rosa was the first Eastern Pacific tropical storm in November since another storm named Rosa in the 2000 season.][[0.0]]
[On November�11, another tropical depression formed off the coast of Mexico, about 450�mi -LRB-720�km-RRB- west-southwest of where Rosa dissipated the previous day.][[0.0]]
[Similar to Rosa, it developed within an environment with unfavorable wind shear, but failed to intensify beyond tropical depression status.][[0.0]]
[About 18�hours after it formed the depression degenerated into a trough.][[0.0]]
[The final storm of the season was Hurricane Sergio, which was both the strongest and longest-lived November Pacific hurricane on record.][[1.0]]
[It formed on November�13 about 460�mi -LRB-740�km-RRB- south of Manzanillo, Colima, and steadily intensified while tracking southeastward.][[0.0]]
[It reached peak winds of 110�mph -LRB-175�km/h-RRB- on November�15, and subsequently began to weaken due to increased wind shear as it turned to the north.][[0.0]]
[Sergio later turned to the west, remaining well off the coast of Mexico, and dissipated on November�20 about 320�mi -LRB-515�km-RRB- west-northwest of it originally formed.][[0.0]]
[The storm brought light rainfall to the Mexican coastline, though no major effects were reported.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Impact During the season, tropical cyclones collectively caused 14�fatalities and $355�million in damage -LRB-2006�USD-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-nb 1-RSB- With its long coastline, the country of Mexico was affected by ten of the cyclones during the season, including four that made landfall.][[0.0]]
[Of the six storms that affected Mexico but did not strike the country, the first was Tropical Storm Aletta, the first storm of the season, which brought light rainfall and caused minor damage.][[0.0]]
[The next tropical depression of the season produced heavy rainfall in the Acapulco area while remaining offshore; mudslides and flooding were reported, and 72�people were forced to leave their homes.][[0.0]]
[In July, Hurricane Carlotta brushed the coastline with light rainfall.][[0.0]]
[When Tropical Storm Emilia passed just off the coast of Baja California, it brought moderate precipitation which caused minor flooding and damage around Cabo San Lucas.][[0.0]]
[Heavy surf from Hurricane Ileana killed a man near Cabo San Lucas.][[0.0]]
[The last storm of the season, Hurricane Sergio, produced light rainfall along the coast while remaining well offshore.][[0.0]]
[Mexico was struck by four tropical cyclones in 2006, all along the Pacific coast.][[0.0]]
[The first was Hurricane John, which made landfall near the southern tip of the Baja California peninsula on September�1.][[1.0]]
[Earlier, it produced flooding and high surf near Acapulco while paralleling the coastline, and later the hurricane damaged or destroyed at least 450�homes in the Baja California peninsula.][[0.0]]
[Hurricane John was the wettest tropical cyclone of the year in Mexico, dropping 17.7�in -LRB-449�mm-RRB- of rainfall.][[0.0]]
[Five people were killed, and damage in Mexico amounted to $663�million -LRB-2006�MXN, $60.8�million 2006�USD-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Hurricane Lane moved ashore in the state of Sinaloa as a Category�3 hurricane on the Saffir-Simpson scale, which was the strongest landfall during the season.][[0.0]]
[Paralleling the coastline a short distance offshore, the hurricane dropped heavy rainfall, causing flooding and mudslides which resulted in four fatalities.][[0.0]]
[Hurricane Lane affected 4,320�houses, and a total of 19,200�mi -LRB-30,000�km-RRB- of roads and highways were damaged to some degree.][[0.0]]
[Monetary damage amounted to about $2.2�billion -LRB-2006�MXN, $203�million 2006�USD-RRB- in damage in the country.][[0.0]]
[In early October, former Tropical Storm Norman passed near or over southwestern Mexico, destroying 20�houses and leaving 20�villages without power.][[0.0]]
[Later, former Hurricane Paul caused four deaths, two of which from rough seas and two from drowning in a flooded river.][[0.0]]
[The storm damaged 5,000�houses, and monetary damage totaled more than $35�million -LRB-2006�MXN, $3.2�million 2006�USD-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Three of the cyclones that affected Mexico also impacted the southwestern United States.][[0.0]]
[Moisture from Tropical Storm Emilia produced thunderstorms in Arizona which caused flooding, and in southern California its rainfall assisted firefighters in combating a wildfire.][[0.0]]
[The remnants of Hurricane John produced moisture across much of the southwestern United States, causing mudslides in California, light rainfall in Arizona, overflowed rivers in New Mexico, and up to 8�in -LRB-200�mm-RRB- of rainfall in Texas.][[0.0]]
[In western Texas, the precipitation was beneficial in some areas but damaging in others, causing flooded roads and washouts.][[0.0]]
[The remnants of Hurricane Lane also produced rainfall in Texas.][[1.0]]
[Four tropical cyclones affected the U.S. state of Hawaii, all of which were the remnants of former tropical cyclones.][[0.0]]
[Moisture from Hurricane Bud produced light rainfall in east-facing slopes of the island chain.][[0.0]]
[Former Hurricane Daniel produced up to 5�in -LRB-125�mm-RRB- of rainfall in the state, though no significant impact was reported.][[0.0]]
[The remnants of Tropical Storm Fabio contributed to heavy rainfall, peaking at 15.08�in -LRB-383�mm-RRB- on Mount Waiʻaleʻale on the island of Kauai; the rainfall caused river and roadway flooding, but little damage.][[0.0]]
[Moisture from Tropical Depression Four-C in October contributed to heavy rainfall on the island of Hawaii.][[0.0]]
[The strongest hurricane of the season was Hurricane Ioke, which reached Category 5 status in the central Pacific Ocean.][[1.0]]
[It first affected the uninhabited Johnston Atoll, although when Ioke struck there was a crew of 12�people taking shelter on the island.][[0.0]]
[Hurricane force winds affected the landmass, powerful enough to knock down trees.][[0.0]]
[In the western Pacific Ocean after being re-classified as a typhoon, Ioke passed near Wake Island, forcing the first full-scale evacuation of the island since a typhoon in 1967.][[0.0]]
[The combination of strong winds and a powerful storm surge damaged 70% of the buildings on the island, many with moderate roof damage.][[0.0]]
[Destruction on the island was estimated at $88�million -LRB-2006�USD-RRB-.][[0.0]]
[Later, the storm passed near the Japanese island of Minami Torishima, which was also fully evacuated; facilities on the island were damaged, although it was repaired and fully operational within three weeks after the storm.][[0.0]]
[The remnants of Ioke later brought hurricane force wind gusts to southwestern Alaska.][[0.0]]

[-LSB-edit-RSB- Storm names The following names were used for named storms that formed in the northeast Pacific in 2006.][[0.0]]
[This is the same list that was used in the 2000 season.][[0.0]]
[There were no names retired from the northeast Pacific list.][[0.0]]
[Therefore, the same list will be reused in the 2012 season.][[0.0]]
[Storms that formed in the central Pacific are given names from a sequential list; in 2006, the name Ioke was used from this list, the first time a name from the Central Pacific list had been used since the 2002 season.][[0.0]]
[-LSB-edit-RSB- Retirement The name Ioke was retired from the north-central Pacific list by the WMO in the spring of 2007 and replaced with Iopa.][[0.0]]
[During the 61st Interdepartmental Hurricane Conference, the Hawaii State Civil Defense requested the retirement of the name Daniel, citing that the storm had become memorable due to threat or damage.][[0.0]]
[However, the request was denied, as the name remains on the tropical cyclone naming list.][[0.0]]
